| M01-C | finding | The immediate response to M01-C terror is paralysis or melting: Gen 35:5 (terror "paralyzing the will to pursue"), Exo 15:16 ("rendering enemies motionless as stone"), Jos 2:9 ("causes the people to melt inwardly, dissolving capacity to resist"). The will collapses immediately. |
| M01-D | finding | The immediate response to M01-D dismay is inner speechlessness or cognitive shutdown: Gen 45:3 (brothers "cannot answer"), Isa 21:3 ("cannot see"), Job 32:15 (friends in "complete speechlessness"). The cognitive and verbal faculties are the first to fail. |
| M01-E | finding | The immediate response to M01-E terror-trembling is involuntary bodily trembling that precedes conscious processing: Exo 19:16 (the trembling is the direct response to the overwhelming sensory phenomena at Sinai — there is no gap between encounter and trembling). |
| M01-F | finding | M01-F anxiety does not have a single "immediate first response" — it is a sustained condition. But when anticipatory dread materializes (F-VCG-02, Job 3:25), the immediate experience is the correspondence between feared event and actual event. |
| M01-G | finding | The immediate response to the situation that provokes timidity (M01-G) is passive inaction: Mat 25:25 (servant buries the talent rather than acts), Joh 14:27 (heart yields to cowardly shrinking). Timidity's first response is the suppression of action. |

### T1.5.2  ·  Tier T1

> Is the immediate response consistent across the verse evidence, or does it vary?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The immediate response is not consistent across the cluster — it varies by object, sub-group, and context. This variation is itself a finding: fear is a highly context-sensitive characteristic whose immediate expression is governed by what triggered it and toward what it is directed. |
| M01-A | finding | The immediate response in M01-A varies by context: in ethical contexts the response is restraint from wrongdoing (Lev 19:14); in wisdom contexts it is the opening of the cognitive faculty to knowledge (Pro 1:7); in worship contexts it is approach to God (Psa 5:7; Heb 12:28); in the corporate miracle context it is glorifying God (Mat 9:8). There is variation, but all responses are characterised by alignment with God's reality rather than resistance to it. |
| M01-B | finding | M01-B's immediate response varies significantly: theophany fear produces prostration (Mat 17:6; Luk 24:5); Jesus-miracle fear produces wonder and questioning (Mar 4:41); military threat fear produces flight (Gen 32:7; 1Sa 17:24); social fear produces speech-suppression (Joh 7:13). The variation is a function of the object of fear. |
| M01-C | silent | M01-C terror is consistently paralyzing or melting in its immediate effect — less variation than M01-B. |
| M01-D | finding | M01-D varies between speechlessness (Job 32:15; Gen 45:3) and violent agitation (Dan 11:44: "alarming news converting inward alarm into violent external action"). The ba.hal root spans both responses. |

### T1.5.3  ·  Tier T1

> Where the verse evidence is silent on immediate response, note this explicitly.

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| M01-F | silent | M01-F-VCG-01 (chronic pervasive anxiety) and M01-F-VCG-03 (covenantal curse-dread) are silent on immediate response because they describe sustained conditions rather than acute events. By definition they lack a first response — they are the condition the person is already in. |

### T1.6.1  ·  Tier T1

> What does this characteristic produce in the inner being over time?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | Over time, fear in its ordered form (M01-A) produces wisdom, life, confidence, ethical character, and community. In its disordered forms (M01-F, G), fear produces: temporal distortion, life-colonization by dread, and apostasy. The sustained effect of fear depends entirely on whether it is ordered (directed toward God) or disordered (directed toward threat, punishment, or human opinion). |
| M01-A | finding | M01-A reverential fear produces over time: (1) wisdom — Pro 2:5 ("fear of God is the fruit of earnest seeking after wisdom — an inner understanding arrived at through diligent pursuit"); (2) life — Pro 10:27 ("fear of the Lord extends life"); Pro 19:23 ("fear of the Lord leads to life and produces a restful inner satisfaction"); (3) confidence — Pro 14:26 ("fear of the Lord functions as an inner foundation of strong confidence, not anxiety"); (4) ethical character — the person who sustains this fear develops trustworthiness, integrity, and justice (Exo 18:21; 2Ch 19:9); (5) community identity — the God-fearers form a recognizable community (Mal 3:16; Act 10:2; Ecc 8:12-13). |
| M01-B | finding | M01-B acute fear in its ongoing form (where dread persists) produces avoidance behaviors and sustained enmity: 1Sa 18:29 ("Saul's fear of David intensifies and becomes permanent — it is the inner root of his sustained enmity"). The commanded-release pattern (B-VCG-06) aims to prevent the sustained negative effect of unresolved fear. |
| M01-F | finding | M01-F-VCG-03 shows covenantal-curse dread producing over time: temporal distortion ("the sufferer constantly wishes the present moment away," Deu 28:67), insomnia, and the total colonization of daily life by dread (Eze 12:18-19 anchor). |
| M01-G | finding | M01-G timidity sustained produces apostasy (Rev 21:8: the coward is listed among those consigned to the lake of fire in a context suggesting sustained failure under pressure) and the paralysis of gifts and callings (2Ti 1:7). |

### T1.6.2  ·  Tier T1

> What states, qualities, capacities, or orientations does sustained exposure to or possession of this characteristic establish?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | Sustained ordered fear (M01-A) establishes wisdom, integrity, and covenant identity. Sustained disordered fear (M01-F, G) establishes inner bondage, paralysis, and apostasy. The sustained effects confirm that fear is a formative characteristic — what the person fears over time shapes who the person becomes. |
| M01-A | finding | Sustained possession of M01-A reverential fear establishes: the capacity for genuine wisdom (Pro 1:7; 9:10); ethical reliability in positions of power (Exo 18:21; Neh 5:15); the relational posture that receives covenant love (Psa 103:11-17); multigenerational identity ("fear of the Lord" as the characteristic from which God's steadfast love runs across generations, Psa 103:17); and the inner integration that fear of God requires — Psa 86:11 ("fear of God requires inner integration; a divided heart is an obstacle to genuine reverence"). |
| M01-B | finding | Sustained acute fear (unresolved) establishes permanent inner states of dread (1Sa 18:29: Saul's fear becoming permanent inner root of enmity) and speech-suppression (Joh 20:19: disciples' fear causing them to lock their doors). Sustained exposure to fear as the commanded-release corpus produces: trust (Psa 56:3-4), courage (1Ch 22:13; 28:20), and the capacity for mission (Mat 28:10). |
| M01-F | finding | Sustained M01-F dread establishes: the "spirit of slavery" (Rom 8:15 secondary: the spirit of slavery associated with fear, displaced by adoption) and lifelong inner bondage (Heb 2:15: "fear of death held people in lifelong inner slavery"). |
| M01-G | finding | Sustained M01-G timidity establishes failure of stewardship (Mat 25:25-26: the buried talent) and ultimately the full apostasy pattern of Rev 21:8. |

### T1.6.3  ·  Tier T1

> Does the sustained effect differ from the immediate response — and if so, how?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | Across M01, the sustained effect consistently differs from the immediate response in the dimension of scale and constitutional depth. The immediate response is situational; the sustained effect is formative. This is a significant cluster-level finding: fear is not merely an episodic experience but a formative characteristic whose sustained operation shapes the inner person over time. |
| M01-A | finding | In M01-A, the sustained effect (wisdom, life, confidence, identity) differs significantly from the immediate response (obedience, worship, restraint from wrong). The immediate response is situational; the sustained effect is constitutive. This confirms that M01-A is dispositional — it works cumulatively and formatively, not merely episodically. |
| M01-B | finding | In M01-B, the sustained effect (permanent enmity, doors locked, speech suppressed) differs from the immediate response (flight, prostration, silence). The immediate response is situational; the sustained effect represents the calcification of the fear into a relational structure. Unresolved acute fear becomes a settled inner state — approaching the dispositional character of M01-F. |
| M01-G | finding | In M01-G, the sustained effect (apostasy, failed stewardship) differs from the immediate response (inaction, burying) in scale and consequence. What begins as a momentary failure of nerve accumulates into a settled disposition of cowardly shrinking and ultimately full apostasy. |

### T1.7.1  ·  Tier T1

> What inner conditions or orientations enable genuine reception of this characteristic?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | Genuine reception of ordered fear (M01-A, E-VCG-02) is enabled by: humility, an undivided heart, openness to God's word, and ultimately divine gift (Jer 32:40). These are enabling conditions, not sufficient causes — the characteristic flows from the person's receptive posture before God. |
| M01-A | finding | In M01-A, genuine reverential fear is enabled by: (1) an undivided heart — Psa 86:11 ("fear of God requires inner integration; a divided heart is an obstacle"); (2) humility — Pro 15:33 ("humility naturally precedes honor" in the context of fear-based wisdom formation); Pro 22:4 (fear paired with humility as the inner disposition whose reward is concrete blessing); (3) hearing God's word — Deu 31:12-13 (fear is formed through regular hearing of the law); (4) divine implantation — Jer 32:40 (God himself pledges to implant the fear, suggesting that ultimately human reception is enabled by divine gift). |
| M01-B | finding | M01-B acute fear's "reception" is involuntary — it is not received but struck. However, the commanded-release corpus (B-VCG-06) implies that for fear to be genuinely released, the person must have a receptive will — Isa 43:1's "do not fear" presupposes a will capable of receiving and acting on the divine word. |
| M01-E | finding | M01-E-VCG-02's trembling-at-God's-word is enabled by a spirit of humility and contrition (Isa 66:2 anchor: trembling paired with "humility and a contrite spirit as the inner posture God looks for"). The trembling is not manufactured but flows from the contrite spirit. |

### T1.7.2  ·  Tier T1

> What inner conditions block, distort, or prevent reception?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | Reception of ordered fear (M01-A) is blocked by hardened hearts, divided allegiance, pride, accumulated sin, and the substitution of external compliance for inner reality. These are consistent with the programme's finding across other M-clusters that the heart's integrity is the primary enabling/blocking factor for inner-being characteristics. |
| M01-A | finding | In M01-A, reception is blocked by: (1) a hardened heart — Isa 63:17 ("God himself has hardened their heart so that they do not fear him"); (2) a divided heart — Psa 86:11; (3) false-object attachment — 2Ki 17 corpus (fear misplaced on other gods blocks genuine fear-of-God); (4) external compliance without inner reality — Isa 29:13 ("hollow fear — learned external formula with no inner reality"); (5) pride and self-reliance — Pro 3:7 (fear-of-God set against self-reliant pride); (6) accumulated sinful patterns — Jer 3:8 ("Judah did not fear despite witnessing Israel's divorce-judgment — a will hardened against the corrective lesson before her"). |
| M01-B | finding | M01-B's disordering of acute fear is blocked or distorted by: prior experience producing distrust (Act 9:26: Jerusalem disciples' fear of Saul based on his history), misidentification (Mat 14:26: disciples misidentify Jesus as a ghost, generating fear), and the crowd's conspiratorial social fear that displaces genuine fear-of-God (Isa 8:12: "inner disposition of communal dread that distorts perception of true danger"). |
| M01-G | finding | M01-G's ordered courage is blocked by: insufficient investment in the spirit of power, love, and self-control (2Ti 1:7 implies that the blocking condition is the failure to stir up the gift God has given — 2Ti 1:6 context). |

### T1.7.3  ·  Tier T1

> What is the inner-being state of the person who encounters this characteristic but does not receive it?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | Non-reception of reverential fear (M01-A) produces moral blindness and defiant self-sufficiency. Non-reception of commanded-fear-release (M01-B's "do not fear") produces paralysis. Non-reception of courage-over-timidity (M01-G) produces apostasy. The common feature: non-reception leaves the inner person structurally misaligned — either toward wrong objects of fear or toward no genuine alignment at all. |
| M01-A | finding | The person who encounters the stimulus for reverential fear but does not receive it is in a state of moral blindness (Psa 36:1: "no dread of God before their eyes — fundamental moral blindness that allows transgression to speak freely in the heart"); defiant self-sufficiency (Psa 55:19: "not fearing God marks an inner disposition of defiant self-sufficiency"); and ultimately apostasy or judgment-bound hardness (Jer 5:22-24: "the people do not say in their hearts 'let us fear the Lord'" — ingratitude and irreverence are one; the absence of fear in the heart is the root of covenant failure). The NT is direct: Rom 3:18 ("absence of fear of God in their inner orientation — indicates that godless humanity lacks the reverential awareness that should govern all thought and conduct"). |
| M01-B | finding | The person who encounters acute fear's stimulus and is commanded "do not fear" but does not receive the release remains in the grip of paralysis, silence, or flight. The commanded-release corpus (B-VCG-06) assumes the person's ongoing struggle with the fear until the divine word penetrates. |
| M01-G | finding | The person who encounters the call to courage but remains in timidity is in the state described by Rev 21:8: cowardice as a defining inner orientation, heading toward apostasy. |

### T1.8.1  ·  Tier T1

> What is the primary inner-being dimension of this characteristic from the programme's dimension vocabulary?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The cluster's primary dimension is **affective** across most sub-groups, with **volitional** as the most consistent secondary dimension across all sub-groups. M01-E is unique in its **somatic** primary; M01-G unique in its **volitional-constitutional** primary. The cluster confirms that fear is primarily a felt inner state (affective) with immediate volitional consequences. |
| M01-A | finding | M01-A's primary dimension is **affective-relational** — the characteristic is the inner feeling-posture that orients the person in relationship toward God. However, it is unusual in that it is equally **volitional** (governing conduct through constraint and redirection) and **cognitive** (being the foundation of genuine knowledge). This multi-dimensionality is a finding rather than a classification problem: M01-A genuinely inhabits the intersection of affect, volition, and cognition. **[Folded from wa_session_b_findings.id=38; finding_id=DIM-11-001; registry=awe]** Awe spans both Affective/Emotional and Spiritual/God-ward dimensions. God-ward groups (1682-001, 1682-003, 703-002, 703-003) show that the deepest fear/awe content is Spiritual/God-ward rather than merely affective. Session B s… |
| M01-B | finding | M01-B's primary dimension is **affective** — it is an acute emotional experience triggered by an external stimulus. The secondary dimension is **volitional** — the acute fear immediately governs the will's response. |
| M01-C | finding | M01-C's primary dimension is **force** or **dynamic** — terror as a quality/power that acts upon the inner person from outside. If the dimension vocabulary does not include a "force" category, the nearest is **affective** (the terror produces a felt state in the recipient) with **volitional** as secondary (paralyzing the will). |
| M01-D | finding | M01-D's primary dimension is **affective** (the inner experience of dismay) with **cognitive** as a significant secondary (the dismay shuts down cognition — speechlessness, inability to see, inability to think). The bodily collapse dimension (D-VCG-03) adds a **somatic** secondary. |
| M01-E | finding | M01-E's primary dimension is **somatic** — the characteristic is definitionally the body's expression of inner fear. The E-VCG-02 trembling-at-word subset adds a **spirit-level** and **volitional-reverential** secondary dimension. |
| M01-F | finding | M01-F's primary dimension is **affective-temporal** — the characteristic is the inner experience of sustained anticipatory dread. The **cognitive** dimension is significant (de.a.gah as ruminating, forward-oriented thought). The **volitional** dimension is secondary (anxiety driving avoidance or flight). |
| M01-G | finding | M01-G's primary dimension is **volitional-constitutional** — the characteristic is a failure of the will's constitutive courage, operating at the spirit level (2Ti 1:7). |

### T1.8.2  ·  Tier T1

> What evidence from the verse evidence supports this classification?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The affective classification is supported by the overwhelming dominance of experiential-state language across the cluster's 941 verses: fear is consistently described as something that fills the person, grips them, falls upon them, overwhelms them — the language of involuntary affective experience. |
| M01-A | finding | M01-A's affective-relational classification is supported by the consistent nominal forms (*yir.ah* as a possessed quality, "Fear of Isaac" as a name, Mal 2:5 as a covenant defined by fear-as-inner-posture) and by the relational framing (Psa 25:14: "positioned for intimate covenant relationship"). The volitional dimension is supported by the consistent "governing conduct" pattern across A-VCG-01 (ethical restraint), A-VCG-02 (orienting the cognitive life), A-VCG-03 (aligning the relational life). The cognitive dimension is supported by Pro 1:7; Psa 111:10; Job 28:28. |
| M01-B | finding | M01-B's affective primary is supported by the consistent involuntary character of the acute fear (Gen 3:10; 1Sa 17:24; Luk 2:9). The volitional secondary is supported by the systematic descriptions of fear governing what the person does immediately after it strikes. |
| M01-E | finding | M01-E's somatic primary is supported by the entire vocabulary corpus: cha.rad, cha.ra.dah, ra.gaz, ra.ad, pal.la.tsut, sa.ar, rog.zah, re.tet, tromos, entromos — all name bodily states. The sub-group's 98 verses consistently describe physical manifestation as the characteristic's primary mode. |
| M01-G | finding | M01-G's volitional-constitutional primary is supported by 2Ti 1:7 ("spirit-level disposition") and by the consistent description of timidity as will-suppression (Mat 25:25: "paralyzed his will and produced passive self-preservation"). |

| M01-A | finding | M01-A's secondary dimensions — **volitional** (governing conduct) and **cognitive** (grounding knowledge) — do not compete with the affective-relational primary but integrate into it. The fear is a felt posture (affective) that simultaneously governs conduct (volitional) and orients knowing (cognitive). These dimensions are aspects of a single complex disposition rather than competing classifications. **[Folded from wa_session_b_findings.id=38; finding_id=DIM-11-001; registry=awe]** Awe spans both Affective/Emotional and Spiritual/God-ward dimensions. God-ward groups (1682-001, 1682-003, 703-002, 703-003) show that the deepest fear/awe content is Spiritual/God-ward rather than merely affective. Session B should examine whether awe functions as a distinct inner-being category integrating a… |
| M01-E | finding | M01-E-VCG-02's **spirit-level reverential** secondary dimension is genuinely distinct from the **somatic** primary. The trembling-at-word tradition (Isa 66:2 anchor) is not primarily somatic in origin — it arises from a spirit-posture that then expresses somatically. This is the one sub-group where the somatic primary and the spirit-level secondary are in genuine tension as a classification question. The programme should note this at Phase 12. |
| M01-G | finding | M01-G's **spirit-level constitutional** dimension does not compete with the volitional primary but specifies its constitutional depth: the failure of volition in timidity is a spirit-level failure (2Ti 1:7), not merely a situational weakness. |

### T2.1.1  ·  Tier T2

> Is this characteristic explicitly located at the spirit level in the verse evidence?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | Explicit spirit-level location is present in only two locations across the cluster's 941 verses: (1) Isa 66:2 (E-VCG-02) — trembling at God's word located in the spirit as a reverence-posture; (2) 2Ti 1:7 (G-VCG-01) — timidity explicitly named as a spirit-level disposition not from God. The BOUNDARY term ke.ra (H3735, Dan 7:15) may constitute a third instance: "distress is located explicitly within Daniel's **spirit** — the visions grip the innermost self." This is in M01-BOUNDARY (not a full analytical sub-group), but the spirit-level location is explicit. All other sub-groups are silent on spirit-level location. |
| M01-A | silent | M01-A has no verse that explicitly locates reverential fear at the spirit level. The Jer 32:40 material (God "pledges to implant the fear of himself directly into the hearts of his people") locates the implantation in the heart, not the spirit. The Isa 11:2-3 material (fear-of-the-Lord as a Spirit-given inner quality resting on the messianic king) comes closest — it names fear as a Spirit-given endowment — but locates the gift in the Spirit of the Lord, not in the human spirit itself. |
| M01-B | silent | Acute fear, terror-as-force, dismay, somatic trembling (except E-VCG-02), and anticipatory dread are not explicitly located at the spirit level in any verse in these sub-groups. |
| M01-C | silent | Acute fear, terror-as-force, dismay, somatic trembling (except E-VCG-02), and anticipatory dread are not explicitly located at the spirit level in any verse in these sub-groups. |
| M01-D | silent | Acute fear, terror-as-force, dismay, somatic trembling (except E-VCG-02), and anticipatory dread are not explicitly located at the spirit level in any verse in these sub-groups. |
| M01-E | silent | Acute fear, terror-as-force, dismay, somatic trembling (except E-VCG-02), and anticipatory dread are not explicitly located at the spirit level in any verse in these sub-groups. |
| M01-E | finding | M01-E-VCG-02 contains the cluster's most explicit spirit-level location. Isa 66:2 (anchor): "Trembling at God's word is paired with humility and a contrite spirit as the inner posture God looks for; **the trembling is located in the spirit** and shows reverence that orients the whole inner person toward God's communication." The trembling-at-word characteristic is explicitly spirit-level in Isa 66:2. |
| M01-F | silent | Acute fear, terror-as-force, dismay, somatic trembling (except E-VCG-02), and anticipatory dread are not explicitly located at the spirit level in any verse in these sub-groups. |
| M01-G | finding | M01-G-VCG-01 contains the cluster's most explicit negative spirit-level location. 2Ti 1:7 (anchor): "Timidity is contrasted with the spirit God gives — power, love, and self-control; it is **identified as a spirit-level disposition that God has not implanted**, making it a failure of inner constitution rather than circumstance." Timidity is explicitly named as a spirit-level characteristic — the one the wrong spirit produces. |

### T2.1.2  ·  Tier T2

> Does the evidence indicate that this characteristic originates in or is primarily a spirit-level phenomenon?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The cluster's evidence confirms that the vast majority of M01's inner-being content does not originate at the spirit level. Spirit-level origin is confirmed for: (1) M01-G timidity (2Ti 1:7) and (2) M01-E-VCG-02 reverential trembling (Isa 66:2). The cluster's primary constitutional home is the heart (see T2.3), not the spirit. This is a significant finding: fear as experienced in Scripture is predominantly a heart-and-body phenomenon rather than a spirit-level one. |
| M01-A | silent | The evidence does not indicate that these sub-groups originate at the spirit level. Their constitutional language points to heart, soul, and body rather than spirit. |
| M01-B | silent | The evidence does not indicate that these sub-groups originate at the spirit level. Their constitutional language points to heart, soul, and body rather than spirit. |
| M01-C | silent | The evidence does not indicate that these sub-groups originate at the spirit level. Their constitutional language points to heart, soul, and body rather than spirit. |
| M01-D | silent | The evidence does not indicate that these sub-groups originate at the spirit level. Their constitutional language points to heart, soul, and body rather than spirit. |
| M01-E | finding | For the trembling-at-word tradition (Isa 66:2; Ezr 9:4; 10:3), the evidence suggests spirit-level origin. Isa 66:2 pairs the spirit-trembling with "humility and a contrite spirit" — both spirit-level characteristics in the programme. The trembling appears to flow from a spirit-posture of reverence, not from somatic arousal. |
| M01-F | silent | The evidence does not indicate that these sub-groups originate at the spirit level. Their constitutional language points to heart, soul, and body rather than spirit. |
| M01-G | finding | For timidity (M01-G), the 2Ti 1:7 evidence explicitly names it as spirit-level in origin — "a spirit-level disposition that God has not implanted." The origin is at the spirit, not a downstream effect of other inner states. |

### T2.1.3  ·  Tier T2

> What does spirit-level location reveal about the nature and depth of this characteristic?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | Where spirit-level location is evidenced (E-VCG-02, G-VCG-01), it reveals fear as operating at the deepest constitutional level. Spirit-level fear (whether the reverential trembling of Isa 66:2 or the failed constitution of 2Ti 1:7) is constitutional in the deepest sense — it defines what kind of person the individual is, not merely what they experience at a given moment. |
| M01-E | finding | The spirit-level location of trembling-at-God's-word in Isa 66:2 reveals that this form of reverential sobriety is constitutionally deeper than somatic trembling: it originates in the person's deepest self and expresses through the body. Isa 66:2's pairing with "humble and contrite spirit" positions this trembling as emerging from the same constitutional depth as contrition and humility — characteristics that the programme has confirmed operate at spirit level. This establishes a category of reverential trembling that is not a fear-response to threat but a spirit-posture of deep creaturely sobriety before God's communication. |
| M01-G | finding | The spirit-level location of timidity (2Ti 1:7) reveals that cowardly shrinking is not merely a situational weakness or temperamental trait — it is a constitutional failure at the deepest level. By naming it a spirit-level disposition God has not implanted, Paul identifies timidity as a replacement or absence at the person's constitutional core. This also implies that courage is itself a spirit-level characteristic — the spirit God does implant (power, love, self-control) is the spirit-level positive of which timidity is the spirit-level failure. |

No verse in these sub-groups explicitly locates the characteristic at the spirit level. The heart is the dominant constitutional home across these sub-groups (see T2.3). ### T2.10.1  ·  Tier T2

> Does this characteristic move across constitutional levels — from spirit to soul, from soul to body, or across boundaries in other directions?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | Constitutional movement in M01 is primarily from inner-person (heart, mind, or spirit) toward the body: inner states producing somatic expression. The movement from mind-to-heart-to-body is most fully documented in M01-F (de.a.gah progressing to quivering). The movement from spirit-to-body is documented in M01-E-VCG-02 (Isa 66:2). No movement from body inward (body feeding back to spirit) is explicitly documented, though it is consistent with the somatic marker framework in the science extract. |
| M01-A | finding | M01-A reverential fear moves from the heart (primary constitutional location) outward to conduct (ethical behaviour, Lev 19:14), cognition (wisdom, Pro 1:7), and community identity (Mal 3:16). This is a heart-to-action movement rather than a spirit-to-soul-to-body movement. The one direction that approaches spirit-to-heart is the Jer 32:40 implantation — God places the fear in the heart, but the text does not specify a spirit-level origination point in the human person. |
| M01-D | finding | M01-D shows movement from inner-person to body: Dan 5:6 (dismay striking the inner person, then manifesting as color change, limb-failure, and knee-knocking); Dan 7:28 (dismay working through thoughts and then changing color). Direction: inner-cognitive → somatic-expressive. |
| M01-E | finding | M01-E documents the most explicit constitutional movement in the cluster: inner fear → somatic trembling throughout the sub-group. The E-VCG-02 tradition (Isa 66:2) documents spirit → body: the spirit-posture of reverence produces trembling as its somatic expression. |
| M01-F | finding | M01-F shows movement from cognitive-anticipatory (the mind projecting forward, de.a.gah; 2Cor 12:20) through the heart (Pro 12:25: anxiety weighing down the heart) to the body (Eze 12:18: quivering in the most ordinary daily acts). Direction: mind → heart → body. |

### T2.10.2  ·  Tier T2

> What does the evidence reveal about the sequence or pattern of that movement?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The dominant pattern of constitutional movement in M01 is: triggering reality (external or internally projected) → inner-person engagement (heart, mind, spirit) → somatic expression. The sequence is consistent across sub-groups though the triggering reality and the somatic expression vary. The movement is consistently outward (inner → body), not inward (body → inner), in the verse evidence's explicit language. |
| M01-D | finding | M01-D's movement follows a pattern of: (1) triggering event (catastrophic news, overwhelming encounter); (2) inner cognitive disruption (thoughts race, Dan 4:19; comprehension collapses, Isa 21:3); (3) somatic manifestation (color change, limb-failure, Dan 5:6; speechlessness, Job 32:15). The sequence is event → inner disruption → somatic expression. |
| M01-E | finding | M01-E-VCG-01's Sinai trembling (Exo 19:16 anchor) follows a pattern of: (1) overwhelming sensory phenomena; (2) involuntary whole-body trembling (the somatic and inner state appear simultaneously — there is no gap between encounter and trembling). The sequence is encounter → simultaneous inner-and-somatic response. |
| M01-F | finding | M01-F's movement follows a pattern of: (1) anticipatory cognitive projection (thinking about possible futures); (2) heart-burden (Pro 12:25: anxiety weighing down the heart); (3) pervasive somatic expression (Eze 12:18: quivering even while eating and drinking). The sequence is cognitive → heart → somatic colonisation of daily acts. |

### T2.10.3  ·  Tier T2

> If no constitutional movement is evidenced, note this explicitly.

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| M01-A | finding | M01-A's reverential fear shows movement from heart-disposition to conduct and cognition, but not the spirit-to-soul-to-body constitutional movement in the strict sense. The movement is dispositional expression (inner posture governing outward action) rather than constitutional-level traverse. |
| M01-G | silent | M01-G timidity shows no documented constitutional movement. The spirit-level failure (2Ti 1:7) has no documented sequence of traverse from spirit through soul to body. The bodily inaction (burying the talent, locking doors) is evidenced but the constitutional movement from spirit-deficiency to behavioural paralysis is not explicitly traced in the verse evidence. |

### T2.2.1  ·  Tier T2

> Is this characteristic identified in the verse evidence as a soul-level phenomenon?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | Explicit soul-level location of fear within M01 is sparse: Psa 6:3 (dismay in the soul, M01-D-VCG-01 anchor) is the clearest instance. The Mat 10:28 material (M01-B-VCG-03: "fear of those who can only kill the body is contrasted with fear of God who can destroy **soul and body** in hell") locates the soul as the deeper seat of the person affected by ultimate fear — this is not a location statement but a comparative statement about depth. The cluster as a whole does not routinely locate fear at the soul level explicitly. |
| M01-A | silent | M01-A reverential fear is not explicitly located at the soul level. The nearest instance is Luk 1:50 ("fear of God here is the enduring inner orientation that receives divine mercy across generations — it is a reverent posture **of the soul** directed toward God") — but this is the translated Greek psychē context, and the meaning focuses on the posture being sustained, not on constitutional location at the soul level. |
| M01-D | finding | M01-D-VCG-01 has an explicit soul-level instance. Psa 6:3 (anchor): "**the psalmist's soul itself** is greatly dismayed — the inner being, not just the body, is the seat of this profound turmoil, and it drives the anguished cry to God asking how long." The dismay is explicitly in the soul (nefesh/Hebrew) as the seat of the profound turmoil. |
| M01-G | finding | M01-BOUNDARY and M01-B: Mat 26:37 (BOUNDARY term ademoneo): "Jesus begins to be sorrowful and troubled in Gethsemane; the distress is a deeply agitated inner state engaging **his soul** as he faces the approaching suffering." Soul-level location evidenced for ademoneo (BOUNDARY term). |

### T2.2.2  ·  Tier T2

> What does soul-level location reveal about this characteristic's place in the innermost personal experience?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | Where soul-level location is evidenced (Psa 6:3 for dismay), it reveals that fear at its most devastating reaches the person's innermost experienced life. The soul-level location confirms the depth of the characteristic's impact — it is not peripheral but central to who the person is. |
| M01-D | finding | Psa 6:3's soul-level location of dismay reveals that the inner collapse of M01-D reaches to the person's deepest experienced self. It is not merely an emotional event at the surface of the inner life but a shattering of the person at their innermost experiential level. The soul (nefesh as the seat of hunger, desire, and personal life in Hebrew anthropology) being "greatly dismayed" means the characteristic has penetrated to the core of personal existence. |

> If the evidence is silent on soul-level location, note this explicitly.

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| M01-A | silent | Sub-groups M01-A, B, C, E, F, and G are largely silent on explicit soul-level location of the characteristic. The heart is the dominant constitutional language across these sub-groups. Soul-level location is not a consistent finding across the cluster. |
| M01-B | silent | Sub-groups M01-A, B, C, E, F, and G are largely silent on explicit soul-level location of the characteristic. The heart is the dominant constitutional language across these sub-groups. Soul-level location is not a consistent finding across the cluster. |
| M01-C | silent | Sub-groups M01-A, B, C, E, F, and G are largely silent on explicit soul-level location of the characteristic. The heart is the dominant constitutional language across these sub-groups. Soul-level location is not a consistent finding across the cluster. |
| M01-E | silent | Sub-groups M01-A, B, C, E, F, and G are largely silent on explicit soul-level location of the characteristic. The heart is the dominant constitutional language across these sub-groups. Soul-level location is not a consistent finding across the cluster. |
| M01-F | silent | Sub-groups M01-A, B, C, E, F, and G are largely silent on explicit soul-level location of the characteristic. The heart is the dominant constitutional language across these sub-groups. Soul-level location is not a consistent finding across the cluster. |
| M01-G | silent | Sub-groups M01-A, B, C, E, F, and G are largely silent on explicit soul-level location of the characteristic. The heart is the dominant constitutional language across these sub-groups. Soul-level location is not a consistent finding across the cluster. |

### T2.3.1  ·  Tier T2

> Does the verse evidence locate this characteristic in the heart?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The heart is the most consistently evidenced constitutional location across all sub-groups of M01. It is explicitly named in M01-A (Deu 5:29; Jer 32:40), M01-B (Psa 27:3; 1Sa 28:5), M01-D (Job 23:16; Isa 21:4), M01-E (Job 37:1; 1Sa 4:13), M01-F (Deu 28:67; Pro 12:25), and implied in M01-G (Joh 14:27). The heart is fear's primary constitutional home in Scripture's own vocabulary. |
| M01-A | finding | Yes, extensively. Deu 5:29 ("God longs for Israel to have **a heart** always disposed to fear him — this reverence is located in the heart, seen as the seat of enduring moral orientation"); Jer 5:24 ("the people do not say **in their hearts** 'let us fear the Lord'"); Psa 86:11 ("fear of God requires inner integration; **a divided heart** is an obstacle to genuine reverence"); Jer 32:40 (God pledges to implant the fear "directly into **the hearts** of his people"). The heart is the dominant constitutional location for reverential fear in M01-A. |
| M01-B | finding | Yes. Psa 27:3 ("even when war surrounds him, the psalmist's **heart** will not fear — the inner locus of fear is explicitly named as the heart"); Neh 2:2 (Nehemiah's fear "seated in the heart, visible in his countenance"); 1Sa 28:5 (Saul's trembling "explicitly located in his **heart**"). Acute fear is located in the heart across multiple instances in M01-B. |
| M01-D | finding | Yes, centrally. Psa 6:3 anchor (dismay in the soul, which collapses the heart); Job 23:16 ("God has made **Job's heart** faint and the Almighty has terrified him — identifying the heart as the constitutional seat where divine action produces dismay and inner collapse"); Dan 5:10 (queen recognizes dismay "originates in the inner life of thought" — the inner life centered in the heart); Dan 5:6 (dismay "strikes Belshazzar's inner person" — the color change driven from within, centered in the heart-seat). |
| M01-E | finding | Yes, in specific instances. Isa 21:4 ("horror shudders through the prophet's **heart**, appalling him — the shuddering is located explicitly in the heart, the center of inner life"); Job 37:1 ("Elihu's **heart** trembles and leaps at the thunder of God's voice — locating trembling in the heart as the inner organ that responds with physical agitation to overwhelming divine power"); 1Sa 4:13 (Eli's trembling "located explicitly in **his heart**"). |
| M01-F | finding | Yes. Deu 28:67 ("dread is explicitly located in **the heart** and tied to what the eyes see — it produces such unbearable inner anguish that the sufferer constantly wishes the present moment away"); Pro 12:25 ("anxiety weighs down **a man's heart**"). The heart is the primary constitutional seat for M01-F's anticipatory dread. |
| M01-G | finding | Yes, by implication. Joh 14:27 ("Jesus contrasts his given peace with an inner timidity or cowardly shrinking, commanding **the heart** not to yield to that fearful recoiling"). |

### T2.3.2  ·  Tier T2

> What does the heart-location reveal — what aspect of the heart's integrating function (knowing, willing, feeling, moral awareness) does this characteristic engage?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The heart's three primary functions engaged by M01 are: (1) the willing function — M01-A's reverential fear governs the heart's moral choices; (2) the feeling function — M01-B, E, F locate the emotional experience of fear in the heart; (3) the moral-awareness function — M01-A's absence-of-fear is moral blindness (Psa 36:1), and M01-F's Deu 28:67 dread is located in the heart's awareness of its exposure. The knowing function is secondary across the cluster. |
| M01-A | finding | M01-A's heart-location engages the heart's willing and moral-awareness functions primarily. Deu 5:29 (heart disposed to fear — volitional); Jer 5:24 (people do not say in their hearts "let us fear" — the heart as the seat of moral self-direction, the decision to fear or not to fear); Jer 32:40 (fear implanted in the heart "preventing them from turning away" — the heart as the seat of covenant faithfulness). The heart's knowing function is also engaged: Psa 86:11 (heart integration required for genuine reverence — the heart must be unified in its knowing to produce authentic fear). |
| M01-B | finding | M01-B's heart-location engages the heart's feeling function primarily: Psa 27:3 (the heart "yields to dread" — the affective registration of threat); Neh 2:2 (fear "seated in the heart, visible in his countenance" — the heart as the source of the emotional experience that then appears on the face); 1Sa 28:5 ("Saul's visual perception of the enemy army triggers an inner collapse of courage, with the emotion immediately registered in his heart" — the heart as the affective registration center). |
| M01-D | finding | M01-D's heart-location engages the knowing and feeling functions together. Dan 5:10 (dismay "originates in the inner life of thought and then visibly destabilizes the body" — the knowing function disrupted); Job 23:16 ("God has made Job's heart faint" — the feeling/sustaining function of the heart). |
| M01-E | finding | M01-E's heart-location (Isa 21:4; Job 37:1) engages the feeling function — the trembling expresses the heart's emotional state through the body. |
| M01-F | finding | M01-F's heart-location engages the feeling function (Deu 28:67: unbearable anguish) and the moral-awareness function (Pro 12:25: anxiety as a burden on the heart relieved by an encouraging word — the heart's capacity to receive and be moved by speech). |

### T2.3.3  ·  Tier T2

> If the evidence is silent on heart-location, note this explicitly.

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| M01-C | finding | M01-C (terror-as-force) has limited explicit heart-location language. The closest is Psa 55:4 (M01-C-VCG-04 anchor: "terror is located in the heart — the terrors of death fall upon the psalmist, causing inner anguish so intense it is felt as a physical collapse within the chest") — an explicit heart-location for divine-majesty terror. Job 23:16 (M01-D-VCG-01: "God has made Job's heart faint") crosses into the D/C borderland. Within the pure M01-C terror-as-force texts (C-VCG-01, 02, 03), explicit heart-language is largely absent — the terror is described as falling upon the person as a whole rather than specifically entering the heart. |

### T2.4.1  ·  Tier T2

> Does the verse evidence locate this characteristic in the mind?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The mind is a secondary but evidenced constitutional location for M01, primarily in: M01-D (dismay disrupting thought, Dan 4:19; 7:28) and M01-F (anxiety as cognitive rumination, de.a.gah; 2Cor 12:20). The mind is not the primary location for fear across the cluster — the heart is dominant — but M01-D and M01-F have clear mind-engagement. |
| M01-A | silent | M01-A reverential fear is not explicitly located in the mind in the programme's dimension vocabulary. The cognitive engagement (Pro 1:7: wisdom's foundation) describes the mind's orientation but does not locate fear in the mind as a constitutional site. The heart is the primary location. |
| M01-B | finding | M01-B has limited mind-location. Dan 4:5 (M01-B-VCG-01: "fear is produced by a dream that targets the mind — the visions of the head alarm the inner person, showing that dread can be generated internally through the mind's nocturnal experience"). This is a clear mind-location for one form of acute fear. Job 22:10 (M01-D boundary: "sudden terror overwhelms Job because snares surround him" — the inner shock strikes without conscious mind engagement). |
| M01-D | finding | M01-D has significant mind-location. Dan 4:19 (D-VCG-03: "dismay holds Daniel for a moment as **his thoughts** race — the inner impact of understanding a terrible message temporarily overrides speech and composure, with alarmed thoughts pressing on the inner person"); Dan 5:10 (dismay "originates in the inner life of thought"); Dan 7:28 ("dismay works through **Daniel's thoughts**"). The mind is a significant secondary constitutional location for M01-D. |
| M01-F | finding | M01-F has the strongest mind-location. The de.a.gah terms (H1674 — anxiety, worry) carry a cognitive-ruminating quality: Jer 49:23 ("anxiety seizes Damascus as troubled restlessness on hearing bad news — the inner state is compared to a churning sea unable to be still, showing anxiety as an agitated, **uncontrollable inner condition**"); 2Cor 12:20 anchor ("Paul's fear is an anticipatory dread rooted in **thought** about what he may find — engaging the mind with anxious expectation before the visit even happens"). The M01-F-VCG-05 pastoral anxiety is explicitly cognitive-anticipatory: it is rooted in thinking about a future encounter, not in present perception of threat. |

### T2.4.2  ·  Tier T2

> What does mind-location reveal — what aspect of the mind's function (thought, discernment, understanding) does this characteristic engage?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | Mind-engagement by M01 is primarily in the thought function (M01-D: comprehending a terrible message; M01-F: anticipating a threatening future). The discernment and understanding functions are engaged indirectly — fear both enables and distorts discernment, depending on whether it is reverential (M01-A, which opens the mind to genuine knowledge) or anxious (M01-F, which distorts by excessive projection). |
| M01-D | finding | M01-D's mind-location reveals fear engaging the thought function primarily: Dan 4:19 (alarmed thoughts overwhelming the ability to speak), Dan 7:28 (thoughts as the originating site of dismay-agitation). The dismay begins in the mind as comprehension and then destabilizes body and composure. This is the reverse of M01-E (where the body registers the inner state): in M01-D, the mind processes the terrible message and the processing produces the inner collapse. |
| M01-F | finding | M01-F's mind-location reveals anxiety engaging the thought function in its anticipatory mode: 2Cor 12:20 (anxious expectation before the visit — the mind projecting forward and processing possible negative outcomes). The de.a.gah terms describe a mind that cannot be stilled, circling around potential threats. This engages the understanding function (assessing what might happen) but in a disordered mode (unable to rest). |

### T2.5.1  ·  Tier T2

The BOUNDARY term ademoneo (Mat 26:37) engages "his soul" (psychē) in the Gethsemane distress. --- [S] Beyond the Psa 6:3 soul-instance and the BOUNDARY material, no additional soul-level locations distinct from heart and mind are evidenced consistently across these sub-groups. |

### T2.5.2  ·  Tier T2

> If so, what is that location, and what does it reveal?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| M01-D | finding | The soul-location (nefesh) in Psa 6:3 reveals that dismay penetrates to the personal-life center of the person. The nefesh in Hebrew anthropology is the seat of the person's own experienced aliveness — hunger, desire, vitality. When dismay seizes the nefesh, the person's capacity to sustain their own inner life is disrupted. This is constitutionally deeper than heart-disturbance: it is the person's experienced existence itself that is shaken. |

### T2.6.1  ·  Tier T2

> Does the verse evidence link this characteristic to a specific body part?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | M01 links to body-parts across multiple sub-groups. The most consistently named body-parts are: **bones** (shaking), **flesh** (trembling), **heart** (as organ of fear-registration), **face/countenance** (expressing fear visibly), **knees** (giving way), **hair** (bristling with horror), **lips** (quivering), and **hands** (paralyzed or dropping from work). M01-E is the anatomically richest sub-group. The cluster as a whole confirms that fear is one of Scripture's most somatically described inner characteristics. |
| M01-A | finding | M01-A has one explicit body-part link: Psa 119:120 (M01-E-VCG-02, but relevant to the reverential dimension): "Fear of God's judgments produces a somatic response — **the psalmist's flesh trembles**." The flesh is the body-part named. Lev 19:14's prohibition against exploiting "the deaf and the blind" implies bodily vulnerability as the context for fear's ethical restraint, but the fear itself is not located in a specific body part. |
| M01-B | finding | M01-B has body-part links through the trembling-in-the-heart pattern: 1Sa 28:5 (Saul's trembling "explicitly located in **his heart**" — the heart as a body-organ), Neh 2:2 (fear "visible in his countenance" — the face as the body-part expressing the inner fear). |
| M01-C | finding | M01-C-VCG-04 has an explicit body-part link: Psa 55:4 (anchor: "terror is located **in the heart** — the terrors of death fall upon the psalmist, causing inner anguish so intense it is felt as a physical collapse within **the chest**"). The chest/heart-organ is the body-part named for the physical experience of divine-majesty terror. |
| M01-D | finding | M01-D has significant body-part evidence: Dan 5:6 (anchor: dismay causes "**limbs to give way** and **knees to knock**"); Isa 21:3 ("cannot see" — the eyes affected); Job 32:15 (speechlessness — the speech faculties affected). Multiple body-parts are named as sites of dismay's manifestation. |
| M01-E | finding | M01-E is the sub-group with the richest body-part links: **bones** shaking (Job 4:14: "physically expressing the inner terror by shaking all his bones"), **flesh** trembling (Job 21:6 anchor E-VCG-05: "shuddering takes hold of Job's flesh"), **hair** bristling (Eze 27:35 anchor E-VCG-03: "kings' hair bristles"), **lips** quivering (Hab 3:16: "trembling saturates the entire inner and physical person — his lips quiver and his bones decay"), **knees** knocking (Dan 5:6 — on the D/E boundary), and the whole body trembling involuntarily (Exo 19:16 anchor E-VCG-01). E has the most body-part diversity of any sub-group. |
| M01-F | finding | M01-F has body-part links through the somatic-expression of anxiety: Eze 12:18 anchor (quivering "accompanies drinking water — inner agitation has become so pervasive it manifests in the body during the most ordinary acts of daily survival"), Eze 12:19 (anxiety shaping every meal — the body's eating activity colonised by anxiety). The body-parts are the hands, mouth, and body in general acts of eating and drinking. |
| M01-G | silent | M01-G timidity has no explicit body-part link beyond the implication that it produces physical inaction (burying the talent, locking the doors) rather than being located in a specific body-part. |

### T2.6.2  ·  Tier T2

> If so, what is Scripture doing by making that link — is it emphatic, functional, expressive, indicative, or mediating?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | Scripture's body-part linking in M01 serves multiple functions: expressive (showing inner states through bodily manifestation), indicative (locating the experience in specific bodily sites), and functional (showing the inner state's effect on bodily activity). The preponderance of expressive and indicative links confirms that Scripture is attending to fear as a whole-person experience, not merely an internal mental event. |
| M01-A | finding | The flesh-trembling link in Psa 119:120 is **expressive**: the trembling of flesh expresses the inner reverential dread; it shows the inner state reaching outward to the body. |
| M01-C | finding | The heart/chest link in Psa 55:4 (M01-C-VCG-04 anchor) is **indicative**: it locates the experience of divine-majesty terror in a specific constitutional site (the heart as the centre of inner life), indicating where the terror is felt. |
| M01-D | finding | The body-part links in M01-D (Dan 5:6: limbs giving way, knees knocking; Isa 21:3: cannot see; Job 32:15: speechlessness) are **expressive** — they show the completeness of the inner collapse by its bodily manifestation. They also function as **indicative** of the severity: color change, limb-failure, and eye-failure indicate that the dismay has overwhelmed the person's ability to sustain basic bodily function. |
| M01-E | finding | M01-E's body-part links are primarily **expressive** — the bones, flesh, hair, and lips register the inner fear by their involuntary response. But the Isa 66:2 anchor (trembling located in the spirit) suggests that for E-VCG-02 the direction is different: the spirit-posture expresses through the body, making the body-link **mediating** — the body mediates the spirit's reverence into visible form. |
| M01-F | finding | M01-F's body-link in Eze 12:18 (quivering while drinking) is **functional**: it shows that anxiety is not merely a conscious experience but has colonised the body's automatic activities. The link is functional because it shows how the inner state affects the person's ordinary functioning. |

### T2.6.3  ·  Tier T2

> If no body-part link is evidenced, note this explicitly.

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| M01-G | silent | M01-G (timidity and cowardly shrinking) has no explicit body-part link. The inaction it produces is behaviourally evidenced (burying the talent, locking doors) but the body-part that mediates the timidity is not named. |

### T2.7.1  ·  Tier T2

> Where a body-characteristic link exists, which direction does it run — does the soul express through the body, does the body feed back to the soul, or does it run in both directions?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The primary direction across M01 is soul/inner person → body (inner fear expressing through somatic symptoms). The evidence is consistent with a primary expressive direction but leaves open the possibility of somatic feedback to the inner state, particularly in the chronic conditions of M01-E and M01-F. The M01-E-VCG-02 (spirit-level trembling) confirms the soul-to-body direction most clearly. |
| M01-A | finding | For M01-A's somatic dimension (Psa 119:120) and M01-E-VCG-02 (trembling at God's word), the direction runs from soul/spirit → body. The reverential dread or spirit-trembling is the inner originating state; the bodily trembling is the expression. Direction: soul expressing through the body. |
| M01-B | finding | For the involuntary somatic expressions in M01-B (face-expression, heart-registration), M01-D (limbs giving way, color change), and most of M01-E (theophanic trembling, military panic-trembling), the direction is complex. The triggering stimulus is external (sight of threat, divine encounter, overwhelming news); the internal state arises; the body expresses it. This is primarily soul/inner person → body, but with an important caveat: the bodily experience of trembling may itself deepen or intensify the inner fear state (the body feeding back to the soul). The Damasio somatic marker framework from the science extract is relevant here: somatic states are constitutive of emotional experience, not merely expressive. |
| M01-D | finding | For the involuntary somatic expressions in M01-B (face-expression, heart-registration), M01-D (limbs giving way, color change), and most of M01-E (theophanic trembling, military panic-trembling), the direction is complex. The triggering stimulus is external (sight of threat, divine encounter, overwhelming news); the internal state arises; the body expresses it. This is primarily soul/inner person → body, but with an important caveat: the bodily experience of trembling may itself deepen or intensify the inner fear state (the body feeding back to the soul). The Damasio somatic marker framework from the science extract is relevant here: somatic states are constitutive of emotional experience, not merely expressive. |
| M01-E | finding | For M01-A's somatic dimension (Psa 119:120) and M01-E-VCG-02 (trembling at God's word), the direction runs from soul/spirit → body. The reverential dread or spirit-trembling is the inner originating state; the bodily trembling is the expression. Direction: soul expressing through the body. |
| M01-E | finding | For the involuntary somatic expressions in M01-B (face-expression, heart-registration), M01-D (limbs giving way, color change), and most of M01-E (theophanic trembling, military panic-trembling), the direction is complex. The triggering stimulus is external (sight of threat, divine encounter, overwhelming news); the internal state arises; the body expresses it. This is primarily soul/inner person → body, but with an important caveat: the bodily experience of trembling may itself deepen or intensify the inner fear state (the body feeding back to the soul). The Damasio somatic marker framework from the science extract is relevant here: somatic states are constitutive of emotional experience, not merely expressive. |
| M01-F | finding | M01-F's body link (Eze 12:18: quivering while drinking) runs from inner anxiety → body (soul expressing through body). But the ongoing somatic anxiety may deepen the inner state, suggesting bidirectional influence. |

### T2.7.2  ·  Tier T2

> What is the consequence of that directionality for understanding the characteristic?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The directionality is significant: M01 consistently describes fear as originating in the inner person's engagement with a reality (God, threat, terrible news) and expressing through the body. This distinguishes Scripture's fear-vocabulary from a purely physiological account (stimulus → body → emotion) and from a purely cognitive account (appraisal → emotion). The biblical account integrates both dimensions within a soul-body unity in which the inner person's engagement with reality produces both inner experience and somatic expression simultaneously. |
| M01-A | finding | The soul-to-body direction for reverential trembling (M01-E-VCG-02) and reverential fear (M01-A's somatic dimension) confirms that these forms of fear are not generated by bodily arousal but by the soul's engagement with God's reality. The body is the expression vehicle, not the origin. This is significant for understanding M01-A: reverential fear is not caused by physiological arousal (the science extract's amygdala-model) but by the person's inner recognition of God's reality. The direction is spirit/soul → body, not stimulus → body → emotion. |
| M01-D | finding | The soul-to-body direction for theophanic trembling and dismay confirms that these are inner events that produce somatic consequences, not somatic events that produce inner experiences. However, the feedback loop (body → soul) may be evidenced in the persistence of the condition: once trembling begins, it may intensify the inner experience. This is the somatic marker dynamic the science extract identifies. |
| M01-E | finding | The soul-to-body direction for reverential trembling (M01-E-VCG-02) and reverential fear (M01-A's somatic dimension) confirms that these forms of fear are not generated by bodily arousal but by the soul's engagement with God's reality. The body is the expression vehicle, not the origin. This is significant for understanding M01-A: reverential fear is not caused by physiological arousal (the science extract's amygdala-model) but by the person's inner recognition of God's reality. The direction is spirit/soul → body, not stimulus → body → emotion. |
| M01-E | finding | The soul-to-body direction for theophanic trembling and dismay confirms that these are inner events that produce somatic consequences, not somatic events that produce inner experiences. However, the feedback loop (body → soul) may be evidenced in the persistence of the condition: once trembling begins, it may intensify the inner experience. This is the somatic marker dynamic the science extract identifies. |

### T2.7.3  ·  Tier T2

> If no body-characteristic link is evidenced, note this explicitly.

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| M01-G | silent | M01-G (timidity) has no evidenced body-characteristic link and therefore no directional finding to report. |

### T2.8.1  ·  Tier T2

> Does sustained operation of this characteristic leave a constitutional deposit in the body or its design — including DNA or generational consequence?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | silent | The verse evidence across M01 is silent on constitutional deposit in the body or generational biological consequence. The generational effects evidenced are formational (fear learned and transmitted, Deu 31:12-13) and covenantal (God's steadfast love running to those who fear him across generations, Psa 103:17) rather than constitutional-biological. |
| M01-A | silent | M01-A's reverential fear does not produce explicit constitutional deposit in the body. The generational transmission evidenced (Deu 31:12-13; Psa 103:17) is through formation and covenant, not through biological or constitutional deposit. |
| M01-B | silent | M01-B (acute fear), M01-C (terror), M01-D (dismay), M01-E (trembling), and M01-G (timidity) are silent on constitutional deposit in the body. |
| M01-C | silent | M01-B (acute fear), M01-C (terror), M01-D (dismay), M01-E (trembling), and M01-G (timidity) are silent on constitutional deposit in the body. |
| M01-D | silent | M01-B (acute fear), M01-C (terror), M01-D (dismay), M01-E (trembling), and M01-G (timidity) are silent on constitutional deposit in the body. |
| M01-E | silent | M01-B (acute fear), M01-C (terror), M01-D (dismay), M01-E (trembling), and M01-G (timidity) are silent on constitutional deposit in the body. |
| M01-F | finding | M01-F-VCG-01 and VCG-03 have the nearest evidence to constitutional deposit: Heb 2:15 ("fear of death held people in **lifelong** inner slavery") suggests that sustained anxiety/dread produces a settled constitutional condition that is not easily reversed — it is not merely a repeated experience but a settled bondage. This is not explicitly bodily deposit but constitutional entrenchment. |
| M01-G | silent | M01-B (acute fear), M01-C (terror), M01-D (dismay), M01-E (trembling), and M01-G (timidity) are silent on constitutional deposit in the body. |

### T2.8.2  ·  Tier T2

> What evidence supports or contradicts this?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | silent | No verse in M01 explicitly addresses constitutional deposit in the body. The Heb 2:15 "lifelong slavery" language could be read as suggesting entrenchment rather than deposit, but this is inferential. No supporting or contradicting verse is identified. |

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |

| — | silent | The evidence across all M01 sub-groups is silent on constitutional deposit in the body or generational biological consequence. This finding is noted and fed forward to T5.7 as required. |

### T2.9.1  ·  Tier T2

> Where does this characteristic originate constitutionally — is it generated from within the person, received from outside, bestowed by God, or carried generationally?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | M01's characteristic has at least four documented origins: divine gift/implantation (M01-A, Jer 32:40), external triggering (M01-B, C, D, E-VCG-01), inner formation through hearing and practice (M01-A, Deu 31:12-13), and constitutional failure (M01-G, 2Ti 1:7). The origin is not singular across the cluster. |
| M01-A | finding | M01-A's reverential fear has multiple documented origins: (1) **divinely bestowed** — Jer 32:40 (God pledges to "implant the fear of himself directly into the hearts of his people"), Isa 11:2-3 (fear-of-the-Lord as a Spirit-given inner quality resting on the messianic king); (2) **formed through hearing** — Deu 4:10; 31:12-13 (fear is an outcome God intends from the Horeb encounter; cultivated through regular Torah reading); (3) **transmitted generationally** — Deu 31:13 (children to be taught so they may learn to fear God); (4) **responsive to God's acts** — Exo 14:31 (fear arising from witnessing God's power); (5) **socially reinforced** — Deu 13:11; 17:13 (public judgment producing fear throughout the community as deterrent). |
| M01-B | finding | M01-B's acute fear originates externally — it is triggered by an external stimulus (threat, divine encounter, inexplicable event). Gen 32:7 (Esau's approach triggers Jacob's fear), Luk 2:9 (the angel's appearance and divine glory trigger the shepherds' fear). The origin is outside the person and involuntary. |
| M01-C | finding | M01-C's terror-as-force originates from God (C-VCG-01: "God's terror is sent"), from the inherent quality of powerful entities (C-VCG-05: the Babylonians' terror as self-derived, Hab 1:7), and from the dynamics of violent history (C-VCG-02: encircling terror in the wicked's experience). Multiple external origins. |
| M01-D | finding | M01-D's dismay originates externally (from catastrophic news, from witnessing collapse, from divine action) — it is not generated from within but imposed by circumstances. |
| M01-E | finding | M01-E's trembling has mixed origin: theophanic trembling (E-VCG-01) originates from the external divine encounter; trembling-at-word (E-VCG-02) originates from the spirit's inner reverence. Two distinct origins within the same sub-group. |
| M01-F | finding | M01-F's anticipatory dread originates from within (the mind/heart projecting forward) but in response to real external circumstances (covenantal curse, judicial expectation). The origin is both inner (the cognitive projection) and outer (the real threat or covenant reality being projected about). |
| M01-G | finding | M01-G's timidity has the most explicit negative-origin statement: 2Ti 1:7 (it is not from God; by implication it originates from a failed or corrupted inner constitution, not from divine gift). |

### T2.9.2  ·  Tier T2

> What does the evidence reveal about whether the origin is singular or multiple?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The origin is multiple across the cluster. The multiplicity is structured: ordered fear (M01-A) is formed through divine gift and human formation; disordered fear (M01-G) originates in constitutional failure; acute fear (M01-B) is externally triggered; chronic anxiety (M01-F) originates in the mind's forward projection in response to real circumstances. |
| M01-A | finding | M01-A has a clearly multiple origin: divine implantation, human formation through hearing, social reinforcement, and responsive awe at God's acts all produce the same reverential fear. This multiplicity is itself a finding: the characteristic can be generated through different pathways converging on the same inner disposition. |

### T2.9.3  ·  Tier T2

> Does the origin of this characteristic change across different contexts evidenced in Scripture?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The origin changes consistently with context. This is expected given the cluster's scope — the characteristic spans from military crisis to divine encounter to social pressure. The changing origin across contexts is not a contradicion but reflects the breadth of the cluster's evidential base. |
| M01-A | finding | Yes. In the wisdom tradition (Pro 1:7; 9:10), fear-of-God arises through seeking wisdom — it is the fruit of diligent pursuit. In the Deuteronomic tradition (Deu 4:10; 31:12-13), it arises through hearing Torah. In the prophetic tradition (Jer 32:40), it is divinely implanted. In the narrative tradition (Exo 14:31; Hag 1:12), it arises from encountering God's power through events. The origin varies by canonical context. |
| M01-B | finding | Yes. In OT military contexts, acute fear arises from visible human threat. In NT theophanic contexts, it arises from encountering divine power through Jesus. In the social-fear contexts (B-VCG-04), it arises from crowd opinion and social pressure. The triggering context shapes the character of the fear. |

### T3.1.1  ·  Tier T3

> Does this characteristic engage the perceptive faculty — the inner senses including hearing, sight, taste, touch, smell, and spiritual discernment — and if so, which inner sense and how?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The perceptive faculty is engaged across all sub-groups of M01. The dominant inner senses are **sight** (primary across B, C, D, E-VCG-03, A) and **hearing** (primary in A, E-VCG-01, F). Spiritual discernment is evidenced in M01-A (Job 1:1) and M01-B (1Sa 18:12). The perceptive faculty is the trigger-gateway for fear across the cluster — what is seen or heard initiates the fear-state. This confirms that M01 is heavily perception-driven: the characteristic is routinely initiated by perceptive engagement with external reality. |
| M01-A | finding | M01-A engages the perceptive faculty primarily through **sight** and **hearing** as triggers of reverential awe. Exo 14:31 (Israel witnessed God's power over Egypt and feared the Lord — sight of divine action triggers reverential fear); Psa 145:6 (God's deeds produce fear-inducing wonder in those who "speak of them" — verbal-cognitive perception); Hag 1:12 (hearing the prophetic word produces fear — auditory trigger). Also spiritual discernment: Job 1:1 (Job's fear of God is the inner moral quality that discerns rightly across all circumstances — a discernment-based orientation rather than a perception-based response). |
| M01-B | finding | M01-B engages the perceptive faculty extensively, primarily through **sight**: 1Sa 17:24 (sight of Goliath produces extreme fear), Mat 14:26 (sight of Jesus walking on water triggers fear), Dan 5:6 (sight of the writing on the wall produces dismay/fear), Luk 2:9 (sight of the angel and divine glory fills the shepherds with fear). **Hearing** also triggers B-fear: 2Ki 19:6 (fear triggered by Assyrian threatening words), Jer 51:46 (fearfulness from successive alarming reports). Spiritual discernment: 1Sa 18:12 (Saul's fear of David "rooted in theological perception — he recognises that God's presence has transferred from himself to David"). |
| M01-C | finding | M01-C engages **sight** as the primary perceptive trigger: Dan 2:31 (the great image's appearance produces fear), Job 41:14 (Leviathan's face radiates terror outward — sight of Leviathan produces terror in beholders). Also the inner sense of **hearing**: Jer 20:10 (Jeremiah hears whispers of "terror on every side" — auditory trigger for the encircling-terror experience). |
| M01-D | finding | M01-D engages **sight** and **hearing**: Isa 21:3 (the vision the prophet sees produces dismay so overwhelming he cannot see), Dan 7:7 (the fearful beast — its appearance produces fear as the immediate inner response to sight of its dreadful strength). The distortion of sight and hearing (cannot see, speechlessness) is the distinctive pattern of D's perceptive engagement. |
| M01-E | finding | M01-E engages **hearing** as a primary perceptive trigger: Exo 19:16 (thunder and trumpet at Sinai produced involuntary trembling — the auditory trigger is explicit). Amos 3:6 (a trumpet blast naturally produces trembling — auditory). Job 37:1 ("Elihu's heart trembles and leaps at the **thunder** of God's voice" — auditory trigger for somatic trembling). Also sight: Eze 26:16 (trembling seizes the sea-princes at **witnessing** Tyre's fall — visual trigger for somatic trembling). |
| M01-F | finding | M01-F engages **hearing** as a primary trigger: Jer 49:23 (anxiety seizes Damascus "on hearing bad news"); 2Cor 12:20 (Paul's anticipatory dread rooted in "thought about what he may find" — imaginative rather than actual perceptive engagement). Also **sight**: Deu 28:67 ("dread explicitly located in the heart and tied to what **the eyes see**" — visual experience driving anticipatory dread). |
| M01-G | silent | M01-G timidity's perceptive triggers are not explicitly described in the verse evidence. The threat situations (storm, master's harshness, persecution) are implied but the specific inner-sense engagement is not named. |

### T3.1.2  ·  Tier T3

> Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair the perceptive faculty in the person?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The perceptive faculty is: **enabled/deepened** by M01-A reverential fear; **bypassed** by the involuntary character of M01-B's theophanic fear (the disciples cannot choose not to fear the risen Jesus); **impaired** by M01-D dismay (systematic shutdown) and by M01-B's distorting social-fear (Isa 8:12: social fear "distorts perception of true danger"). The pattern suggests that ordered fear (M01-A) enhances perception while disordered fear (M01-B's social register, M01-C, M01-D) impairs it. |
| M01-A | finding | M01-A reverential fear **enables and deepens** perception in the ordered direction. Pro 2:5 ("fear of the Lord is the fruit of earnest seeking after wisdom — an inner understanding arrived at through diligent pursuit") implies that fear sharpens spiritual discernment. Psa 25:14 (fear positions the person to receive God's friendship and knowledge of his covenant — covenant knowledge opened by fear-posture). Fear of God appears to enable a kind of receptive attentiveness to God's communication. |
| M01-B | finding | Acute fear (M01-B), terror-as-force (M01-C), and dismay (M01-D) routinely **impair** the perceptive faculty: Isa 21:3 (dismay so overwhelming the prophet "cannot see"); Job 32:15 (friends dismayed into speechlessness — the verbal-perceptive loop shut down); Dan 5:6 (color change and limb-failure as perceptive-system overwhelm); Mat 14:26 (disciples mis-perceive Jesus as a ghost — fear distorting perceptive identification). M01-D-VCG-03 is the most explicit: dismay systematically shuts down perception and speech. |
| M01-C | finding | Acute fear (M01-B), terror-as-force (M01-C), and dismay (M01-D) routinely **impair** the perceptive faculty: Isa 21:3 (dismay so overwhelming the prophet "cannot see"); Job 32:15 (friends dismayed into speechlessness — the verbal-perceptive loop shut down); Dan 5:6 (color change and limb-failure as perceptive-system overwhelm); Mat 14:26 (disciples mis-perceive Jesus as a ghost — fear distorting perceptive identification). M01-D-VCG-03 is the most explicit: dismay systematically shuts down perception and speech. |
| M01-D | finding | Acute fear (M01-B), terror-as-force (M01-C), and dismay (M01-D) routinely **impair** the perceptive faculty: Isa 21:3 (dismay so overwhelming the prophet "cannot see"); Job 32:15 (friends dismayed into speechlessness — the verbal-perceptive loop shut down); Dan 5:6 (color change and limb-failure as perceptive-system overwhelm); Mat 14:26 (disciples mis-perceive Jesus as a ghost — fear distorting perceptive identification). M01-D-VCG-03 is the most explicit: dismay systematically shuts down perception and speech. |
| M01-E | finding | M01-E somatic trembling — where it is the response to theophany — does not impair but rather **registers** divine reality through the body. The E-VCG-02 trembling-at-word tradition may **deepen** receptive perception: Ezr 9:4; 10:3 (those who tremble at God's word gather for covenant action — the trembling marks a community whose perceptive attentiveness to God's word is heightened). |

### T3.1.3  ·  Tier T3

> What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with perception reveal about the nature of this characteristic?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The pattern reveals that fear is a perceptively-saturated characteristic: it is triggered by perception (sight, hearing) and it modifies perception (enabling or impairing). Ordered fear (M01-A) enables a clearer perception of God and reality; disordered fear (M01-D's dismay, M01-B's social fear) systematically distorts or shuts down perception. This is a significant finding: the presence or absence of correctly ordered fear shapes what the person can see and hear accurately. The cluster confirms that fear is not merely an inner experience but a perceptual orientation — it determines what the person is able to register about the world. |

### T3.10.1  ·  Tier T3

> Does this characteristic engage conscientiousness — the integrated response of moral awareness, volition, and action — and if so, how?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | M01-A is the most conscientiousness-enabling sub-group. Timidity (M01-G) is the most conscientiousness-impairing. Social fear (M01-B-VCG-04) disrupts conscientiousness by substituting crowd-fear for moral awareness. The pattern: ordered fear integrates moral awareness, volition, and action; disordered fear disintegrates them. |
| M01-A | finding | M01-A is the most conscientious sub-group in the programme's vocabulary. Fear of God as governing orientation produces integrated moral awareness + volition + action: the midwives (Exo 1:17 — moral awareness of God's authority + will to disobey Pharaoh + action of sparing the children); Nehemiah (Neh 5:15 — moral awareness of unjust authority patterns + will to act differently + action of not burdening the people); the God-fearer of Psa 128:1 (fearing the Lord and walking in his ways — the disposition integrating into a whole pattern of life). Conscientiousness is the lived expression of M01-A reverential fear. |
| M01-G | finding | M01-G timidity represents the failure of conscientiousness. Mat 25:25 (the servant had moral awareness of the master's expectations and the will to preserve himself, but not the integrated will-and-action of faithful stewardship — the three elements of conscientiousness are present but disintegrated by timidity). |

### T3.10.2  ·  Tier T3

> Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair conscientiousness in the person?
