| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | Ordered fear (M01-A) is one of the programme's clearest conscientiousness-enabling characteristics. It integrates the inner person's moral awareness, will, and action into a coherent pattern of faithful living. |
| M01-A | finding | M01-A **enables and deepens** conscientiousness. The God-fearer acts rightly even when not observed (Lev 19:14), sustains ethical conduct over time (Neh 5:15), and integrates belief with action (Job 1:1: "blameless, upright, fearing God, turning from evil" — a fully integrated character description). |
| M01-B | finding | Social fear (M01-B-VCG-04) and timidity (M01-G) **bypass and impair** conscientiousness. Social fear displaces moral awareness with crowd-preference (Gal 2:12; 1Sa 15:24). Timidity suppresses the volitional-action dimension of the conscience-volition-action triad. |
| M01-G | finding | Social fear (M01-B-VCG-04) and timidity (M01-G) **bypass and impair** conscientiousness. Social fear displaces moral awareness with crowd-preference (Gal 2:12; 1Sa 15:24). Timidity suppresses the volitional-action dimension of the conscience-volition-action triad. |

### T3.10.3  ·  Tier T3

> What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with conscientiousness reveal about the nature of this characteristic?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The pattern reveals that ordered fear of God is not an isolated inner experience but an integrating principle of the inner life. It enables the person to act consistently with their moral awareness and will across contexts — including contexts of power asymmetry (Lev 19:14: power over the deaf and blind), sustained difficulty (Neh 5:9-15), and crisis (Job 2:3: fear holding through intense suffering). Conscientiousness is one of fear-of-God's most distinctive outputs. The cluster confirms that the inner life of the God-fearer is characterised by integrated wholeness, while the inner life of those governed by social fear or timidity is characterised by fragmentation. |

### T3.11.1  ·  Tier T3

> Does this characteristic engage the relational capacity — the constitutional equipment for genuine connection with another person — and if so, how?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The relational capacity is engaged across M01 in three modes: (1) **enabled** — by M01-A, which grounds human-human and human-God relationship in reverential fear; (2) **distorted** — by M01-B's social fear, which governs relational conduct through crowd-fear rather than truth and genuine care; (3) **expressed** — by M01-F-VCG-05 (pastoral anxiety flowing from relational love). |
| M01-A | finding | M01-A engages the relational capacity directly and pervasively. Reverential fear of God is the ground of human-human relationships throughout M01-A: Lev 19:14 (fear governing treatment of vulnerable others — relational ethics rooted in divine fear); Lev 25:17; 36; 43 (fear governing economic relationships and power-over-servant relationships); Gen 42:18 (Joseph's fear of God governing his treatment of his brothers — "an inner moral orientation that governs his treatment of others and gives him a reason not to exploit his power"). Fear of God governs relational conduct toward others precisely where human oversight is absent. |
| M01-A | finding | Psa 25:14 (anchor: "the fear of God positions a person for intimate **covenant relationship** with the Lord — those whose inner life is marked by this reverence receive God's **friendship** and knowledge of his covenant") is the most explicit human-divine relational statement. Fear enables genuine relationship with God. |
| M01-B | finding | M01-B's social fear (B-VCG-04) engages the relational capacity by distorting it: fear of social consequences governs relational behavior (Joh 9:22: parents' fear of the Jews governing their speech and deflecting questions to their son; Joh 19:38: Joseph's discipleship hidden because fear of the Jews governed his public behavior). Social fear produces relational inauthenticity. |
| M01-F | finding | M01-F-VCG-05 (pastoral anxiety) engages the relational capacity through care: Paul's anticipatory dread for his churches (2Cor 12:20; Gal 4:11) is relationally motivated — the anxiety flows from genuine concern for the other. Phili 2:26 (Epaphroditus's distress because the Philippians heard of his illness — "the distress is relational, an inner anguish arising from **concern about how his condition has troubled those he loves**"). |

### T3.11.2  ·  Tier T3

> Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair relational capacity in the person?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | Ordered fear (M01-A) enables relational depth; social fear (M01-B-VCG-04) impairs relational authenticity; dismay (M01-D) ruptures relational bonds; pastoral anxiety (M01-F-VCG-05) flows from and expresses genuine relational care. The cluster's relational picture is complex and differentiated. |
| M01-A | finding | M01-A **enables and deepens** relational capacity. Fear of God is the ground of trustworthy, just, and generous relational conduct (Exo 18:21: fear of God as an inner moral quality qualifying men for leadership paired with trustworthiness; Act 10:2: Cornelius's fear of God expressing outwardly in "generous almsgiving and continual prayer"). Fear of God produces the inner orientation from which genuine other-regard flows. |
| M01-B | finding | Social fear **impairs** relational capacity by substituting crowd-fear for genuine other-care: Gal 2:12 (Peter's withdrawal damaging the relational community); Joh 9:22 (parents' fear-governed deflection damaging their son's witness). Social fear produces relational withdrawal, inauthenticity, and betrayal. |
| M01-D | finding | Dismay **impairs** relational capacity: Psa 31:11 (M01-B-VCG-04: "the psalmist has become an object of dread to his acquaintances — his suffering causes those who know him to recoil in alarm, so that dread **operates as a social and relational rupture**"). Dismay drives others away and disrupts relationship. |

### T3.11.3  ·  Tier T3

> What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with relational capacity reveal about the nature of this characteristic?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The pattern reveals that fear is fundamentally a relational characteristic — its presence and direction determine the quality of the person's relationships. Fear of God (M01-A) is the ground of trust, justice, and genuine care in relationships. Social fear (M01-B-VCG-04) is the systematic distorter of relationship — it substitutes management of others' opinions for genuine other-care. The cluster confirms that the question "what does this person fear?" is the most revealing question about the quality of their relational life. Those who fear God relate authentically, justly, and generously; those who fear human opinion relate inauthentically, self-protectively, and with managed surfaces. |

### T3.2.1  ·  Tier T3

> Does this characteristic engage the cognitive faculty — knowing, understanding, discerning — and if so, how?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The cognitive faculty is engaged across M01 in two opposed directions: M01-A **enables** cognition (fear-of-God as the root of knowledge), while M01-B, D, and F (in different degrees) **disrupt or distort** cognition. This is a structural finding: ordered fear (M01-A) is epistemologically constitutive; disordered fear (M01-D, M01-B's paralysing dimension) is epistemologically destructive. |
| M01-A | finding | M01-A is the most cognitively engaged sub-group in the cluster. Reverential fear is the **root of knowing**: Pro 1:7 (anchor A-VCG-02: "the foundational inner disposition from which all knowledge begins"); Psa 111:10 ("fear of the Lord is the foundational inner disposition from which wisdom begins — constitutive of understanding"); Job 28:28 ("fear of the Lord is identified as wisdom itself"). Fear of God is not merely a precondition for knowledge but is identified as the inner posture that constitutes genuine understanding. It is epistemologically foundational. |
| M01-B | finding | M01-B's acute fear engages cognition in a disruptive mode: 1Sa 17:11 (Saul and all Israel "dismayed and deeply afraid — Goliath's words produce a two-layered inner impact: shock that **disorganises thought** and fear that disables action"); Mar 9:6 ("Peter's inability to know what to say at the transfiguration is explained by the terror gripping the disciples — the fear so overwhelms their inner faculties that thought and speech are disabled"). |
| M01-D | finding | M01-D dismay is a cognitive-shutdown characteristic: Isa 21:3 (cannot see — cognitive-perceptive shutdown); Job 32:15 (friends "dismayed into complete speechlessness — the rational and verbal faculties entirely shut down"); Dan 7:28 (dismay "works through Daniel's thoughts" but Daniel resolves to keep the matter inward — a last cognitive act before the colour changes). |
| M01-F | finding | M01-F anticipatory dread is the cognitively richest disordered sub-group. De.a.gah (H1674) as anxiety carries a cognitive-ruminating quality (Borkovec's verbal-linguistic worry model is directly applicable — see T7.3). 2Cor 12:20 (anchor F-VCG-05: "Paul's fear is an anticipatory dread rooted in **thought** about what he may find — engaging the mind with anxious expectation"). The cognitive engagement is anticipatory and future-oriented. |

### T3.2.2  ·  Tier T3

> Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair cognition in the person?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The pattern: M01-A enables/deepens cognition; M01-D impairs it most severely; M01-F distorts it toward anxious anticipation; M01-B impairs it acutely in moments of overwhelming encounter; M01-G suppresses it volitionally. The ordered fear (M01-A) and the disordered fears (B-severe, D, F, G) are cognitively opposed. |
| M01-A | finding | M01-A **enables and deepens** cognition. Pro 2:5 (fear as "an inner understanding arrived at through diligent pursuit — not merely an emotion but a formed insight"); Pro 1:29 (rejecting fear is "an act of the will — the inner choice to hate knowledge and refuse reverence" — absence of fear closes cognition). Fear-of-God is presented as cognitively constitutive: the person who fears God genuinely understands; the person who does not lacks foundational knowing. |
| M01-B | finding | M01-B and M01-D **impair** cognition. Mar 9:6 (M01-B: fear disabling thought and speech at the Transfiguration); Isa 21:3 (M01-D: dismay shutting down perception and sight). M01-D's D-VCG-03 (Dan 5:6; 5:10) shows the cognitive origin of dismay (thoughts alarmed) and its cognitive consequence (the system shut down). |
| M01-D | finding | M01-B and M01-D **impair** cognition. Mar 9:6 (M01-B: fear disabling thought and speech at the Transfiguration); Isa 21:3 (M01-D: dismay shutting down perception and sight). M01-D's D-VCG-03 (Dan 5:6; 5:10) shows the cognitive origin of dismay (thoughts alarmed) and its cognitive consequence (the system shut down). |
| M01-F | finding | M01-F **distorts** cognition by fixating it on anticipated negative futures. De.a.gah (H1674) is a worry-based cognitive engagement that prevents the mind from resting on present reality. It "bypasses" present truth by substituting anticipated threat. |
| M01-G | finding | M01-G timidity **impairs** cognitive action: Mat 25:25 (servant's failure to think productively about how to use the talent — fear suppresses the cognition that would enable faithful investment). |

### T3.2.3  ·  Tier T3

> What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with cognition reveal about the nature of this characteristic?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The pattern reveals that fear has a fundamental cognitive dimension: it either opens or closes the person's capacity for genuine knowing. Ordered fear of God opens — it is the epistemological root. Disordered fear closes — it either shuts down (M01-D), distorts (M01-F), or suppresses (M01-G) the cognitive faculty. This confirms that fear is not merely an affective experience but a cognitive-orienting characteristic: what the person fears determines what they can genuinely know and what they will fail to see. |

### T3.3.1  ·  Tier T3

> Does this characteristic engage the memory faculty — the holding and retrieving of inner-being reality across time — and if so, how?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | Memory is engaged across M01 in three distinct modes: (1) **formative** — fear of God is built by cumulative memory of his acts (M01-A); (2) **corrective** — memory of past divine deliverance counters present acute fear (M01-B); (3) **triggering** — memory of past fear retrieves that fear in the present (M01-F-VCG-02). Memory is not a dominant faculty engagement in M01 but it is consistently present as a mediating element. |
| M01-A | finding | M01-A engages memory in its formation: Deu 31:12-13 (public Torah-reading produces fear in children who have not yet heard — fear is formed through cumulative hearing and memory of God's word); 1Sa 12:24 ("fear of the Lord is commanded as an all-heart devotion **grounded in memory of God's great deeds**" — memory grounds reverential fear); 2Ki 17:38 ("correct inner fear is inseparable from **memory and loyalty**; forsaking the covenant opens the heart to misplaced reverence"). |
| M01-B | finding | M01-B engages memory as a preventive or corrective: Deu 7:18 ("Israel is told not to be afraid of the nations they must displace — the inward dread of numerous enemies is to be **replaced by memory of what God did to Pharaoh**, grounding courage in historical experience"); Isa 33:18 (M01-C-VCG-04: "the heart will **muse on the past terror** after the enemy is gone — the inner faculty of reflection revisits the dread once it has passed"). Memory of God's past acts counters present fear. |
| M01-F | finding | M01-F engages memory in a specific way: Job 21:6 (M01-E-VCG-05: "shuddering takes hold of Job's flesh the **moment memory brings dismay**" — memory triggering somatic fear response); Deu 28:60 (M01-F-VCG-02: "Israel's former terror of Egypt's diseases is recalled — God will bring back the very afflictions they once dreaded, **exploiting that deep-seated fear**" — memory as the site of embedded anticipatory dread). |

### T3.3.2  ·  Tier T3

> Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair memory in the person?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The pattern: ordered fear (M01-A) deepens and structures memory around God's acts; disordered fear (M01-D, M01-F) impairs or distorts memory. This parallels the cognitive faculty pattern. |
| M01-A | finding | M01-A **deepens** memory by grounding it in God's acts. The repeated pattern of fear arising from witnessing God's deeds (Exo 14:31; Hag 1:12) and fear being formed through cumulative hearing of what God has done (Deu 31:12-13) confirms that reverential fear deepens the person's memory of divine reality. |
| M01-D | finding | M01-D dismay **impairs** memory through cognitive shutdown: Isa 21:3 (dismay shuts down perception; by extension, the capacity to retrieve relevant memories is also impaired). M01-F **distorts** memory by retrieving embedded fears (Deu 28:60: embedded fears being retriggered as covenant curse). |
| M01-F | finding | M01-D dismay **impairs** memory through cognitive shutdown: Isa 21:3 (dismay shuts down perception; by extension, the capacity to retrieve relevant memories is also impaired). M01-F **distorts** memory by retrieving embedded fears (Deu 28:60: embedded fears being retriggered as covenant curse). |

### T3.3.3  ·  Tier T3

> What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with memory reveal about the nature of this characteristic?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | Fear's engagement with memory reveals that it is a temporally situated characteristic: reverential fear is grounded in the remembered past (God's acts in history) and oriented toward the anticipated future (M01-F). The ordered form roots the person in historical memory of divine faithfulness; the disordered form either impairs present-moment awareness or retrieves embedded past fears. Memory is one of the pathways through which fear is both formed and deformed. |

### T3.4.1  ·  Tier T3

> Does this characteristic engage the affective faculty — feeling and emotional experience — and if so, how?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The affective faculty is the primary dimension of M01 across all sub-groups. Fear is constitutively affective. The affective range across the cluster is wide: from reverent delight (M01-A, Psa 2:11; Heb 12:28) through acute alarm (M01-B) to overwhelming anguish (M01-D, F) to horror (M01-C). The characteristic's affective diversity reflects the cluster's seven-sub-group structure. |
| M01-A | finding | M01-A engages the affective faculty in a complex way. Reverential fear itself is an affective state — it is a felt orientation, not merely a cognitive assessment. But M01-A shows the affect paired with joy: Psa 2:11 ("fear of the Lord coexists with joy, shaping worship as a **reverent, trembling delight** rather than casual confidence"); Heb 12:28 (fear and awe as "the fitting inner disposition for approaching God in worship, prompted by gratitude"). Fear-as-reverence is an affective state that is not mutually exclusive with positive affect. **[Folded from wa_session_b_findings.id=38; finding_id=DIM-11-001; registry=awe]** Awe spans both Affective/Emotional and Spiritual/God-ward dimensions. God-ward groups (1682-001, 1682-003, 703-002, 703-003) show that the deepest fear/awe content is S… |
| M01-B | finding | M01-B engages the affective faculty centrally — acute fear is by definition an intense affective experience. The range includes: alarm (Gen 32:7), awe-mingled-dread (Mar 4:41), social anxiety (Joh 7:13), and relief-producing fear (Psa 105:38: Egypt's terror "produced gladness at their departure"). Mat 28:8 (women departing "holding **fear and great joy simultaneously**") is the most vivid example of complex affective coexistence. |
| M01-D | finding | M01-D engages the affective faculty through the dismay-experience: Psa 6:3 (the psalmist's soul "greatly dismayed — profound turmoil driving the anguished cry to God"). The affective content is anguish, horror, and internal upheaval. |
| M01-F | finding | M01-F's affective content is sustained apprehension: de.a.gah (H1674) anxiety as a weighing-down burden on the heart (Pro 12:25); the anticipatory dread of M01-F-VCG-03 as unrelenting anguish that "distorts the experience of time" (Deu 28:67). |

### T3.4.2  ·  Tier T3

> Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair affect in the person?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The pattern: ordered fear (M01-A) deepens and integrates affect; disordered fear (M01-B extreme, C, D, F) overwhelms, displaces, or colonises affect. The cluster's affective dimension confirms the programme's broader finding that ordered inner characteristics enrich the inner life while disordered ones impoverish it. |
| M01-A | finding | M01-A **deepens** affect by integrating fear with joy, delight, and confidence. Psa 2:11 (trembling delight), Pro 14:26 (fear as "foundation of strong confidence, not anxiety"), Neh 1:11 (fearing God's name as "something the servants delight in — a willing, joyful inner devotion rather than reluctant dread"). Reverential fear does not flatten the affective life but deepens and integrates it. |
| M01-B | finding | M01-B acute fear, M01-C terror, and M01-D dismay **overwhelm** affect in their extreme forms. The sheer intensity of the experience monopolises the inner life: Dan 5:6 (dismay striking so violently that color changes and limbs fail — all other affect is displaced). Mat 28:8 (fear and joy coexisting) is the exception rather than the rule in the acute register. |
| M01-C | finding | M01-B acute fear, M01-C terror, and M01-D dismay **overwhelm** affect in their extreme forms. The sheer intensity of the experience monopolises the inner life: Dan 5:6 (dismay striking so violently that color changes and limbs fail — all other affect is displaced). Mat 28:8 (fear and joy coexisting) is the exception rather than the rule in the acute register. |
| M01-D | finding | M01-B acute fear, M01-C terror, and M01-D dismay **overwhelm** affect in their extreme forms. The sheer intensity of the experience monopolises the inner life: Dan 5:6 (dismay striking so violently that color changes and limbs fail — all other affect is displaced). Mat 28:8 (fear and joy coexisting) is the exception rather than the rule in the acute register. |
| M01-F | finding | M01-F **impairs** the affective range by colonising it: Eze 12:18-19 (anxiety saturating every moment of eating and drinking — the affective space available for other emotions is occupied by persistent dread). Heb 2:15 (fear of death holding people in "lifelong inner slavery" — the affect of enslaved dread displacing other affective engagement). |

### T3.4.3  ·  Tier T3

> What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with affect reveal about the nature of this characteristic?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The pattern reveals that fear is the inner-being characteristic with the widest natural affective range in the programme's cluster evidence: from reverent delight (M01-A) to overwhelming horror (M01-C, D). This range is not arbitrary but reflects the cluster's structural axis: the object and direction of fear determines its affective quality. Ordered fear directed toward God is integrated with joy and confidence; disordered fear directed toward threat produces only negative affective experience. The characteristic's affective range is object-determined. |

### T3.5.1  ·  Tier T3

> Does this characteristic engage the creative faculty — imagination and the capacity to originate — and if so, how?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The creative/imaginative faculty is most clearly engaged in M01-B-VCG-05 (fear generating elaborate negative interpretations) and M01-F (anticipatory dread as imagined futures). The pattern suggests that disordered fear activates the imagination in its negative projection mode — fear drives the person to imagine worst-case scenarios. Ordered fear (M01-A) does not appear to engage the creative faculty distinctively. |
| M01-A | silent | M01-A reverential fear does not have explicit engagement with the creative faculty in the verse evidence. The formation of the fear through hearing God's word and witnessing his acts is receptive rather than creative. |
| M01-B | finding | M01-B engages the imagination in M01-B-VCG-05 (self-preservation fear): Gen 43:18 ("the men feel afraid on being brought into Joseph's house, **immediately imagining the worst** — enslavement and seizure; the inner fear generates an elaborate, **anxiety-driven interpretation of events**"). Fear activates the imaginative faculty to project negative scenarios from partial evidence. |
| M01-F | finding | M01-F is the most imagination-engaged sub-group. Anticipatory dread by definition involves imagining a feared future: 2Cor 12:20 (Paul's fear "rooted in thought about what he may find" — imaginative projection of possible disorder before the visit); Job 3:25 (Job's dreaded thing "already sat within him as an anticipated fear" — the feared scenario was held in the imagination before it materialised). De.a.gah as worry is fundamentally imaginative in structure. |

### T3.5.2  ·  Tier T3

> Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair creativity in the person?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | Fear's engagement with the creative faculty is primarily distorting in the disordered sub-groups: the imagination is captured by anticipated threat (M01-F) or negative scenario-construction (M01-B-VCG-05). Ordered fear (M01-A) does not appear to engage or impair creativity. |
| M01-A | silent | No evidence that M01-A either enables or impairs creativity distinctively. |
| M01-B | finding | Disordered fear (M01-B's self-preservation register, M01-F) **distorts** the creative faculty by channelling imagination toward negative projection rather than constructive origination. The imagination is active but in a constrained, threat-oriented mode. |
| M01-F | finding | Disordered fear (M01-B's self-preservation register, M01-F) **distorts** the creative faculty by channelling imagination toward negative projection rather than constructive origination. The imagination is active but in a constrained, threat-oriented mode. |

### T3.5.3  ·  Tier T3

> What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with creativity reveal about the nature of this characteristic?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The pattern reveals that disordered fear captures the imagination for negative projection, while ordered fear does not distinctively engage the creative faculty. Fear is not a creative-enabling characteristic but a creative-channelling one: in its disordered forms it channels imagination toward threat-scenarios. This is consistent with the science extract's Borkovec worry-model (verbal-linguistic, future-oriented, repetitive cognitive engagement). |

### T3.6.1  ·  Tier T3

> Does this characteristic engage the volitional faculty — the capacity to choose — and if so, how?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The volitional faculty is the most consistently engaged inner faculty across all M01 sub-groups. Fear governs, channels, overrides, paralyses, or dissolves the will across every sub-group. The cluster's unifying feature is volitional impact: all seven sub-groups describe how fear determines what the person does or fails to do. The volitional faculty is M01's primary operating theatre. |
| M01-A | finding | M01-A engages the volitional faculty pervasively. Reverential fear governs the will's choices across all ethical and covenant contexts: Lev 19:14 (fear preventing the will from exploiting the vulnerable — the will restrained by the inner reverential disposition); Deu 6:24 (fear as the inner posture "that produces obedience" — directly governing the will); Pro 16:6 ("fear of the Lord is an operative inner force that **turns the person away from evil**, functioning as the moral agent that drives ethical avoidance"). The will is fear-of-God's primary operating theatre. |
| M01-B | finding | M01-B engages the volitional faculty through will-governance: Gen 32:7 (fear "immediately drives strategic action" — the will is channelled by fear); 1Sa 17:24 (all men of Israel flee "without deliberation" — fear overrides the deliberative will); Joh 19:38 (Joseph's discipleship was hidden because "fear of the Jews **governed** his public behavior"). Fear in M01-B systematically governs or overrides the will. |
| M01-C | finding | M01-C engages the volitional faculty by paralyzing or redirecting it: Gen 35:5 (terror "paralyzing the will to pursue Jacob's sons"); Est 9:3 (dread of Mordecai "redirected the will of those in authority" — the will of officials redirected by fear of Jewish power); Deu 11:25 (dread of Israel "placed in enemies' hearts so no one can withstand them" — the will to resist neutralized by divinely-imposed dread). |
| M01-D | finding | M01-D engages the volitional faculty by dissolving it: Isa 21:3 (dismay so complete that the prophet cannot see — the will to perceive has collapsed); Eze 7:27 ("dismay so overwhelms the people that **their hands are paralyzed**" — the will to act physically disabled); Gen 45:3 (brothers "cannot answer" — the will to speak is shut down). |
| M01-G | finding | M01-G is definitionally volitional: timidity is a failure of the will to act faithfully under pressure. Mat 25:25 (the will choosing passive self-preservation over faithful risk); Joh 14:27 (the heart commanded not to "yield to that fearful recoiling" — the will choosing to resist or surrender to timidity); Rev 21:8 (the will choosing apostasy under sustained threat). |

### T3.6.2  ·  Tier T3

> Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair volition in the person — including its three aspects: capacity, interaction with other characteristics, and the constraints under which it operates?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The pattern: M01-A enables/deepens volition (governance toward right action); M01-B and C bypass or override volition (urgency overwhelming deliberation); M01-D dissolves volition (hands paralyzed, speech gone); M01-G impairs volition (misdirection toward passivity). Ordered fear enriches volitional life; disordered fear degrades it. |
| M01-A | finding | M01-A **enables and deepens** volition by aligning it with right action. Fear of God does not suppress the will but governs it toward wisdom, ethics, and covenant faithfulness. Pro 14:16 ("the wise person's reverential caution causes him to turn from evil — the inner quality is a wary, fear-informed prudence that **restrains reckless action**"). This is volition enabled and governed, not suppressed. |
| M01-B | finding | M01-B's acute fear and M01-C's terror **bypass** or **override** volition in many instances: 1Sa 17:24 (flight "without deliberation" — the will bypassed); Gen 35:5 (terror paralyzing the will — bypassed). But in some B instances, fear governs without bypassing: Mat 14:5 (Herod's social fear "restrained his will from executing John" — fear governing the will without bypassing it). |
| M01-C | finding | M01-B's acute fear and M01-C's terror **bypass** or **override** volition in many instances: 1Sa 17:24 (flight "without deliberation" — the will bypassed); Gen 35:5 (terror paralyzing the will — bypassed). But in some B instances, fear governs without bypassing: Mat 14:5 (Herod's social fear "restrained his will from executing John" — fear governing the will without bypassing it). |
| M01-D | finding | M01-D dismay **impairs and dissolves** volition: Eze 7:27 (hands paralyzed — volitional capacity physically disabled); Job 32:15 (friends speechless — the will to speak dissolved). Dismay is the sub-group most destructive of the volitional faculty. |
| M01-G | finding | M01-G timidity **impairs** volition by channelling it toward passive self-preservation. The will is not absent but misdirected — toward burying, hiding, and shrinking rather than action. |

### T3.6.3  ·  Tier T3

> What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with volition reveal about the nature of this characteristic?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The pattern reveals that fear is fundamentally a volitional characteristic: its defining effect in every sub-group is on what the person chooses or fails to choose. This is the cluster's most structurally significant finding for the inner-faculties tier. Fear is not merely felt — it determines action. The ordered form (M01-A) makes the will's choices wise and ethical; the disordered forms (M01-B-D, F, G) suppress, bypass, misdirect, or dissolve those choices. The characteristic cannot be understood apart from its volitional impact. |

### T3.7.1  ·  Tier T3

> Does this characteristic engage the agency faculty — the capacity to act, initiate, and make happen — and if so, how?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The agency faculty is: **enabled** by M01-A (courage to act against tyranny, prayer in the face of disaster, ethical restraint as a form of moral agency); **conditionally engaged** by M01-B (enabling or disabling depending on the fear-object and intensity); **disabled** by M01-C, D (paralysis, hands immobilized, flight); and **suppressed** by M01-G (passive self-preservation rather than initiative). The pattern mirrors the volitional finding: ordered fear enables agency; disordered fear impairs or suppresses it. |
| M01-A | finding | M01-A **enables** agency by generating ethical and covenant-faithful action: Exo 1:17 (the midwives' fear of God "functions as an inner moral allegiance that overrides the king's command — it is a reverent loyalty to God that controls the will even under coercive royal authority" — agency enabled against tyranny by fear of God); Jer 26:19 (Hezekiah "feared the Lord and entreated him, and disaster was averted — the inner reverence is shown to be an **active posture that turned toward God in prayer**, producing a concrete historical outcome"). Fear-of-God is an agency-enabling characteristic. |
| M01-B | finding | M01-B's relationship to agency is complex: acute fear can either enable agency (Gen 32:7: Jacob's fear immediately drives strategic action — splitting the camp, sending gifts ahead) or disable it (1Sa 17:24: all men of Israel flee without deliberation). The object and intensity of the fear determines whether it enables or disables agency. |
| M01-C | finding | M01-C and D primarily **impair or disable** agency: Gen 35:5 (terror paralyzing the will to pursue), Eze 7:27 (hands paralyzed — agency physically disabled), Jer 46:5 (terror causing Egypt's warriors to "abandon their posts and flee — inner resolve shattered by overwhelming dread"). |
| M01-D | finding | M01-C and D primarily **impair or disable** agency: Gen 35:5 (terror paralyzing the will to pursue), Eze 7:27 (hands paralyzed — agency physically disabled), Jer 46:5 (terror causing Egypt's warriors to "abandon their posts and flee — inner resolve shattered by overwhelming dread"). |
| M01-G | finding | M01-G timidity **suppresses** agency: Mat 25:25 (burying the talent instead of investing — the action not taken); Luk 19:21 (fear of the severe master producing inaction). Timidity is the failure of the agency-courage that would take faithful action. |

### T3.7.2  ·  Tier T3

> Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair agency in the person?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | Ordered fear enables agency; disordered fear suppresses or destroys it. The pattern is consistent across all sub-groups. |
| M01-A | finding | M01-A **enables and deepens** agency. The ethical courage of the midwives (Exo 1:17), Nehemiah's wall-building despite threats (Neh 4:14; 6:9-14), and Job's sustained integrity despite suffering (Job 1:8; 2:3) all show fear of God enabling courageous, initiative-taking action against opposition. |
| M01-C | finding | M01-C and D **bypass and impair** agency. Terror-as-force bypasses the person's deliberative agency entirely (God's terror produces immediate paralysis, Gen 35:5). Dismay impairs agency by dissolving the physical and volitional capacity to act (Eze 7:27; Job 32:15). |
| M01-D | finding | M01-C and D **bypass and impair** agency. Terror-as-force bypasses the person's deliberative agency entirely (God's terror produces immediate paralysis, Gen 35:5). Dismay impairs agency by dissolving the physical and volitional capacity to act (Eze 7:27; Job 32:15). |
| M01-G | finding | M01-G **suppresses** agency by channelling it toward passive self-preservation rather than initiative. |

### T3.7.3  ·  Tier T3

> What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with agency reveal about the nature of this characteristic?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The pattern confirms that fear is an agency-shaping characteristic at its core: what the person fears determines what they are willing to do and what they are too afraid to do. Ordered fear (M01-A) produces the most courageous agency in the cluster — the midwives defy Pharaoh, Nehemiah builds in the face of death threats. Disordered fear produces the most paralysed or suppressed agency (M01-D hands paralysed; M01-G burying the talent). The inverse relationship between ordered fear of God and suppression of human-threat agency is a significant structural finding: the more a person genuinely fears God, the less they fear human opposition (Deu 7:21; 1Ch 22:13; Neh 4:14). |

### T3.8.1  ·  Tier T3

> Does this characteristic engage the moral evaluation faculty — the capacity to assess against a standard of right, wrong, good, and true — and if so, how?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The moral evaluation faculty is: **enabled and deepened** by M01-A (fear of God as the interior moral standard); **bypassed** by M01-B's social fear (crowd opinion overriding moral judgment); **impaired** by M01-G timidity (cowardly failure of moral discernment under pressure). Ordered fear activates and grounds moral evaluation; disordered fear bypasses or suppresses it. |
| M01-A | finding | M01-A is the most morally evaluative sub-group in the cluster. Fear of God provides the interior moral standard against which the person's conduct is assessed in the absence of external accountability: Lev 19:14 (fear as the moral evaluator operating where "no human court can see"); Neh 5:9 (fear of God as "the inner ethical standard that should have restrained the leaders from oppressing their own people"); 2Ch 19:9 (judicial conduct governed by fear of the Lord "paired explicitly with faithfulness and whole-heartedness"). The moral evaluation faculty is the primary channel through which M01-A operates in practical contexts. |
| M01-A | finding | M01-A-VCG-05 (reorientation of fear) engages moral evaluation directly: the person must morally assess what they are fearing and judge whether the object is appropriate (God) or not (crowds, idols, human power). Isa 8:12-13 (the prophet commanded not to adopt the crowd's fear-object — a moral assessment of fear's direction is required). |
| M01-B | finding | M01-B's social fear (B-VCG-04) **bypasses** moral evaluation: Gal 2:12 (Peter's social fear driving withdrawal "against conviction" — the person's own moral assessment is overridden by fear-of-crowd-opinion); 1Sa 15:24 (Saul confesses that "fear of the people was the inner motive behind his disobedience — human social dread displaced his fear of God and drove him to comply with the crowd" — moral evaluation suppressed by social fear). |
| M01-G | finding | M01-G timidity **impairs** moral evaluation: Rev 21:8 (cowardice listed alongside idolatry and murder — timidity is a moral failure); Mat 25:25 (the servant's misjudgment of the master's character drives the wrong decision — moral evaluation distorted by fear). |

### T3.8.2  ·  Tier T3

> Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair moral evaluation in the person?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The pattern is the clearest moral-evaluation finding in the cluster: M01-A reverential fear is the foundation of interior moral evaluation; social fear (M01-B-VCG-04) and timidity (M01-G) are the systematic bypasses of it. |
| M01-A | finding | M01-A **enables and deepens** moral evaluation by providing an interior standard (fear of God as inner ethical judge, Lev 19:14; Neh 5:15). The person who fears God has an interior moral referee that continues to operate even when external consequences are removed. |
| M01-B | finding | M01-B's social fear and M01-G timidity **bypass and impair** moral evaluation. Social fear substitutes crowd opinion for moral principle (Gal 2:12; 1Sa 15:24). Timidity substitutes self-preservation for moral faithfulness (Mat 25:25; Rev 21:8). |
| M01-G | finding | M01-B's social fear and M01-G timidity **bypass and impair** moral evaluation. Social fear substitutes crowd opinion for moral principle (Gal 2:12; 1Sa 15:24). Timidity substitutes self-preservation for moral faithfulness (Mat 25:25; Rev 21:8). |

### T3.8.3  ·  Tier T3

> What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with moral evaluation reveal about the nature of this characteristic?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The pattern reveals that fear-of-God is the constitutive interior moral faculty in Scripture's account of the human person. Psa 36:1 (absence of fear as "fundamental moral blindness"), Rom 3:18 (absence of fear as defining godless humanity's moral condition), and the Lev 19 corpus (fear as the operative moral restraint where no court sees) all confirm that ordered fear is not merely adjacent to morality but is its interior ground. This is a significant cluster-level finding for the programme's governing question: the inner moral faculty is, at its root, fear-of-God. |

### T3.9.1  ·  Tier T3

> Does this characteristic engage the conscience — the acute inner witness of sin, guilt, and conviction — and if so, how?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The conscience is engaged across M01 in three modes: (1) **activated** by reverential fear of God (M01-A: fear as interior moral witness); (2) **suppressed** by social fear displacing it (M01-B-VCG-04: crowd-fear overriding conscience); (3) **haunted** by anticipatory judgment-dread (M01-F: the conscience as the site of anticipated divine judgment). |
| M01-A | finding | M01-A engages conscience through fear's role as interior moral restraint: Lev 19:14 (fear of God operating as conscience in situations of power over the vulnerable — an interior witness that prevents exploitation); Neh 5:9; 5:15 (fear of God operating as Nehemiah's interior restraint against the abuse of authority — functioning as conscience before any external witness speaks). The 2Cor 5:11 material (M01-A-VCG-04: "knowing the fear of the Lord shapes the will toward persuasion of others — a motivating inner awareness of divine accountability that **can be known by conscience**") explicitly names conscience alongside fear. |
| M01-B | finding | M01-B engages conscience through the social-fear corpus: 1Sa 15:24 (Saul confesses that social fear displaced his conscience — the fear of people overrode the fear of God that should have governed); 2Sa 1:14 (David's rebuke frames the absence of fear as a moral failure — "the messenger lacked the reverential dread that should have prevented him from touching God's anointed, exposing a void in **his inner conscience**"). |
| M01-F | finding | M01-F-VCG-04 engages conscience through anticipatory guilt: Act 24:25 (Felix became alarmed as Paul reasoned about righteousness, self-control, and coming judgment — "moral and eschatological argument penetrated his inner being and produced a **frightened, avoidant response**" — conscience stirred by fear of judgment producing avoidance rather than repentance). Job 15:21 (M01-B-VCG-05: "the wicked man hears dreadful sounds in his ears even in prosperity — dread as an **internal auditory experience haunting the conscience** and anticipating destruction"). |

### T3.9.2  ·  Tier T3

> Does this characteristic enable, deepen, bypass, or impair conscience in the person?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The conscience is enabled by M01-A, bypassed by M01-B's social fear register, and haunted but not necessarily responsive in M01-F's judgment-anticipation material. Ordered fear of God is the ground of an active, functioning conscience; social fear (M01-B-VCG-04) is one of its primary suppressors. |
| M01-A | finding | M01-A **enables and deepens** conscience. Fear of God creates the interior moral sensitivity (Psa 36:1: its absence produces moral blindness). The more clearly evidenced direction: reverential fear opens and sustains conscience; its absence or displacement closes it. |
| M01-B | finding | Social fear (M01-B-VCG-04) **bypasses** conscience: Gal 2:12 (Peter's social fear overriding his own convictions — the conscience is there but overridden). |
| M01-F | finding | Anticipatory judgment-dread (M01-F-VCG-04) **engages** conscience in its avoidant mode: Act 24:25 (Felix alarmed but avoidant — conscience stirred but not yielded to). Heb 10:27 (fearful expectation of judgment lodged in the mind) shows conscience as the site of anticipated divine assessment. |

### T3.9.3  ·  Tier T3

> What does the pattern of engagement or non-engagement with conscience reveal about the nature of this characteristic?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The pattern confirms a structural relationship between fear of God and conscience: fear-of-God is the constitutive ground of a functioning conscience (Psa 36:1; Lev 19:14). Social fear is its primary competitor — when the person fears the crowd more than God, the conscience is suppressed. This structural relationship means that the diagnostic of a person's inner life (is the conscience functioning or suppressed?) is closely tied to whether they fear God or fear human opinion. The cluster makes this causal relationship explicit at multiple points. |

### T4.1.1  ·  Tier T4

> Does the verse evidence show this characteristic operating from God toward the human person — and if so, how?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | God operates toward the human person across M01 in at least five distinct ways: commanding fear (M01-A), implanting it (M01-A, Jer 32:40), deploying it as weapon against enemies (M01-C), imposing it as judicial instrument against rebels (M01-D), and imposing covenantal-curse dread on the unfaithful (M01-F). God is uniquely active across the entire cluster — more so than in most other programme clusters examined to date. |
| M01-A | finding | M01-A shows God operating toward the human person by: (1) **commanding** fear — Deu 6:13; 10:20; Ecc 12:13 (God directly requiring the reverential posture); (2) **implanting** it — Jer 32:40 (God pledging to place fear directly in the hearts of his people as a permanent disposition); (3) **forming** it through encounter — Deu 4:10 (God intending the Horeb encounter to produce lasting fear); (4) **rewarding** it — Exo 1:21 (God rewarding the midwives' fear-of-God-based disobedience with families). |
| M01-B | finding | M01-B shows God operating toward the human person through: (1) **angelic appearances** producing fear (Luk 1:12-13; Luk 2:9-10); (2) **Jesus's acts** producing fear (Mar 4:41; Act 5:5-11); (3) **divine commands to release fear** (Isa 43:1 anchor B-VCG-06; "do not fear" as God speaking directly to the person's fear-state); (4) **theophanic encounters** (Exo 19:16 — God's descent at Sinai producing involuntary trembling). **[Folded from wa_session_b_findings.id=68; finding_id=DIM-61-002; registry=fear]** ya.re (H3372G) groups add the divine 'Fear not' command (298-001) as a structuring element — showing the divine address to inner fear as a distinct inner-being category. The reassurance pattern (divine declaration of presence + commanded displacement of fear) is significant for understandin… |
| M01-C | finding | M01-C shows God deploying terror toward enemy peoples: Exo 23:27 (anchor C-VCG-01: "God's terror is sent as an advance weapon" — God actively deploying terror into enemy inner lives); Jer 32:40 / Deu 11:25 (God placing dread of Israel in surrounding nations). |
| M01-D | finding | M01-D shows God producing dismay as judicial action: Psa 2:5 (God's wrath producing dismay in rebel kings); Jer 49:37 (anchor D-VCG-02: "God will terrify Elam before their enemies, making dismay the inner condition through which he breaks their will — his fierce anger is the divine source"). |
| M01-F | finding | M01-F-VCG-03 shows God imposing covenantal-curse dread: Deu 28:66-67 (anchor: "continual dread without assurance of life is a covenantal curse" — God imposing the chronic dread as a covenant consequence of unfaithfulness). |

### T4.1.2  ·  Tier T4

> What does the evidence reveal about the basis on which God extends this characteristic — is it conditional, unconditional, covenantal, or responsive?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The basis of God's operation across M01 is primarily **covenantal and responsive**: God extends reverential fear-formation to covenant members (M01-A), deploys terror against covenant enemies (M01-C), and imposes dread as covenant-curse on the unfaithful (M01-F). The characteristic's operation from God toward the human person is consistently embedded in the covenant structure. |
| M01-A | finding | M01-A shows a primarily **covenantal** basis: the fear God implants (Jer 32:40) is a covenant promise; the fear God commands is grounded in the covenant relationship (Deu 6:13-14; Mal 2:5). The Psa 25:14 material (covenant intimacy offered to those who fear) suggests a **responsive** dimension — God's covenant friendship responds to the human person's reverential posture. |
| M01-C | finding | M01-C and D show a **conditional-responsive** basis: God deploys terror against Israel's enemies in response to their opposition to his covenantal purposes (Exo 23:27; Deu 11:25); he dismays rebels in response to their defiance (Psa 2:5; Jer 49:37). The basis is conditional on the enemies' opposition. |
| M01-D | finding | M01-C and D show a **conditional-responsive** basis: God deploys terror against Israel's enemies in response to their opposition to his covenantal purposes (Exo 23:27; Deu 11:25); he dismays rebels in response to their defiance (Psa 2:5; Jer 49:37). The basis is conditional on the enemies' opposition. |
| M01-F | finding | M01-F-VCG-03 (covenantal curse-dread) is explicitly **conditional** on covenant violation: Deu 28:66-67 is the direct consequence of failing to obey the terms of the covenant. |

### T4.1.3  ·  Tier T4

> What does God's extension of this characteristic reveal about his disposition toward the human person?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | God's disposition toward the human person as revealed through M01 is: (1) intimately relational and care-ful toward those who fear him; (2) actively formative — working to produce the right inner orientation; (3) sovereignly just — deploying fear as an instrument of historical governance. The cluster reveals God as both the object of human fear and the sovereign producer of it. |
| M01-A | finding | God's command to fear him, combined with his pledge to implant that fear (Jer 32:40), reveals a disposition of **covenant commitment and pastoral care**: God is not indifferent to whether the human person has the right inner orientation — he actively works to produce it. Psa 25:14 (offering covenant friendship to those who fear him) reveals God's disposition as intimate and relational — the fear-posture opens access to God's friendship. |
| M01-B | finding | God's repeated "do not fear" commands in M01-B-VCG-06 (Isa 43:1 anchor: "you are mine" as the ground for releasing fear) reveal a disposition of **possessive care and relational nearness**: God addresses the frightened person directly, names himself as their ground of security, and commands the release of fear from a position of personal commitment. |
| M01-C | finding | God's deployment of terror against enemies (M01-C-VCG-01) and imposition of dismay as judgment (M01-D-VCG-02) reveals his disposition as **sovereignly just**: he uses fear as an instrument of historical governance, not arbitrarily but in response to opposition to his covenantal purposes. |
| M01-D | finding | God's deployment of terror against enemies (M01-C-VCG-01) and imposition of dismay as judgment (M01-D-VCG-02) reveals his disposition as **sovereignly just**: he uses fear as an instrument of historical governance, not arbitrarily but in response to opposition to his covenantal purposes. |

### T4.1.4  ·  Tier T4

> If the evidence is silent on God-to-human operation, note this explicitly.

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| M01-G | silent | M01-G timidity does not evidence direct God-to-human operation of the characteristic. God's operation toward M01-G is the negative: 2Ti 1:7 establishes what God has not given (timidity), and by implication what God has given (power, love, self-control). The absence of God's gift of timidity is the finding, not a positive extension. |

### T4.2.1  ·  Tier T4

> Does the verse evidence show this characteristic operating in the human person's movement toward God — in seeking, supplication, worship, or covenant — and if so, how?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The human-to-God movement across M01 is most extensively documented in M01-A (worship, prayer, covenant, vow) and M01-E-VCG-02 (trembling-at-word as the posture of receptive covenant engagement). M01-B shows fear functioning as a gateway to worship when the fear is triggered by encounter with divine power. |
| M01-A | finding | M01-A extensively documents the human person moving toward God in reverential fear: (1) **worship** — Psa 5:7 (fear drawing the psalmist into the temple — "reverence for who God is motivates his approach to the temple and shapes his posture of bowing down"); Heb 12:28 (fear and awe as "the fitting inner disposition for approaching God in worship"); (2) **prayer** — Dan 9:4 (reverential fear of God as the inner disposition from which Daniel's prayer arises); Jer 26:19 (Hezekiah's fear producing active prayer that averted disaster); (3) **covenant** — Mal 2:5 (Levi's reverential fear as the covenant response to God's gift of life and peace — fear governing the covenant relationship); (4) **vow** — Jon 1:16 (the sailors' fear leading to sacrifice and vows — fear becoming the ground of devoti… |
| M01-B | finding | M01-B shows movement toward God through the theophanic fear and subsequent worship: Jon 1:16 (storm-terror converting to reverential worship — "fear becomes the inner ground of devotion"); Mat 27:54 (centurion's fear producing confession — "Truly this was the Son of God"); Mat 9:8 (crowd's fear "moves inward immediately into glorifying God" — fear as gateway to worship). |
| M01-E | finding | M01-E-VCG-02 shows the human person trembling before God's word as a specific mode of movement toward God: Isa 66:2 (trembling at God's word as the inner posture God looks for — the human person responsive before divine communication); Ezr 9:4; 10:3 (those who tremble at God's commandment gathering for covenant decision-making — trembling as the posture of covenant engagement). |

### T4.2.2  ·  Tier T4

> What does the evidence reveal about the inner posture required for this movement?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The inner posture required for movement toward God across M01 is: undivided heart, humility, whole-heartedness, and the absence of competing fear-objects. These are enabling conditions for the reverential posture that moves the person toward God. |
| M01-A | finding | The inner posture required for genuine movement toward God in M01-A includes: (1) **an undivided heart** (Psa 86:11: "fear of God requires inner integration; a divided heart is an obstacle"); (2) **humility** (Pro 15:33; 22:4: fear paired with humility); (3) **whole-heartedness** (1Sa 12:24: "all-heart devotion grounded in memory of God's great deeds"); (4) **the absence of competing fear-objects** (Isa 8:12-13: the prophet must not fear what the crowd fears in order to rightly fear God). |
| M01-E | finding | The inner posture required for trembling-at-God's-word (M01-E-VCG-02) includes: humility and a contrite spirit (Isa 66:2 anchor) — the posture that makes genuine responsiveness to God's word possible. |

### T4.2.3  ·  Tier T4

> What does the human-to-God direction of this characteristic reveal about the person's relationship with God?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The human-to-God direction of M01 reveals that genuine relationship with God begins in and is sustained by reverential fear. The absence of this fear (Rom 3:18; Psa 36:1) is the diagnostic of a broken relationship. The presence of it is the ground of covenant intimacy (Psa 25:14), divine provision (Psa 34:9), and eschatological reward (Rev 11:18; 19:5). The relationship is not possible without the asymmetrical inner posture that fear provides. |
| M01-A | finding | The extensive documentation of human-to-God reverential fear in M01-A reveals that the relationship between the human person and God is fundamentally asymmetrical: God is the holy, incomparable sovereign; the human person is the created image-bearer whose appropriate posture before God is awe and reverence. But the evidence also reveals this as a *relationship* rather than mere subjection: Psa 25:14 (fear positioning for covenant friendship — intimacy, not servility), Psa 103:13 (God showing "fatherly compassion" to those who fear him — parental, not merely imperial relationship). The human-to-God direction of M01-A reveals a relationship of asymmetrical intimacy: the appropriate posture is reverential, and that very reverential posture opens the person to God's friendship and covenant lo… |

### T4.2.4  ·  Tier T4

> If the evidence is silent on human-to-God operation, note this explicitly.

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| M01-C | silent | M01-C terror-as-force does not evidence human-to-God movement. The terror is deployed by God or imposed by military powers; it does not constitute a movement of the human inner person toward God. |
| M01-D | finding | M01-D dismay has limited human-to-God movement. Psa 6:3 (the dismay driving the "anguished cry to God asking how long") and Psa 30:7 (the psalmist's dismay producing prayer) show dismay triggering prayer — but the movement is toward God in crisis rather than the sustained worship of M01-A. |

### T4.3.1  ·  Tier T4

> Does the verse evidence show this characteristic being extended by one person toward another — and if so, how does it operate in that giving?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | Fear is not typically "given" as a gift from one person to another. The human-to-human dimension of M01 is primarily indirect: fear of God produces just treatment of others (M01-A), the command to release fear is extended from one to another (M01-B-VCG-06), and pastoral anxiety flows from loving concern (M01-F-VCG-05). |
| M01-A | finding | M01-A's ethical dimension involves extending the effects of fear toward others: the God-fearer treats the vulnerable justly (Lev 19:14; 25:43) and extends generosity (Lev 25:36-37). But the fear itself is not "given" to another — it is the inner posture that governs the person's treatment of others. The one quasi-exception is the pedagogical dimension: the psalmist offers to "teach fear of the Lord" (Psa 34:11) — fear being transmitted through instruction and example. |
| M01-B | finding | M01-B's "do not fear" command shows one person extending release from fear toward another: David to Mephibosheth (2Sa 9:7), Elisha to his servant (2Ki 6:16), Jesus to the disciples (Mar 4:40; Mat 28:10). The characteristic being extended is not fear itself but the command and ground that releases fear. |
| M01-F | finding | M01-F-VCG-05 (pastoral anxiety) shows one person extending concern toward another: Paul's anticipatory dread for his churches (2Cor 12:20; Gal 4:11) flows from his care. The anxiety is in Paul, motivated by love for others — a one-directional giving of concerned attention. |

### T4.3.2  ·  Tier T4

> What inner conditions or orientations in the giver enable genuine extension of this characteristic?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| M01-A | finding | For the transmission of reverential fear through instruction (Psa 34:11): the giver must themselves possess the fear genuinely (2Ki 17:28 shows that a priest who doesn't know how to fear God cannot teach it authentically — formation precedes transmission). |
| M01-B | finding | For the extension of "do not fear" release commands: the person who extends this must stand in a position of genuine authority or covenant assurance relative to the other (Jesus extending release from a position of divine authority; Jonathan extending it to David grounded in divine promise). |
| M01-F | finding | For the pastoral anxiety that flows from love: Paul's anxiety is enabled by his genuine love for his churches (Gal 4:11 context: "I am afraid I may have labored in vain for you" — the anxiety flows from the labour of love already invested). |

### T4.3.3  ·  Tier T4

> What does the evidence reveal about what the person must have received or become before they can genuinely give this characteristic?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The general principle confirmed by M01: genuine giving of the characteristic's effects requires genuine possession of the characteristic. The God-fearer who treats others justly does so from the interior ground of their own reverential fear. The person who releases another from fear does so from the ground of their own courageous trust. The person whose pastoral anxiety flows from love does so from the ground of genuine relational investment. |
| M01-A | finding | To transmit reverential fear through instruction (Psa 34:11), the instructor must themselves have received and been formed by the fear. Deu 31:12-13 implies a multi-generational formation chain: each generation hearing and forming the fear, then transmitting it to the next. The person cannot give what they have not received and been formed by. |

### T4.3.4  ·  Tier T4

> If the evidence is silent on the giving direction, note this explicitly.

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| M01-C | silent | M01-C (terror-as-force), M01-D (dismay), M01-E (trembling), and M01-G (timidity) are largely silent on the human-to-human giving direction. Terror, dismay, and trembling are experienced and not typically given. Timidity has no giving direction at all. |
| M01-D | silent | M01-C (terror-as-force), M01-D (dismay), M01-E (trembling), and M01-G (timidity) are largely silent on the human-to-human giving direction. Terror, dismay, and trembling are experienced and not typically given. Timidity has no giving direction at all. |
| M01-E | silent | M01-C (terror-as-force), M01-D (dismay), M01-E (trembling), and M01-G (timidity) are largely silent on the human-to-human giving direction. Terror, dismay, and trembling are experienced and not typically given. Timidity has no giving direction at all. |
| M01-G | silent | M01-C (terror-as-force), M01-D (dismay), M01-E (trembling), and M01-G (timidity) are largely silent on the human-to-human giving direction. Terror, dismay, and trembling are experienced and not typically given. Timidity has no giving direction at all. |

### T4.4.1  ·  Tier T4

> Does the verse evidence show this characteristic being received by a person from another — and if so, how does it operate in that reception?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The receiving direction shows three modes: (1) voluntary formed reception — reverential fear received through instruction (M01-A); (2) commanded-release reception — the frightened person receiving the command that releases acute fear (M01-B-VCG-06); (3) involuntary imposition — terror received against the will of the recipients (M01-C-VCG-01). |
| M01-A | finding | Reverential fear can be received through instruction: Deu 31:12-13 (the assembled community receiving the formation of fear through hearing Torah — the community is positioned to receive); 2Ki 17:28 (a priest sent to teach the settlers "how to fear the Lord" — reception through instructed formation); Psa 34:11 (the psalmist's offer to "instruct children in fear of the Lord" — explicit receptive formation context). |
| M01-B | finding | The "do not fear" command is received by the person who is gripped by acute fear: Lam 3:57 (divine response to the inner cry: "God drew near and spoke 'Do not fear' — the divine response to the inner cry is direct personal reassurance, addressing fear with the intimacy of God's nearness"). The reception requires the will's openness to the divine word. |
| M01-C | finding | Terror-as-weapon is "received" involuntarily by enemy peoples: Gen 35:5 (terror falling on surrounding cities — no choice in reception); Exo 23:27 (God's terror working on enemy peoples' inner being — involuntary imposition). |

### T4.4.2  ·  Tier T4

> What inner conditions enable or block reception of this characteristic from another person?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The enabling conditions for receiving fear-related communication (whether instructed formation or commanded release) are: will-openness, trust in the speaker, and freedom from prior competing commitments. The blocking conditions are: divided or hardened heart, distrust, competing allegiances, and overwhelming grief or dismay. |
| M01-A | finding | Reception of reverential fear through instruction is enabled by: openness of will (Deu 31:12-13 implies that gathering and hearing are necessary — the person must present themselves); not yet having competing allegiances (2Ki 17 corpus shows that syncretistic prior allegiances block genuine reception of fear-of-God). Reception is blocked by: divided heart (Psa 86:11), hardened heart (Isa 63:17), and prior commitment to other fear-objects (2Ki 17:33 — fearing the Lord and serving other gods simultaneously, which prevents genuine reception). |
| M01-B | finding | Reception of the "do not fear" command is enabled by: trust in the one speaking (Isa 43:1 anchor: the "you are mine" ground for releasing fear requires trust in the speaker's authority), and the will's openness to release the fear (the command is addressed to the will, which must choose to comply). It is blocked by: distrust (Act 9:26: Jerusalem disciples not trusting Paul's conversion), or by fear so overwhelming that the command cannot penetrate (1Sa 4:20: the dying mother unable to receive the reassurance because grief overwhelms everything). |

### T4.4.3  ·  Tier T4

> What is the inner-being state of the person who encounters this characteristic from another but does not receive it?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | Non-reception of the commanded-or-instructed forms of M01 leaves the person in the state they were in: if in acute fear, still gripped; if in moral blindness, still blind; if in divided allegiance, still divided. The characteristic must be received by the will for it to take effect — outer exposure without inner reception leaves the person unchanged. |
| M01-A | finding | The person who encounters instruction in the fear of the Lord but does not receive it is in the state of: moral blindness (Psa 36:1; Rom 3:18), defiant self-sufficiency (Psa 55:19), or syncretistic compromise (2Ki 17:33 — fearing the Lord and other gods simultaneously, which is the non-reception of genuine fear). Jer 5:24 (people who do not say in their hearts "let us fear the Lord" — ingratitude and irreverence are one, the inner state is a closed heart toward God). |
| M01-B | finding | The person who hears "do not fear" but does not receive it remains in paralysis, flight, or speech-suppression. 1Sa 4:20 (dying mother unable to receive the reassurance — grief so total that the word cannot penetrate). |

### T4.4.4  ·  Tier T4

> If the evidence is silent on the receiving direction, note this explicitly.

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| M01-D | silent | M01-D (dismay), M01-E (trembling, except E-VCG-02's instructed dimension), and M01-G (timidity) do not have extensive evidence of the receiving-from-another direction. These sub-groups describe primarily involuntary or inner-constitution-based characteristics rather than received ones. |
| M01-E | silent | M01-D (dismay), M01-E (trembling, except E-VCG-02's instructed dimension), and M01-G (timidity) do not have extensive evidence of the receiving-from-another direction. These sub-groups describe primarily involuntary or inner-constitution-based characteristics rather than received ones. |
| M01-G | silent | M01-D (dismay), M01-E (trembling, except E-VCG-02's instructed dimension), and M01-G (timidity) do not have extensive evidence of the receiving-from-another direction. These sub-groups describe primarily involuntary or inner-constitution-based characteristics rather than received ones. |

### T4.5.1  ·  Tier T4

> Does the evidence indicate whether this characteristic operates differently within existing relational bonds versus across relational distance or difference?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | M01-A operates consistently across all relational bonds and distances. The characteristic's ethical dimension specifically addresses power-asymmetric relationships where relational exploitation would otherwise be possible. This confirms that fear-of-God is not a parochial characteristic limited to in-group relationships but operates as a universal governing orientation. |
| M01-A | finding | M01-A operates consistently across relational distance — fear of God applies to the person's treatment of strangers (Lev 25:36-37: not exploiting a stranger's poverty), servants (Lev 25:43: no ruthless domination over a servant who is a fellow Israelite), enemies (Deu 25:18: Amalekites' attack on the weak is evidence of absent God-fear), and foreigners (Act 10:35: "anyone who fears God and does what is right is acceptable to him regardless of nationality"). The characteristic operates across all relational distance and difference. It does not narrow to existing bonds. |
| M01-A | finding | M01-A's ethical dimension operates specifically in power-asymmetry relationships: Lev 19:14 (the vulnerable deaf and blind), Lev 25:43 (the servant). Fear of God operates precisely where power difference would otherwise enable exploitation. The characteristic does not narrow to relational equals. |
| M01-B | finding | M01-B's social fear (B-VCG-04) operates across relational difference in the direction of crowd-management: the leaders' fear of the crowd is fear across social distance (the crowd as mass, not individuals in relationship). M01-B's self-preservation fear (B-VCG-05) also operates across relational distance — Jacob's fear of Esau (Gen 32:7-11), the Gibeonites' fear of the covenant community (Jos 9:24). |

### T4.5.2  ·  Tier T4

> Does this characteristic operate within covenantal contexts only, or does it cross covenantal boundaries?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | M01-A's reverential fear of God crosses covenantal boundaries and is presented as universally required of all peoples. The characteristic is not parochial. The covenant community is the primary locus of its formation, but it is directed toward and required of all. |
| M01-A | finding | M01-A crosses covenantal boundaries. The Gen 20:11 material (Abraham assuming absence of God-fear in Gerar's people — implying fear-of-God is expected in non-Israelites), Act 10:35 ("anyone who fears God and does what is right is acceptable to him regardless of nationality"), and the nations-fearing-God material (Psa 102:15; Isa 25:3; Rev 14:7; 19:5) all show that reverential fear of God is not limited to covenant members. God demands and expects it of all peoples; the goal is universal fear-of-God (Mal 1:14: "God's name will evoke genuine reverent fear among all nations"). |
| M01-A | finding | M01-C and M01-A-VCG-07 show God deploying fear across covenantal boundaries as a historical governance instrument: God instilling fear of Israel in surrounding nations, God producing fear in Egyptian overseers at the Exodus. The covenantal-cross operation is explicit. |
| M01-C | finding | M01-C and M01-A-VCG-07 show God deploying fear across covenantal boundaries as a historical governance instrument: God instilling fear of Israel in surrounding nations, God producing fear in Egyptian overseers at the Exodus. The covenantal-cross operation is explicit. |

### T4.5.3  ·  Tier T4

> What does the evidence reveal about the relational scope of this characteristic — who is included and who is not?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The relational scope of M01-A is genuinely universal: God requires reverential fear of all peoples and rewards it wherever it is found (Act 10:35). The characteristic's scope is as wide as God's sovereignty — which is total. |
| M01-A | finding | M01-A's scope includes: all Israel (the primary covenant community throughout the Deuteronomy and Psalms corpus), the messianic king (Isa 11:2-3), individual leaders and judges (Exo 18:21; 2Ch 19:9), foreigners who come to know God (Solomon's prayer for foreigners, 1Ki 8:43; Cornelius, Act 10:2), and ultimately all nations (Rev 14:7; 19:5). The scope is universal in aspiration. Exclusions are not based on ethnic identity but on the inner disposition: those whose hearts are hardened (Isa 63:17), whose allegiance is divided (2Ki 17:33), or who do not fear God at all (Psa 36:1) are excluded not from God's demand but from receiving the blessing that fear-of-God confers. |

### T4.5.4  ·  Tier T4

> If the evidence is silent on relational boundaries, note this explicitly.

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| M01-D | silent | M01-D (dismay), M01-E (trembling), and M01-F (anticipatory dread) do not have distinct relational boundary evidence. These sub-groups describe primarily individual inner experiences rather than relationally scoped characteristics. |
| M01-E | silent | M01-D (dismay), M01-E (trembling), and M01-F (anticipatory dread) do not have distinct relational boundary evidence. These sub-groups describe primarily individual inner experiences rather than relationally scoped characteristics. |
| M01-F | silent | M01-D (dismay), M01-E (trembling), and M01-F (anticipatory dread) do not have distinct relational boundary evidence. These sub-groups describe primarily individual inner experiences rather than relationally scoped characteristics. |

### T4.6.1  ·  Tier T4

> Does the verse evidence show this characteristic operating in relation to other spiritual beings — angelic or adversarial — and if so, how?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | Angelic beings are prominent mediators of M01-B fear (appearances producing fear, commands releasing fear). The divine council evidences reverential fear of God (Psa 89:7 — M01-A). Adversarial spiritual operations are less prominent in the evidenced material: the beasts of Daniel's visions (M01-B-VCG-01) and the general spiritual-resistance context of M01-G (Rev 21:8's apostasy-under-pressure) are the nearest instances. |
| M01-A | finding | M01-A shows fear of God operating in the angelic realm: Psa 89:7 (God is "greatly to be feared among the holy ones in the divine council — his awesomeness surpasses all heavenly beings, making reverential fear the only fitting inner response **even in heaven**"). Fear of God is not merely a human posture but the appropriate posture of the divine council before God. Gen 22:12 (the angel of the Lord affirming Abraham's fear of God as evidenced by his willingness to sacrifice — the fear tested and confirmed through angelic mediation). |
| M01-B | finding | M01-B shows angelic mediation of fear extensively: the angelic appearances throughout the NT that produce fear in human persons (Luk 1:12-13; Luk 2:9-10; Mat 28:4-5; Luk 24:5; Act 10:4; Rev 1:17) are the most concentrated evidence. Angels both produce acute fear and command its release ("do not be afraid" from angels across the corpus). Angels operate as the interface through which divine holiness makes itself felt in the human inner life. |
| M01-B | finding | M01-B-VCG-01 (fear before supernatural encounters) shows specific instances of adversarial encounter producing fear: Dan 7:7 (the fourth beast — terrifying in appearance, producing fear — in the visionary realm); Mar 14:33 (Jesus in Gethsemane, ekthambeo — though this is the suffering Son before the Father's judgment rather than adversarial encounter). The adversarial spiritual dimension is present but not dominant in the evidenced material. |
| M01-F | finding | M01-F-VCG-04's fearful expectation of judgment (Heb 10:27) operates in the context of divine judgment as the eschatological reality — a spiritual-being interface in the sense that it anticipates encountering God as judge. |

### T4.6.2  ·  Tier T4

> Is this characteristic a site of adversarial activity — something that can be attacked, distorted, or weaponised by adversarial spiritual powers?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The characteristic is a site of adversarial activity in at least three forms: (1) the displacement of God-directed fear by false-object fear (M01-A-VCG-05: idols, crowds, political powers); (2) the use of fear-induction as a weapon against God's servants (M01-B-VCG-03: Neh 6:9-14); (3) the spirit of timidity as a non-divine inner disposition that may have adversarial origin (M01-G, 2Ti 1:7). |
| M01-A | finding | M01-A shows fear being displaced by false-object attachment — a pattern consistent with adversarial distortion: 2Ki 17 corpus (reverential fear of God replaced by fear of idols — idols as adversarial alternatives to the living God); Isa 8:12 (social fear being substituted for fear of God — Isaiah commanded to resist adopting the crowd's conspiratorial dread). The systematic displacement of fear-of-God by fear-of-idols or fear-of-crowd represents a pattern in which the characteristic's proper direction is corrupted. |
| M01-B | finding | M01-B's social fear (B-VCG-04) and self-preservation fear can be used as tools of adversarial pressure: Neh 6:9-14 (enemies deliberately engineering fear in Nehemiah and his workers as a weapon — "fear used as a tool to corrupt his will"). The intentional use of fear-induction as a weapon against God's servants is evidenced. |
| M01-G | finding | M01-G timidity (2Ti 1:7: "God has not given us a spirit of timidity") implies that the spirit of timidity has a spiritual source distinct from God. This is the nearest statement to adversarial spiritual activity against the characteristic. |

### T4.6.3  ·  Tier T4

> Is this characteristic communicated, strengthened, or mediated through angelic ministry in the evidence?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | Angelic ministry is the primary mediation structure for M01-B's theophanic fear (producing it) and for the commanded release of that fear (commanding it away). Angels are the agents through which divine holiness crosses the threshold between the divine and the human, producing both fear and its commanded release. |
| M01-B | finding | Yes, extensively in M01-B. Angels both produce fear (Luk 2:9 anchor; Mat 28:4) and release it ("do not be afraid" — Luk 1:13; Luk 1:30; Luk 2:10; Mat 28:5; Rev 1:17). The angelic role is to mediate divine presence (producing appropriate fear) and divine reassurance (releasing inappropriate fear). Angels function as the two-directional interface between divine holiness and human inner life in the fear register. |
| M01-E | finding | The theophanic trembling at Sinai (Exo 19:16 anchor, E-VCG-01) is mediated through divine presence itself rather than specifically through angels. |

### T4.6.4  ·  Tier T4

> If the evidence is silent on the spiritual beings interface, note this explicitly.

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
