| M01-D | silent | M01-D (dismay), most M01-E sub-groups (somatic trembling beyond the theophanic), and M01-F (anticipatory dread) are largely silent on explicit spiritual beings interface. Their operations do not require angelic mediation in the evidenced material. |
| M01-E | silent | M01-D (dismay), most M01-E sub-groups (somatic trembling beyond the theophanic), and M01-F (anticipatory dread) are largely silent on explicit spiritual beings interface. Their operations do not require angelic mediation in the evidenced material. |
| M01-F | silent | M01-D (dismay), most M01-E sub-groups (somatic trembling beyond the theophanic), and M01-F (anticipatory dread) are largely silent on explicit spiritual beings interface. Their operations do not require angelic mediation in the evidenced material. |

### T5.1.1  ·  Tier T5

> Does this characteristic produce transformation in the person — and if so, does it change the person's condition, the person's orientation to their condition, or both?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | M01 produces transformation in both condition and orientation across all sub-groups. The most consistent transformation pattern is: fear directed toward God (M01-A) produces stable new conditions (wisdom, life, security) and transformed orientations (from threat-directed to God-directed). Fear commanded away (M01-B-VCG-06) transforms orientation without necessarily changing circumstance. Chronic fear overcome (M01-F, G) transforms condition (from bondage to freedom). The cluster confirms that fear is formatively powerful in both directions — ordered fear builds the person up; unaddressed disordered fear tears the person down. |
| M01-A | finding | M01-A reverential fear produces transformation in both dimensions. It changes **orientation**: Exo 14:31 (Israel's witness of God's power over Egypt produces fear of the Lord and belief — the people's inner orientation shifts from terror of Egypt to reverent trust in God); Jon 1:16 (sailors' storm-terror converts into reverential worship — "fear becomes the inner ground of devotion" — a transformation of orientation from threat-directed to God-directed fear). It also produces change in **condition**: Pro 10:27 (fear of the Lord extending life — a condition-change); Pro 19:23 (fear leading to life and "restful inner satisfaction" — a settled new condition of security); Jer 32:40 (God implanting fear as a permanent disposition "preventing them from turning away" — a condition of inner stabi… |
| M01-B | finding | M01-B's commanded-release register (M01-B-VCG-06, anchor Isa 43:1) produces transformation in orientation: the person who receives "do not fear" moves from a grip of acute dread to a posture of trust grounded in divine presence. Dan 10:19 (M01-B-VCG-01: "fear is commanded away and replaced by peace and strength — the inner person moves from fearful weakness to fortified courage as the heavenly messenger speaks"). This is primarily **orientation-change** — the person's relationship to their threatening circumstance shifts without the circumstance itself changing. |
| M01-C | finding | M01-C's divinely deployed terror produces **condition-change** in enemy peoples: Gen 35:5 (God-sent terror paralysing the will of surrounding cities — their condition of active hostility becomes one of paralysis); Est 9:2-3 (dread of the Jews redirecting the will of provincial officials — their condition of opposition converts to active assistance). The condition of the enemy is transformed by the terror imposed. |
| M01-D | finding | M01-D dismay produces **condition-change** through its destructive dimension (inner collapse) and through its commanded-against-dismay corpus (M01-D-VCG-04): Jer 1:17 (the prophet commanded not to let dismay grip him — the implied transformation is from potential collapse to sustained composure grounded in divine commission). Dismay unchecked is a condition-worsening transformation; commanded against, it is resisted as the precondition of a transformed stable condition. |
| M01-E | finding | M01-E-VCG-02 (trembling at God's word, anchor Isa 66:2) produces transformation in orientation: those who tremble at God's word form a defined community whose orientation toward divine communication is permanently marked by reverential sobriety (Isa 66:5: their trembling reverence marks their identity and sets them apart, with God's vindication promised to this inner posture — an orientation-change producing a stable identity). |
| M01-F | finding | M01-F's primary transformative movement is from chronic anxiety to rest. Isa 12:2 (M01-F-VCG-04: "trust in God displacing dread from the inner person — the speaker declares that because God is his strength, fear no longer has a hold on his heart"); 1Jo 4:18 (M01-A-VCG-06/F-VCG-04: "perfect love expels fear entirely" — a transformation of inner condition in which the characteristic is removed). Psa 34:4 (anchor M01-F-VCG-02: "the psalmist sought the Lord and was delivered from all his fears — these fears were inner terrors and anxieties; divine response removed them entirely"). Both condition and orientation change. |
| M01-G | finding | M01-G's transformation is the spirit-level move from timidity to the spirit of power, love, and self-control (2Ti 1:7 anchor: the contrast implies that the gift of God's spirit displaces the spirit of timidity — a spirit-level condition-change). 2Ti 1:6 context (the call to stir up the gift) implies the transformation is not automatic but involves the person's own engagement. |

### T5.1.2  ·  Tier T5

> Is the transformation produced by this characteristic reversible or irreversible in the verse evidence?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The transformation produced by M01 is: reversible in its acute form (M01-B: fear addressed and released); permanently formative in its sustained ordered form (M01-A: Jer 32:40 implantation); reversible through corruption or hardening (M01-A: Isa 29:13; 2Ki 17 corpus); and eschatologically irreversible in its final expression (M01-G: Rev 21:8; M01-A: Rev 11:18 — the redeemed fear God permanently). |
| M01-A | finding | M01-A evidences both reversible and irreversible transformation. The **irreversible** dimension: Jer 32:40 (God implanting the fear as a "permanent inner disposition preventing them from turning away" — permanence is explicit); the "Fear of Isaac" formula (Gen 31:42; 31:53 — anchors A-VCG-06) suggests a defining characterisation that became Isaac's identity, not a reversible episode. The **reversible** dimension: 2Ki 17 corpus (M01-A-VCG-05: the settlers' syncretistic fear shows that genuine fear of God can be corrupted — a reversal of the right inner orientation). Isa 29:13 (fear becoming hollow external formula — a degradation of what was once genuine). The evidence shows transformation can be reversed through corruption, hardened heart (Isa 63:17), and competing allegiance. |
| M01-B | finding | M01-B's acute-fear transformations are primarily **reversible** in the moment (fear released when divine reassurance comes: Mat 17:7; Luk 5:10) but can calcify into permanent states (1Sa 18:29: Saul's fear of David intensifies and "becomes permanent — the inner root of his sustained enmity"). Reversibility depends on whether the fear is addressed or left to solidify. |
| M01-G | finding | M01-G: 2Ti 1:7 (timidity is not from God) implies it is a reversible condition — the gift of power, love, and self-control is available (2Ti 1:6). But Rev 21:8 (cowardice in the lake of fire) suggests that sustained unchecked timidity culminates in irreversible judgment-state. |

### T5.1.3  ·  Tier T5

> If the evidence is silent on transformation, note this explicitly.

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| M01-C | silent | M01-C (terror-as-force) is largely silent on transformation of the person who experiences it in any sustained formative sense. The terror is imposed, not formative. The exception is the Ezekiel 32 corpus (M01-C-VCG-03) which shows terror stripped from empires in death — a transformation of the terrorisers rather than the terrorised. |

### T5.2.1  ·  Tier T5

> Does the verse evidence describe a sequence of inner states through which this characteristic moves the person — a before, during, and after?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The verse evidence describes clear before-during-after sequences primarily in M01-A (complacency → encounter → reverential fear), M01-B-VCG-06 (fear → divine word → release), M01-E-VCG-02 (insensitivity → humility → trembling identity), and M01-F's redemptive form (dread → seeking → deliverance). The sequences across the cluster share a common structure: an initial state, a transformative encounter or word, and a new settled inner condition. |
| M01-A | finding | M01-A-VCG-04 (fear arising from witnessing God's deeds) shows a clear before-during-after sequence. Before: complacency or absence of fear (Exo 9:30: Pharaoh and servants do not yet fear the Lord). During: encounter with God's power (Exo 14:31: witnessing God's victory at the sea). After: fear and belief (Exo 14:31: "Israel feared the Lord and believed" — a settled new inner state following the encounter). Jon 1:5-16 shows the most complete sequence: before (mariners fearing the storm, crying to their own gods), during (encounter with Jonah's testimony and the storm's cessation), after (Jon 1:16: "the men feared the Lord greatly" and offered sacrifice and vows — a transformed reverential state). |
| M01-B | finding | M01-B-VCG-06 (commanded release of fear, anchor Isa 43:1) shows a before-during-after sequence structurally: before (fear gripping the inner person), during (divine word of identity and assurance spoken), after (the commanded release taking effect as trust replaces dread — implicit in the corpus as the intended outcome of each "do not fear" command). Dan 10:19 (M01-B-VCG-01: fear gripping Daniel → angel touching him and speaking → "inner person moves from fearful weakness to fortified courage") is the most explicit sequence. **[Folded from wa_session_b_findings.id=68; finding_id=DIM-61-002; registry=fear]** ya.re (H3372G) groups add the divine 'Fear not' command (298-001) as a structuring element — showing the divine address to inner fear as a distinct inner-being category. The reassuranc… |
| M01-E | finding | M01-E-VCG-02 (trembling at God's word) shows a sequence: before (the condition of those who do not tremble — spiritual insensitivity), during (encountering God's word in a posture of humility and contrition), after (trembling as the stable inner-somatic posture of the community defined by it, Isa 66:5: "God's vindication promised to this inner posture"). Ezr 9:4-10:3 shows the sequence more concretely: before (covenant unfaithfulness discovered), during (Ezra and the trembling community gathering in appalled grief), after (covenant decision made from the posture of trembling — a transformed community orientation toward God's commandments). |
| M01-F | finding | M01-F-VCG-02 (anchor Job 3:25) shows the dread-sequence: before (dread sitting within as anticipated fear), during (the dreaded event materialising), after (the correspondence between fear and event — confirmation of the anticipatory dread). Psa 34:4 (anchor F-VCG-02: fear → seeking the Lord → deliverance from all fears) shows the redemptive sequence. |

### T5.2.2  ·  Tier T5

> What are those states, and what does the sequence reveal about how this characteristic works?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | Across the evidenced sequences, the operative mechanism is consistent: encounter with a superior reality (divine presence, God's word, divine identity) transforms the inner person's prior state. The characteristic works through encounter, not through mere cognitive recalibration. |
| M01-A | finding | The states in M01-A's sequence are: (1) absence of reverential fear / competing fear-objects; (2) encounter with God's power or word; (3) settled reverential orientation. The sequence reveals that fear-of-God is formed through encounter and then becomes stable disposition — it is not achieved by effort alone but by genuine meeting with God's reality. The Jer 32:40 implantation sequence (divine implantation → permanent disposition) shows the divine-initiative version of the same structure. |
| M01-B | finding | The states in M01-B-VCG-06's sequence are: (1) acute fear gripping the will; (2) divine word of identity and presence ("you are mine," Isa 43:1); (3) trust replacing dread. The sequence reveals that the characteristic works through personal address — the release of fear requires not just information but relational claim. God's "you are mine" is the operative mechanism, not a generic reassurance. |

### T5.2.3  ·  Tier T5

> If the evidence is silent on sequence, note this explicitly.

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| M01-C | silent | M01-C (terror-as-force) and M01-D (dismay) are largely silent on positive formative sequences. M01-C's terror produces paralysis with no before-during-after growth sequence documented. M01-D-VCG-04 (commanded against dismay) implies a before (potential collapse) and an after (commanded composure) but the during and the mechanism are less detailed than in M01-A and B. |
| M01-D | silent | M01-C (terror-as-force) and M01-D (dismay) are largely silent on positive formative sequences. M01-C's terror produces paralysis with no before-during-after growth sequence documented. M01-D-VCG-04 (commanded against dismay) implies a before (potential collapse) and an after (commanded composure) but the during and the mechanism are less detailed than in M01-A and B. |
| M01-G | silent | M01-G timidity has no documented inner-states sequence. 2Ti 1:7 describes the contrast between timidity and the spirit God gives but does not narrate a sequence through which the transformation is accomplished. |

### T5.3.1  ·  Tier T5

> What mechanism does this characteristic use to produce change in the person — discipline, encounter, gradual formation, sudden transformation, or something else?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The mechanisms producing change in M01 are: encounter (M01-A from God's acts, M01-B from angelic/divine appearance), gradual formation (M01-A through Torah and worship practices), divine implantation (M01-A, Jer 32:40), divine word (M01-B-VCG-06 commanded release), divine response to seeking (M01-F resolution), and active engagement with divine gift (M01-G, 2Ti 1:6-7). The cluster does not evidence discipline as a primary mechanism for forming reverential fear; formation is primarily through encounter and sustained practice. |
| M01-A | finding | M01-A uses multiple mechanisms: (1) **encounter** — Exo 14:31 (witnessing God's power at the sea); Hag 1:12 (hearing the prophetic word); Jon 1:16 (storm + testimony producing sudden reverential shift); (2) **gradual formation** — Deu 14:23; 31:12-13 (regular worship and Torah-reading designed to cultivate the fear over time — explicitly long-term formative process); Pro 2:5 (fear as "fruit of earnest seeking" — arrived at through diligent pursuit rather than sudden encounter); (3) **divine implantation** — Jer 32:40 (God pledging to place the fear directly in the hearts of his people — a divine act of immediate transformation rather than gradual process); (4) **social transmission** — Psa 34:11 (psalmist teaching fear to children — interpersonal formation mechanism). |
| M01-B | finding | M01-B's acute fear is produced by **encounter** (sudden, involuntary): 1Sa 17:24 (sight of Goliath immediately triggering overwhelming fear); Luk 2:9 (angelic appearance immediately filling the shepherds with great fear). The release of acute fear (B-VCG-06) uses the mechanism of **divine word** — the spoken command "do not fear" grounded in divine identity and presence. **[Folded from wa_session_b_findings.id=68; finding_id=DIM-61-002; registry=fear]** ya.re (H3372G) groups add the divine 'Fear not' command (298-001) as a structuring element — showing the divine address to inner fear as a distinct inner-being category. The reassurance pattern (divine declaration of presence + commanded displacement of fear) is significant for understanding how the inner-being state of fear is meant to be… |
| M01-E | finding | M01-E-VCG-02's trembling-at-word is produced by **gradual formation** in community: Ezr 9:4; 10:3 (the community of those who tremble at God's word — a formed posture, not a sudden event). The M01-E-VCG-01 theophanic trembling is produced by **sudden encounter** (Exo 19:16: the Sinai phenomena producing immediate involuntary trembling). |
| M01-F | finding | M01-F's chronic anxiety operates as a sustained **condition** rather than a mechanism producing change. Its resolution (Psa 34:4 anchor: seeking the Lord → deliverance from all fears) uses the mechanism of **divine response to seeking** — not discipline or self-effort but relational engagement with God producing the resolution. |
| M01-G | finding | M01-G's transformation from timidity to the spirit of power uses the mechanism of **stirring up the divine gift** (2Ti 1:6-7 context: "stir up the gift of God" — implying active engagement with what God has already given, not a passive waiting for sudden transformation). |

### T5.3.2  ·  Tier T5

> Does the evidence distinguish between mechanisms in different contexts?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | Different canonical contexts deploy different mechanisms for forming the same reverential fear. The consistency of the destination (reverential fear as governing orientation) with the diversity of the mechanisms confirms that the characteristic is convergently achievable through multiple pathways. |
| M01-A | finding | Yes. In the wisdom tradition the mechanism is diligent seeking (Pro 2:5). In the Deuteronomic tradition the mechanism is communal hearing of Torah (Deu 14:23; 31:12-13). In the prophetic tradition the mechanism is divine implantation (Jer 32:40). In the narrative tradition the mechanism is witnessed encounter with divine power (Exo 14:31; Hag 1:12). The mechanism is context-dependent, with all pathways converging on the same inner disposition. |

### T5.3.3  ·  Tier T5

> If the evidence is silent on mechanism, note this explicitly.

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| M01-C | silent | M01-C (terror-as-force) and M01-D (dismay) are silent on any positive formation mechanism. These sub-groups describe imposed states rather than formative processes. No mechanism for developing terror-endurance or dismay-resilience is evidenced in the verse material. |
| M01-D | silent | M01-C (terror-as-force) and M01-D (dismay) are silent on any positive formation mechanism. These sub-groups describe imposed states rather than formative processes. No mechanism for developing terror-endurance or dismay-resilience is evidenced in the verse material. |

### T5.4.1  ·  Tier T5

> Does the verse evidence show this characteristic operating in relation to suffering or affliction — as a response to it, a product of it, or a context for it?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | Suffering and affliction are the primary context for M01's disordered sub-groups (B's social fear, D's dismay, F's chronic anxiety, G's timidity). Suffering is the **test** for M01-A's reverential fear (Job corpus) and the **context** in which the characteristic either holds (Job 2:3) or yields (Isa 63:17; Jer 3:8). The cluster confirms that suffering is the crucible in which the inner fear-disposition is revealed and tested. |
| M01-A | finding | M01-A operates in the context of suffering. Job 1:8; 2:3 (God affirming Job's fear-of-God character after intense suffering — the suffering does not destroy the reverential posture; rather, the fear is shown to hold through it). Job 2:3 anchor: "God again upholds Job's God-fearing character after intense suffering, showing that **genuine reverence is a disposition that holds fast even under severe trial**." Fear-of-God is tested by suffering and shown to be the characteristic that does not yield to affliction. |
| M01-B | finding | M01-B operates extensively as a **response to suffering**: 2Cor 7:5 (M01-F-VCG-05 context: "fear is located 'within' as an inward experience alongside external conflicts, describing an internal climate of dread or anxiety that the body itself endured with no rest" — suffering producing acute inner fear). 1Pe 3:14 (M01-B-VCG-03: believers who suffer for righteousness are commanded not to let fear of persecutors grip their inner being — suffering is the context in which the command against fear is necessary). |
| M01-D | finding | M01-D dismay is routinely produced by catastrophic suffering: Job 4:5 (M01-D-VCG-01: "when suffering touched Job personally, dismay overtook him — adversity reaching one's own self breaks inner composure in a way advising others could not prepare one for"); Psa 6:2-3 (anchor M01-D-VCG-01: the psalmist's bones deeply troubled and soul greatly dismayed — physical suffering producing inner collapse). Suffering is the primary context and producer of M01-D. |
| M01-F | finding | M01-F-VCG-01 (chronic pervasive anxiety) is explicitly a product of sustained suffering and threat: Eze 4:16; 12:18-19 (anxiety accompanying eating bread by weight in besieged Jerusalem — siege conditions as the producing context for chronic anxiety). Heb 2:15 (fear of death holding people in lifelong inner slavery — mortality itself as the suffering context for this anxiety). |
| M01-G | finding | M01-G timidity's context is explicitly persecution and threat: Rev 21:8 (cowardice in the context of apostasy under pressure); 1Pe 3:14-15 (M01-B-VCG-03/A-VCG-06: believers commanded not to fear persecutors — the threat of persecution is the suffering context for the timidity-temptation). |

### T5.4.2  ·  Tier T5

> Does suffering deepen, test, reveal, or produce this characteristic in the person?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The cluster divides on this question: suffering tests and reveals the ordered fear (M01-A), while it produces the disordered forms (M01-B's severity, D, F, G). This asymmetry is a significant formative finding: the person whose inner life is governed by reverential fear of God (M01-A) has a fear that can withstand suffering; those governed by other fears find that suffering intensifies and reveals the inadequacy of those fear-objects. |
| M01-A | finding | Suffering **tests and reveals** reverential fear in M01-A. Job 1:9 (Satan's question: is Job's fear truly inner and disinterested? — the challenge that suffering is designed to answer); Job 2:3 (God affirming Job's fear after suffering — the trial reveals the genuineness of the disposition). Suffering does not produce the reverential fear but tests whether it is authentic. |
| M01-B | finding | Suffering **produces** the disordered forms of fear in M01-B (acute alarm), D (dismay), F (chronic anxiety), and G (timidity as apostasy-under-pressure). These sub-groups arise directly from suffering and affliction contexts. |
| M01-D | finding | Suffering **produces** the disordered forms of fear in M01-B (acute alarm), D (dismay), F (chronic anxiety), and G (timidity as apostasy-under-pressure). These sub-groups arise directly from suffering and affliction contexts. |
| M01-F | finding | Suffering **produces** the disordered forms of fear in M01-B (acute alarm), D (dismay), F (chronic anxiety), and G (timidity as apostasy-under-pressure). These sub-groups arise directly from suffering and affliction contexts. |
| M01-G | finding | Suffering **produces** the disordered forms of fear in M01-B (acute alarm), D (dismay), F (chronic anxiety), and G (timidity as apostasy-under-pressure). These sub-groups arise directly from suffering and affliction contexts. |

### T5.4.3  ·  Tier T5

> If the evidence is silent on the relationship to suffering, note this explicitly.

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| M01-C | silent | M01-C (terror-as-force) has limited direct relationship to personal suffering in the formative sense. Terror is imposed by God on enemies or wielded by empires — it is not primarily a response to the person's own suffering. |

### T5.5.1  ·  Tier T5

> Does the verse evidence show this characteristic participating in the longer arc of character formation and sanctification — shaping the person over time toward greater likeness?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | M01-A is the most formation-participative sub-group. The longer arc shows: fear of God as the central character-forming orientation produces wisdom, ethical integration, covenant faithfulness, and community identity over time. The characteristic participates in sanctification by orienting the whole person toward God as the governing reality, producing cumulative character formation rather than episodic religious experiences. |
| M01-A | finding | M01-A is the most explicitly formation-participating sub-group in the cluster. The evidence shows fear-of-God operating as the central character-forming orientation across multiple canonical contexts: (1) **transmissibility** — Deu 31:12-13 (cultivated in children across generations); Psa 34:11 (fear taught to the next generation — character formation through pedagogical transmission); (2) **sustained formation** — Deu 14:23 (regular worship practices designed to cultivate enduring inner reverence — a long-arc formative process); Pro 15:33 (fear of the Lord as the medium in which wisdom's instruction is received, shaping the person toward teachability and humility); (3) **character integration** — Job 1:1 (fear of God integrated with blamelessness, uprightness, and turning from evil — a c… |
| M01-E | finding | M01-E-VCG-02's trembling-at-God's-word participates in sanctification formation: Ezr 9:4; 10:3 (those who tremble at God's word form a community gathered around covenant decision-making — the trembling posture leading to covenant action as an expression of ongoing sanctification). |
| M01-G | finding | M01-G's transformation arc (from timidity to the spirit of power, love, and self-control, 2Ti 1:7 anchor) is explicitly part of the Christian formation arc. 2Ti 1:6-7 places this in the context of spiritual development: "stir up the gift" implies an ongoing process of character formation toward the fullness of God's intended spirit. |

### T5.5.2  ·  Tier T5

> What does the evidence reveal about the role of this characteristic in that longer arc?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The cluster confirms that fear-of-God (M01-A) is foundational to the formation arc rather than peripheral to it. It is not the endpoint but the beginning — the orientation from which wisdom, ethics, covenant faithfulness, and relational integrity all grow. The cluster also shows that the freedom from disordered fear (M01-F, G) is part of the sanctification arc: Heb 2:15 (deliverance from fear-of-death slavery) and 1Jo 4:18 (perfect love casting out punishment-anticipatory fear) represent stages of formation toward maturity. |
| M01-A | finding | M01-A's role in the formation arc is **foundational and governing**: Pro 1:7 (fear of the Lord is the beginning of wisdom — not a stage to pass through but the foundation from which all formation proceeds); Ecc 12:13 (fearing God is the whole duty of the human person — the comprehensive orientation of the whole life); Isa 11:2-3 (fear of the Lord as a Spirit-gift resting on the messianic king alongside wisdom, understanding, counsel, and might — the character of complete formation). Fear-of-God is not one formation element among many but the ground from which all other character formation grows. |

They describe states experienced rather than character-forming processes. The commanded-against-dismay material (M01-D-VCG-04) implies formation resistance (not yielding to dismay) but does not describe a positive formation arc. |

### T5.6.1  ·  Tier T5

> Does the verse evidence point this characteristic toward an eschatological fullness — a future state toward which its present operation is oriented?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The cluster's eschatological fullness is a state in which: reverential fear of God is universal, perfected, and permanent (M01-A, Rev corpus); all disordering fears (threat, death, punishment-anticipation) are removed (M01-B, F, G); and the freedom from fear-of-harm is the mark of the redeemed condition (M01-D, E restoration corpus). The cluster points consistently toward an eschatological state of purified, universal, undistorted fear of God — and freedom from every other fear. |
| M01-A | finding | M01-A is the most eschatologically oriented sub-group. Rev 11:18 (fearing God's name as the defining characteristic of those who receive reward at the final judgment); Rev 14:7 (fearing God commanded in view of "the hour of his judgment" — an eschatological framing); Rev 15:4 (fearing the Lord portrayed as "the universal, inevitable response to his holiness and revealed righteous acts" — eschatological universalisation of reverential fear); Rev 19:5 (fearing God as the defining characteristic of his servants called to praise him at the consummation). The fullness of M01-A is the eschatological state in which all creation — redeemed humanity, living creatures, the nations — fears God in unified reverential worship. |
| M01-B | finding | M01-B's eschatological orientation is the freedom from all disordering fear: Rev 2:10 (M01-B-VCG-06/F-VCG-05: commanded not to fear the coming suffering — the faithful endurance through eschatological trial); Luk 21:26 (M01-B-VCG-03: cosmic signs producing fainting from fear — eschatological fear as the context for the "do not be frightened" commands of Luk 21:9 anchor). |
| M01-D | finding | M01-D's eschatological direction is the promise of no-more-dismay: Jer 30:10 (anchor D-VCG-04: "dismay is the inner collapse God forbids Israel to experience — the assurance of salvation and quiet rest is set as the direct antidote"); eschatological fullness as the state of undismayed composure grounded in God's salvation. |
| M01-E | finding | M01-E-VCG-03/04 show eschatological promise through the restoration corpus: Eze 34:28 (M01-E-VCG-03: "none shall make them afraid" — the restored flock free from fear-trembling); Mic 4:4 (anchor E-VCG-04: "no one will make anyone afraid — the ideal future is one where the inner person is wholly free from the threat-driven dread that now afflicts them"). |
| M01-F | finding | M01-F's eschatological direction: Heb 2:15 (Christ's deliverance from lifelong fear-of-death slavery — an eschatological liberation from the most pervasive form of chronic dread); 1Jo 4:18 (perfect love casting out fear — the fullness of M01-F's resolution is the love-perfected state in which no punishment-anticipatory fear remains). |
| M01-G | finding | M01-G's eschatological direction: Rev 21:8 (cowardice leading to the lake of fire — the negative eschatological terminus of sustained timidity); by contrast, the positive is the faithfulness that characterises the redeemed (Rev 11:18; 19:5 — the God-fearers, not the cowards, receive the eschatological reward). |

### T5.6.2  ·  Tier T5

> What does the present experience of this characteristic anticipate about its future fullness?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | Each present experience of ordered fear anticipates the fullness of that fear's eschatological form. Each present deliverance from disordered fear anticipates the fullness of that deliverance. The cluster's present evidence is consistently anticipatory — it describes a movement whose destination is clear. |
| M01-A | finding | The present experience of reverential fear of God (M01-A) anticipates the eschatological state in which that fear is universal (Rev 15:4: "fearing the Lord portrayed as the universal, inevitable response to his holiness and revealed righteous acts" — every creature responding as the God-fearer now does in part). The present partial and contested experience of the reverential posture anticipates a future uncontested, universal, perfected version of the same posture. |
| M01-F | finding | The present experience of deliverance from anxiety (Psa 34:4; Isa 12:2) anticipates the fullness in which perfect love has entirely expelled fear of punishment (1Jo 4:18). The partial deliverances the verse evidence documents are provisional forms of the final state in which no fear of condemnation remains. |

### T5.6.3  ·  Tier T5

> If the evidence is silent on eschatological trajectory, note this explicitly.

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| M01-C | finding | M01-C (terror-as-force) has a limited eschatological trajectory that is primarily negative: the Ezekiel 32 corpus (M01-C-VCG-03) shows terror stripped from empire in death — the eschaton as the end of terror-as-domination. This is the eschatological fullness of M01-C: no more terror wielded by human empires. The evidence is present but thin relative to M01-A's robust eschatological corpus. |

### T5.7.1  ·  Tier T5

> Where T2.8 has identified a constitutional deposit from sustained operation of this characteristic, what developmental consequence does that deposit produce over time?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | silent | T2.8 found the verse evidence across all M01 sub-groups silent on constitutional deposit in the body. The nearest evidence was M01-F's "lifelong inner slavery" (Heb 2:15) and the covenantal-curse dread (Deu 28:66-67) — but these describe a settled condition of bondage rather than a constitutional bodily deposit. T5.7 closes without a developmental-consequence finding because T2.8 found no deposit to trace forward. This is an expected finding given M01's nature as a primarily inner-being characteristic whose bodily dimension is expressive rather than deposit-forming. |

### T5.7.2  ·  Tier T5

> Does the evidence indicate generational consequence — a deposit carried forward beyond the individual?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | silent | The verse evidence does not evidence generational biological/constitutional deposit from M01. The generational effects are covenantal (Psa 103:17) and pedagogical (Deu 31:12-13), not physical inheritance. |
| M01-A | finding | M01-A shows generational consequence of a formational rather than constitutional kind. Psa 103:17 (God's steadfast love runs "to those who fear him across generations" — the covenantal benefit of the fear-posture extends generationally); Deu 31:13 (children being formed in fear of the Lord — the characteristic transmitted pedagogically, not biologically). The generational consequence is formational transmission, not constitutional deposit. |

### T5.7.3  ·  Tier T5

> If T2.8 found no deposit, note this explicitly and close T5.7.

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | silent | T2.8 found no constitutional deposit in the body. T5.7 is closed. The generational dimension of M01 is formational (fear transmitted through instruction and community) and covenantal (God's faithfulness extending across generations to those who fear him) rather than constitutional-biological. |

### T6.1.1  ·  Tier T6

> Which adjacent characteristics appear most frequently alongside this one in the verse evidence?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The most prominent co-occurrence patterns across M01 are: wisdom with fear-of-God (M01-A, extremely frequent); faith/trust as M01-B's opposite; trembling as M01-B's and D's somatic companion; shame as M01-D's judicial companion. The most structurally significant co-occurrence is M01-A with wisdom — so consistent and so central that the two characteristics are almost definitionally linked (Pro 1:7 makes this definitional: fear of the Lord IS the beginning of wisdom). |
| M01-A | finding | The characteristics most consistently co-occurring with M01-A reverential fear across the verse evidence are: (1) **wisdom** — Pro 1:7; 9:10; Psa 111:10; Job 28:28 (fear and wisdom paired as foundation and fruit across the Proverbs and wisdom Psalms corpora — extremely frequent co-occurrence); (2) **obedience / faithful conduct** — Deu 6:2; 8:6; 10:12; 2Ch 19:9; Col 3:22 (fear paired with walking in God's ways, keeping commandments, and faithful service — throughout the Deuteronomic corpus and NT); (3) **trust / confidence** — Pro 14:26; Psa 112:7-8; 1Sa 12:24 (fear of the Lord paired with trust in God and settled confidence, not anxiety); (4) **humility** — Pro 15:33; 22:4 (fear paired with humility as the dispositional ground of honour and blessing); (5) **love of God** — Deu 10:12-13 (… |
| M01-B | finding | M01-B acute fear co-occurs most frequently with: (1) **flight / protective action** — Gen 32:7; 1Ki 1:50; Jer 26:21 (fear driving immediate volitional action); (2) **trembling** (M01-E terms) — 1Sa 28:5 (fear and heart-trembling paired); Heb 12:21 (fear and trembling at Sinai — M01-B and E co-occurring in the same verse); (3) **faith / trust** as its structural opposite — Mar 4:40; Luk 8:50; Mar 5:36 (fear and faith paired as inner opposites). |
| M01-D | finding | M01-D dismay co-occurs with: (1) **shame** — Isa 37:27; Jer 48:20; Jer 50:36 (dismay and shame paired as co-consequences of judgment); (2) **trembling** (M01-E) — Jer 30:5 (trembling and dismay in the same panic-cry); (3) **bodily collapse** — Dan 5:6 (color change, limb-failure as the somatic co-occurrence of dismay). |
| M01-F | finding | M01-F anticipatory dread co-occurs with: (1) **grief / sorrow** — 2Cor 7:5 (fear within alongside external conflicts — fear and anguish co-present); (2) **faith as opposite** — 1Jo 4:18 (fear and perfect love as structural opposites — the absence of one implies the presence of the other). |

### T6.1.2  ·  Tier T6

> What does the pattern of co-occurrence reveal about this characteristic's place in the inner-being landscape?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The co-occurrence pattern places M01 in a structurally central position in the inner-being landscape: reverential fear (M01-A) is adjacent to and foundational for wisdom, obedience, humility, and trust. Disordered fear (M01-B's social register, M01-F, G) is adjacent to and opposed by faith/trust and love. The cluster occupies a pivotal position — ordered fear enables the full range of positive inner-being characteristics; disordered fear suppresses them. |
| M01-A | finding | M01-A's co-occurrence with wisdom, obedience, humility, trust, and love reveals that reverential fear of God is a foundational characteristic — it is the ground from which these others grow. The direction of the co-occurrence is consistently: fear as ground, wisdom/obedience/humility/trust as fruit. This places M01-A at the deep structural layer of the inner-being landscape rather than as one among many equal characteristics. |

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |

M01-E co-occurs with M01-B and M01-D (trembling is the somatic companion of both) but does not have a specific adjacent characteristic relationship beyond the fear cluster itself. |
| M01-E | silent | M01-C (terror-as-force) and M01-E (trembling) have less distinct co-occurrence patterns beyond their own internal sub-group dynamics. M01-E co-occurs with M01-B and M01-D (trembling is the somatic companion of both) but does not have a specific adjacent characteristic relationship beyond the fear cluster itself. |

### T6.2.1  ·  Tier T6

> Does the verse evidence show this characteristic consistently preceding, following, or accompanying another characteristic in a sequence?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The cluster's primary sequences are: perceptive encounter → acute fear → volitional response (M01-B); fear of God → wisdom/ethics (M01-A); catastrophic stimulus → dismay → bodily collapse (M01-D). These sequences are consistent and directional across the evidence. |
| M01-A | finding | M01-A consistently **precedes** wisdom and knowledge as their epistemological root: Pro 1:7; 9:10; Psa 111:10; Job 28:28 (fear is the beginning — it comes before wisdom as its precondition). Fear of God also **precedes** ethical conduct: Lev 19:14 (fear producing ethical restraint — the fear is prior, the conduct is consequent). M01-A is causally prior in the sequences it participates in. |
| M01-B | finding | M01-B's acute fear **follows** perceptive encounter (sight/hearing of threat or divine power) and **precedes** volitional response (flight, submission, worship, or paralysis). The sequence is: perceptive trigger → acute fear → volitional response. This is consistent across M01-B's corpus. |
| M01-D | finding | M01-D dismay **follows** catastrophic news or overwhelming encounter and **precedes** bodily collapse: the sequence is: overwhelming stimulus → inner dismay → somatic expression (color change, limb-failure, speechlessness). Dan 5:6; 7:28 (M01-D-VCG-03) demonstrate this sequence explicitly. |

### T6.2.2  ·  Tier T6

> What does the sequence reveal — is the relationship causal, developmental, or correlational?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The sequential relationships in M01 are primarily **causal** rather than merely correlational or developmental. Fear of God causes wisdom; encounter causes acute fear; overwhelming stimulus causes dismay; dismay causes bodily collapse. The cluster is characterised by causal chains running through the volitional and perceptive faculties. |
| M01-A | finding | The M01-A → wisdom sequence is **causal and constitutive**: Pro 1:7 establishes that without fear of the Lord the mind is disoriented (fools "despise wisdom" in the same verse). The relationship is not merely correlational but constitutional — wisdom requires fear of God as its epistemological ground. |
| M01-B | finding | The encounter → M01-B → volitional response sequence is **causal**: the fear is the direct causal result of the perceptive encounter, and the volitional response is the direct causal result of the fear. The chain is causal at both joints. |
| M01-D | finding | The stimulus → M01-D → bodily collapse sequence is **causal**: the overwhelming stimulus causes the inner dismay which produces the somatic expression. Dan 7:28 ("dismay works through Daniel's thoughts and changes his color" — thought-disruption as the causal intermediary between stimulus and somatic expression). |

> If no sequential pattern is evidenced, note this explicitly.

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| M01-C | silent | M01-C (terror-as-force) and M01-G (timidity) do not have clearly documented sequential relationships with adjacent characteristics in the verse evidence beyond their own internal dynamics. |
| M01-G | silent | M01-C (terror-as-force) and M01-G (timidity) do not have clearly documented sequential relationships with adjacent characteristics in the verse evidence beyond their own internal dynamics. |

### T6.3.1  ·  Tier T6

> Does this characteristic produce another characteristic in the verse evidence — and if so, which one, and by what mechanism?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | M01-A is the most productive sub-group: reverential fear produces wisdom, ethical conduct, life, confidence, and covenant intimacy. M01-B in its disordering register produces flight, deception, and silence; in its awe-register produces worship and proclamation. M01-D produces bodily collapse and paralysis. M01-G produces inaction and apostasy. |
| M01-A | finding | M01-A reverential fear produces: (1) **wisdom** — Pro 1:7; 9:10 (fear as the productive root of genuine knowledge and understanding); (2) **ethical conduct / conscientiousness** — Lev 19:14; Neh 5:15 (fear producing just, restrained conduct by the mechanism of interior moral governance); (3) **life** — Pro 10:27; 19:23 (fear producing longevity and restful satisfaction — by the mechanism of right ordering of the inner life); (4) **confidence / trust** — Pro 14:26 (fear functioning as "an inner foundation of strong confidence, not anxiety" — the mechanism is fear's displacement of anxious uncertainty with grounded divine-presence awareness); (5) **covenant intimacy** — Psa 25:14; Psa 103:11-13 (fear positioning the person to receive God's friendship and steadfast love — by the mechanism of… |
| M01-B | finding | M01-B acute fear produces (in its disordering register): (1) **flight, deception, silence** — Gen 3:10 (fear producing hiding and deception); Joh 7:13 (fear producing speech-suppression); 1Sa 18:29 (fear hardening into sustained enmity). (In its awe-register): (2) **worship and proclamation** — Mat 9:8 (fear moving immediately into glorifying God); Jon 1:16 (fear becoming the ground of vows and sacrifice). |
| M01-D | finding | M01-D dismay produces: **bodily collapse** — Dan 5:6 (color change, limb-failure); **speechlessness** — Job 32:15; **paralysis of hands** — Eze 7:27. |
| M01-G | finding | M01-G timidity produces: **passive inaction** — Mat 25:25 (burying the talent); **apostasy** — Rev 21:8 (the coward in the lake of fire). |

### T6.3.2  ·  Tier T6

> Is this characteristic produced by another — and if so, which one?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The characteristics that produce M01 are: divine encounter and power (producing M01-A and B), wisdom formation (producing M01-A), God's own implantation (producing M01-A), covenant faithfulness violated (producing M01-F), and external threat (producing M01-B and C). The characteristic has both divine-origin and human-situational origins depending on the sub-group. |
| M01-A | finding | M01-A reverential fear is produced by: (1) **encounter with God's power** (Exo 14:31; Hag 1:12 — fear arising from witnessing divine acts — the encounter is the producing characteristic); (2) **wisdom formation / Torah-hearing** (Deu 14:23; 31:12-13 — wisdom formation producing fear through a cumulative process); (3) **divine implantation** (Jer 32:40 — God himself as the producer through direct action); (4) **forgiveness** (Psa 130:4: "God's forgiveness is the basis for being feared — the inner response of reverential fear is properly evoked not by terror alone but by the experience of divine grace and pardon" — forgiveness producing reverential awe as its inner consequence). |
| M01-F | finding | M01-F chronic anxiety is produced by: (1) **covenant unfaithfulness** — Deu 28:66-67 (anxiety as the direct consequence of covenant violation — unfaithfulness producing chronic dread as its curse); (2) **external threats** — Eze 12:18-19 (siege conditions producing pervasive anxiety). |

### T6.3.3  ·  Tier T6

> Is this characteristic a constituent element of another, or does another characteristic constitute part of this one?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | M01-A is constitutively linked to wisdom (as its root), to covenant faithfulness (as its relational ground), and to worship (as its affective expression). These relationships are constitutive, not merely correlational. |
| M01-A | finding | M01-A is a constituent element of: (1) **wisdom** — Pro 1:7 establishes fear as wisdom's beginning/foundation — it is constitutively included in wisdom as its root, though not identical to it; (2) **covenant faithfulness** — Mal 2:5 (Levi's covenant defined by reverential fear — the fear is constitutive of the covenant relationship, not merely its accompaniment). Additionally, M01-A has constituent elements within it: cognitive alignment (knowing God's greatness), volitional governance (choosing to maintain the posture), and affective reverence (the felt awe) are all constituents of the reverential fear itself. |
| M01-B | finding | M01-B's awe-register (B-VCG-02: fear at Jesus's miracles) is a constituent element of **worship** in those contexts: Mat 9:8 (fear moving immediately into glorifying God — the fear is the entry-point and a constituent element of the worship response). |
| M01-G | finding | M01-G timidity is constituted in part by the absence of the spirit of power and love (2Ti 1:7) — the characteristic is constituted by the privation of what God gives. Courage (the spirit of power and self-control) is the constitutive positive of which timidity is the absence. |

> If no causal or constitutive relationship is evidenced, note this explicitly.

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| M01-C | silent | M01-C (terror-as-force) and M01-E (trembling) do not have documented causal or constitutive relationships with adjacent characteristics outside the fear cluster itself beyond what is evidenced in T6.1-6.2 above. |
| M01-E | silent | M01-C (terror-as-force) and M01-E (trembling) do not have documented causal or constitutive relationships with adjacent characteristics outside the fear cluster itself beyond what is evidenced in T6.1-6.2 above. |

### T6.4.1  ·  Tier T6

> Does this characteristic share vocabulary terms with other characteristics in the programme?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The cluster shares its core vocabulary (ya.re, yir.ah, fobos, fobeō, pa.chad) internally across all sub-groups. The shared vocabulary reflects the cluster's unity — all sub-groups are instances of the same fundamental characteristic family, not unrelated characteristics grouped by topic. |
| M01-A | finding | M01-A's primary terms (ya.re, yir.ah, pa.chad, fobeō, fobos) are shared with M01-B, C, D, E, F, G — these terms span the entire cluster. Within the programme more broadly: (1) **fobeō / fobos** are used in contexts that will be classified under other programme clusters (e.g. fobos in 2Cor 7:11 also appears in contexts adjacent to guilt/contrition — M10); (2) **pa.chad** (H6343) is the term used in M01-A-VCG-06 Gen 31:42 as a divine name ("Fear of Isaac") and appears across M01-B, C, E, F — extensive shared vocabulary within the cluster. The programme will identify cross-cluster term sharing when adjacent clusters (M10 Guilt, M02 Anger, M03 Grief) are analysed. |
| M01-B | finding | M01-B shares vocabulary with M01-E (the trembling terms appear in both — cha.rad appears in both B-VCG-01 and E-VCG-04) and with M01-A (ya.re appears across both). M01-B's Greek intensifiers (ekthambeo, ekfobos, emfobos) are specific to theophanic/encounter fear contexts and may be unique to M01-B within the programme. |

### T6.4.2  ·  Tier T6

> Does vocabulary sharing extend to root-level architecture — a shared root that generates terms across two or more characteristics?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The shared root architecture confirms that the cluster is linguistically unified at the root level. The characteristic is not a collection of semantically unrelated terms but a multi-form expression of a single root (or a small set of closely related roots) that generate vocabulary across every aspect of the fear-phenomenon. |
| M01-A | finding | Yes. The Hebrew root ירא (ya.re) generates: the verb ya.re (to fear/revere), the noun yir.ah (fear/reverence), and the adjective ya.re (fearing/reverent). ### T6.4.3  ·  Tier T6

> What does vocabulary sharing reveal about the conceptual relationship between characteristics?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The vocabulary sharing within M01 reveals that its sub-groups are facets of a single characteristic rather than independent phenomena. The same root generates the reverential posture of M01-A, the acute alarm of M01-B, the divine-name formula of M01-A-VCG-06, and the commanded-release corpus of M01-B-VCG-06. This root-level unity is itself a theological datum: Scripture uses a single vocabulary family to span from "fear of God as the whole duty of man" (Ecc 12:13) to "fear of the enemy before battle" (Deu 20:1) — implying that these are not separate inner experiences but related expressions of a constitutively unified characteristic. |

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| M01-G | finding | M01-G's primary vocabulary (deilia, deiliaō, deilos) is not shared with other M01 sub-groups. These terms are unique to the evaluative-timidity register and do not appear in M01-A through F. This vocabulary isolation confirms that M01-G is the sub-group most distinct from the others — it carries the evaluative moral charge that the other sub-groups' vocabulary does not. |

### T6.5.1  ·  Tier T6

> Which adjacent characteristic most closely resembles this one — and what precisely distinguishes them?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | Within M01 itself, the nearest-neighbour pairs are: A/F (dispositional vs. anticipatory), B/E (inner fear/somatic expression), D/E (dissolution vs. trembling). Across the programme's broader landscape, the nearest neighbour to M01-A (reverential fear of God) is likely M18 (Awe/Wonder) if such a cluster is designated — the distinction being that M01-A is specifically relational (directed toward God in covenant posture) while M18's awe may be more broadly generated. |
| M01-A | finding | [E] M01-A's nearest neighbour within the programme is **reverence / awe** (if separately classified) and **trust / faith** (as the complement that fear-of-God enables). The distinction from trust: reverential fear is the *posture* that grounds right relationship with God; trust is the *reliance* that flows from it. Fear and trust coexist and are mutually enabling (Psa 112:7-8; Psa 115:11) but are analytically distinct — fear names the posture of creaturely asymmetry before God; trust names the reliance that the security of that relationship produces. --- [E] M01-A (reverential fear) and M01-F (anticipatory dread) are nearest neighbours on the temporal axis. The distinction: M01-A is a stable dispositional orientation; M01-F is a forward-looking affective condition. Fear-of-God in M01-A pr… |
| M01-B | finding | M01-B (acute fear) and M01-E (trembling) are nearest neighbours. The distinction: M01-B is primarily an inner-state with volitional consequences; M01-E is primarily the somatic expression of that inner state. They co-occur (1Sa 28:5: fear in the heart and trembling paired) but are analytically distinct: M01-B is the inner fear-event; M01-E is the body's registration of it. |
| M01-D | finding | M01-D (dismay) and M01-E (trembling) are nearest neighbours in the somatic register. The distinction: M01-D is the dissolution of inner coherence (the shattering, not the shaking); M01-E is the bodily trembling that registers the fear. Dismay collapses function; trembling expresses the inner state while function remains (partially) intact. |
| M01-E | finding | [E] M01-B (acute fear) and M01-E (trembling) are nearest neighbours. The distinction: M01-B is primarily an inner-state with volitional consequences; M01-E is primarily the somatic expression of that inner state. They co-occur (1Sa 28:5: fear in the heart and trembling paired) but are analytically distinct: M01-B is the inner fear-event; M01-E is the body's registration of it. --- [E] M01-D (dismay) and M01-E (trembling) are nearest neighbours in the somatic register. The distinction: M01-D is the dissolution of inner coherence (the shattering, not the shaking); M01-E is the bodily trembling that registers the fear. Dismay collapses function; trembling expresses the inner state while function remains (partially) intact. |
| M01-F | finding | M01-A (reverential fear) and M01-F (anticipatory dread) are nearest neighbours on the temporal axis. The distinction: M01-A is a stable dispositional orientation; M01-F is a forward-looking affective condition. Fear-of-God in M01-A produces confidence (Pro 14:26); anxiety in M01-F colonises the inner life with dread. They can involve the same vocabulary (pa.chad appears in both) but are constitutively distinct in their inner-person operation. |

### T6.5.2  ·  Tier T6

> Where the evidence shows apparent overlap, what is the precise boundary?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The precise boundaries within M01 are: dispositional vs. episodic (A/B), somatic expression vs. inner dissolution (E/D), anticipatory vs. dispositional (F/A). These boundaries are not arbitrary but are grounded in the verse evidence's own discriminations. |
| M01-A | finding | The overlap between M01-A (reverential fear) and M01-B (acute fear) is considerable — the same vocabulary (ya.re, fobos) appears in both. The precise boundary is dispositional vs. episodic: M01-A is a settled governing orientation that does not require a triggering event; M01-B is triggered by a specific stimulus and resolves when the stimulus is addressed or the person is reassured. Exo 20:20 (Moses distinguishing "panic-fear: do not fear" from "reverential fear: God intends it to stay before them as a moral restraint") is the clearest biblical statement of this boundary. |
| M01-B | finding | The overlap between M01-A (reverential fear) and M01-B (acute fear) is considerable — the same vocabulary (ya.re, fobos) appears in both. The precise boundary is dispositional vs. episodic: M01-A is a settled governing orientation that does not require a triggering event; M01-B is triggered by a specific stimulus and resolves when the stimulus is addressed or the person is reassured. Exo 20:20 (Moses distinguishing "panic-fear: do not fear" from "reverential fear: God intends it to stay before them as a moral restraint") is the clearest biblical statement of this boundary. |
| M01-D | finding | The overlap between M01-E (trembling) and M01-D (dismay) is that both involve somatic and inner disruption. The precise boundary: M01-E's trembling is the body's registering of the inner state while the person may still be functioning; M01-D's dismay is the dissolution of function itself. 1Sa 28:5 (Saul's heart trembling — M01-E) versus 1Sa 28:20 (Saul prostrate, unable to eat, strength all gone — M01-D) shows the same person moving from trembling (E) to collapse (D) as the dismay deepens. |
| M01-E | finding | The overlap between M01-E (trembling) and M01-D (dismay) is that both involve somatic and inner disruption. The precise boundary: M01-E's trembling is the body's registering of the inner state while the person may still be functioning; M01-D's dismay is the dissolution of function itself. 1Sa 28:5 (Saul's heart trembling — M01-E) versus 1Sa 28:20 (Saul prostrate, unable to eat, strength all gone — M01-D) shows the same person moving from trembling (E) to collapse (D) as the dismay deepens. |

### T6.5.3  ·  Tier T6

> Is the distinction between this characteristic and its nearest neighbour one of degree, kind, direction, or constitutional level?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The internal sub-group distinctions are primarily of **kind** (dispositional vs. episodic; somatic vs. inner; ordered vs. disordered) with secondary distinctions of **degree** (intensity within a kind) and **direction** (God-directed vs. threat-directed vs. anticipatory). |
| M01-A | finding | [E] The distinction between M01-A and M01-B is one of **kind**: M01-A is a dispositional orientation (a quality of the person's inner life); M01-B is an episodic condition (an event that occurs and passes). The distinction is not merely of degree (more vs. less fear) but of constitutional type (stable characteristic vs. acute event). --- [E] The distinction between M01-A and M01-F is one of **kind and direction**: M01-A is a stable, God-directed disposition; M01-F is a forward-oriented, threat-directed burden. Same vocabulary family; different constitutional operation. |
| M01-B | finding | The distinction between M01-A and M01-B is one of **kind**: M01-A is a dispositional orientation (a quality of the person's inner life); M01-B is an episodic condition (an event that occurs and passes). The distinction is not merely of degree (more vs. less fear) but of constitutional type (stable characteristic vs. acute event). |
| M01-D | finding | The distinction between M01-E and M01-D is one of **degree** (trembling while functioning vs. trembling as part of collapse) and **kind** (somatic expression vs. inner dissolution). The distinction has both a degree component and a kind component. |
| M01-E | finding | The distinction between M01-E and M01-D is one of **degree** (trembling while functioning vs. trembling as part of collapse) and **kind** (somatic expression vs. inner dissolution). The distinction has both a degree component and a kind component. |
| M01-F | finding | The distinction between M01-A and M01-F is one of **kind and direction**: M01-A is a stable, God-directed disposition; M01-F is a forward-oriented, threat-directed burden. Same vocabulary family; different constitutional operation. |
