### T7.1.1  ·  Tier T7

> What are the primary Hebrew and Greek terms for this characteristic — and what do their root meanings reveal?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The cluster's primary Hebrew terms are: ya.re / yir.ah (the broadest fear root, spanning reverential to acute), pa.chad / pach.dah (dread with intensity), mo.rah / mo.ra (the fear-inspiring quality), ba.hal / cha.tat (dismay/shattering), cha.rad / ra.gaz (trembling), and de.a.gah (anxiety/worry). The primary Greek terms are: fobeō / fobos (the dominant NT fear vocabulary), the ek-/em- intensifier compounds (extreme encounter fear), tromos / entromos (trembling), deilia / deilos (evaluated timidity), and foberos (fearful as an objective quality of the object). The term inventory confirms the cluster's broad semantic range across the fear-spectrum. |
| M01-A | finding | The primary M01-A terms and their root meanings: (1) **ya.re (H3372G, H3372H, H3373)** — root meaning: to fear, to be afraid, to stand in awe. The same root generates the stative verb (to be in a state of fear/reverence), nominal form, and adjective. Stative root significance: the characteristic is a state of being, not primarily an act — it is what the person is, not only what the person does. (2) **yir.ah (H3374)** — nominal form of the ya.re root: "the fear" as a possessed quality, a stable disposition. (3) **pa.chad (H6343)** — root meaning: to dread, to tremble in dread. Derived from a root suggesting the quaking that accompanies overwhelming encounter. (4) **pach.dah (H6345)** — a feminine noun from the pa.chad root — "dread" as a named inner state. (5) **mo.rah / mo.ra (H4172A, H41… |
| M01-B | finding | M01-B's distinctive primary terms: (1) **de.chal (H1763, Aramaic)** — dread, terror in visionary contexts (Dan 2:31 anchor). (2) **za.chal (H2119B)** — to shrink back, crawl in fear (Mic 7:17 anchor — nations crawling out in fearful retreat). (3) **ya.gor (H3016)** — to be afraid of a specific object, anticipatory object-directed dread. (4) **ra.hah (H7297)** — to be afraid, in a specific Isaianic context. (5) **ekthambeo (G1568), ekthambos (G1569)** — to be greatly amazed/alarmed; the ek- prefix intensifies the thambeo root (amazement/astonishment) — extreme awe-shock. (6) **ekfobos (G1630)** — frightened out of one's senses; extreme terror. (7) **emfobos (G1719)** — in a state of fear; afraid, trembling within. (8) **ptoeō (G4422), ptoēsis (G4423), pturomai (G4426)** — roots meaning to … |
| M01-C | finding | M01-C's distinctive terms: (1) **e.mah (H0367)** — terror as an overwhelming force; derived from a root suggesting the effect of dread rather than the feeling itself. (2) **bal.la.hah (H1091)** — sudden terror, consternation; from a root of hasty, overwhelming onset. (3) **chit.tah (H2847)** — terror that paralyzes; related to cha.tat (dismay). (4) **chit.tit (H2851)** — the terror projected by military power; a technical term for the radiating dread of empire. (5) **ma.gor (H4032)** — from a root meaning to sojourn as a stranger, hence the terror of the homeless/unsafe — encircling dread with no refuge. (6) **me.chit.tah (H4288)** — terror/ruin as an instrument of destruction. |
| M01-D | finding | M01-D's distinctive terms: (1) **ba.hal (H0926)** — to dismay, alarm, agitate; root meaning sudden, overwhelming disruption — the term uniquely covers both inner shock and the hasty rashness that follows. (2) **be.hal (H0927, Aramaic)** — the Aramaic cognate, dominant in Daniel. (3) **cha.tat (H2865)** — to be dismayed, shattered; from a root of breaking, shattering — the image is of an inner vessel broken. (4) **tim.ma.hon (H8541)** — bewilderment, confusion of mind; from a root of astonishment leading to cognitive disorientation. |
| M01-E | finding | M01-E's distinctive terms: (1) **cha.rad (H2729)** — to tremble, quake; a bodily root. (2) **cha.red (H2730)** — the trembling one/trembling posture — a qualitative adjective describing the person defined by trembling reverence. (3) **cha.ra.dah (H2731)** — trembling as a noun — "the great trembling." (4) **ra.gaz (H7264)** — to tremble, quake, be agitated — a broader term covering both inner agitation and outward trembling. (5) **ra.ad (H7460, H7461A, H7461B)** — to tremble, shudder — specifically the shaking motion. (6) **sa.ar (H8175A, H8178A)** — to shudder, to bristle (as in hair standing on end) — a visceral somatic reaction. (7) **pal.la.tsut (H6427)** — shuddering, horror-trembling. (8) **entromos (G1790)** — trembling, in a state of trembling; compound of en- (in) + tromos (tremb… |
| M01-F | finding | M01-F's distinctive terms: (1) **de.a.gah (H1674)** — anxiety, worry; from a root suggesting cognitive engagement with something painful — the worry/anxiety that circles around a concern. (2) **ya.gor (H3025)** — to fear, dread in an anticipatory mode; distinct from the M01-B ya.gor (H3016) by a different root grouping — here the anticipatory-dread sense is primary. (3) **me.go.rah (H4034), me.gu.rah (H4035)** — fear as something harboured within the person — an inner terror lodged and held. (4) **foberos (G5398)** — fearful, dreadful; specifically the fearful expectation of judgment (Heb 10:27 anchor) — the adjective form used to describe divine judgment as the object of dread. |
| M01-G | finding | M01-G's distinctive terms: (1) **deilia (G1167)** — timidity, cowardice; a Greek moral-ethical term with evaluative weight — the opposite of andreia (courage/manliness in Greek ethics). (2) **deiliaō (G1168)** — to be timid, to be cowardly. (3) **deilos (G1169)** — cowardly, fainthearted — the adjective used in Jesus's evaluation of the disciples' storm-fear (Mat 8:26; Mar 4:40) and in Rev 21:8. |

### T7.1.10  ·  Tier T7

> What does the full vocabulary arc reveal about this characteristic's complete semantic range?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The full vocabulary arc of M01 — from ya.re / yir.ah / pa.chad (Hebrew) through fobeō / fobos / deilia / ekthambeo (Greek) — reveals that fear as described in Scripture spans a complete semantic range from: (1) the reverential inner disposition of the God-fearer (M01-A) — the highest, most ordered form; (2) the acute alarm of the person before overwhelming threat or divine encounter (M01-B) — situational, involuntary, episodic; (3) the overwhelming force of terror deployed against enemies (M01-C) — terror as a weapon with agency; (4) the shattering inner collapse of dismay (M01-D) — the person undone; (5) the body's involuntary trembling in registering fear or reverence (M01-E) — the somatic pole of the characteristic; (6) the chronic burden of anticipatory dread (M01-F) — fear extended f… |

### T7.1.2  ·  Tier T7

> What is the grammatical range of the primary term (noun, verb, adjective, participle) — and what does that range reveal about how the characteristic operates?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The grammatical range across M01 reveals: stative verbs and nouns cluster in the dispositional sub-groups (M01-A, G); aorist and event verbs cluster in the episodic sub-groups (M01-B, C); passive Niphal forms cluster in the experience-of-imposition sub-groups (M01-D: "to be dismayed/shattered"). The participle as character-defining form appears in M01-A (ya.re — the God-fearer) and M01-E-VCG-02 (cha.red — the one who trembles at God's word) and M01-G (deilos — the cowardly one). Grammar confirms the dispositional vs. episodic distinction structurally. |
| M01-A | finding | The primary M01-A term ya.re functions as: **verb** (ya.re — to fear/revere, stative; the ongoing state of being in fear/reverence), **noun** (yir.ah — the fear as a possessed quality), and **adjective / participle** (ya.re — the one who fears; Job 1:1: "a man who feared God" — the present participle as a character-defining description). This grammatical range reveals that the characteristic operates as: a state of being (stative verb), a stable possession of the person (noun), and a defining character quality (participle). The stative verbal form is especially significant: ya.re describes an ongoing state rather than a completed action, confirming that M01-A is dispositional rather than episodic. |
| M01-B | finding | M01-B's Greek terms: fobeō functions as a verb (episodic — "feared, was afraid") and fobos as a noun. The verb form in M01-B contexts is predominantly aorist or imperfect (completed past or ongoing past event) rather than the present participle (defining quality). This grammatical pattern confirms M01-B as episodic rather than dispositional. |
| M01-D | finding | M01-D's ba.hal functions as a Piel verb (intensive action stem in Hebrew — the characteristic is intensive, not gentle), and cha.tat functions as a Niphal (passive — "to be dismayed, to be shattered") — confirming that dismay is something that happens to the person rather than something they do. |
| M01-E | finding | M01-E's cha.rad functions as a Qal verb (basic stem, often reflexive in context — the body naturally trembles), cha.red as a Qal participle / adjective (the trembling one — character description), and cha.ra.dah as a noun (the trembling as an event). The participle form cha.red (Isa 66:2 anchor: "the one who trembles at my word") functions as a character-defining description, confirming that the trembling-at-word tradition (E-VCG-02) is dispositional like M01-A. |
| M01-G | finding | M01-G's Greek terms (deilia, deiliaō, deilos) are predominantly: noun (deilia — the quality of timidity), verb (deiliaō — to be timid), and adjective (deilos — the cowardly one). The adjective deilos is used in evaluative character-judgments (Mat 8:26; Rev 21:8) — it describes what the person is, not merely what they experience. |

### T7.1.3  ·  Tier T7

> What is the semantic range of the primary term — across what breadth of meaning does it operate?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The primary terms of M01 are semantically broad: ya.re spans reverential awe to cringing alarm; pa.chad spans covenant-name for God (Gen 31:42) to the dread of nocturnal terror (Psa 91:5); ra.gaz spans inner distress to cosmic earth-trembling. This semantic breadth reflects the cluster's genuine scope: fear in Scripture is not a narrow technical term but a broad characterisation of the person's oriented-response to power. |
| M01-A | finding | ya.re (H3372-3374) spans: (a) the reverential posture before God (the large majority of M01-A uses); (b) the acute alarm before threat (M01-B-VCG-03; M01-B-VCG-05 where ya.re terms appear with M01-B routing); (c) the reactive fear at unexpected events (Gen 28:17: Jacob afraid at the divine place); (d) the commanded prohibition of fear ("do not be afraid" — ya.re in M01-B-VCG-06 corpus). The semantic range is extremely broad — a single root covers the full spectrum from cringing alarm to the highest reverential posture of the worshipper. This breadth is itself analytically significant: Hebrew does not distinguish reverential fear from acute alarm at the root level; the distinction is contextual. **[Folded from wa_session_b_findings.id=67; finding_id=DIM-61-001; registry=fear]** fobeō (G539… |
| M01-E | finding | ra.gaz (H7264) spans: (a) trembling of persons in fear (M01-E-VCG-01, 04); (b) trembling of the earth in theophany (set aside — outside inner-being scope); (c) inner agitation and distress (2Sa 18:33: David's grief "shook his inner being violently"); (d) rousing/stirring to action (set aside uses). The semantic range covers bodily fear-trembling, inner agitation, and arousal to action — a broad root used across multiple registers. |

### T7.1.4  ·  Tier T7

> Does the vocabulary include terms that distinguish distinct aspects of this characteristic — disposition versus act, received versus given, condition versus quality?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The vocabulary makes distinctions between disposition (nominal forms: yir.ah, pa.chad, deilia), condition (stative verbal forms, passive Niphal forms: "to be dismayed"), and character-quality (participial/adjectival forms: ya.re, cha.red, deilos). These grammatical distinctions are analytically useful for the programme's classification work. |
| M01-A | finding | Yes, the M01 vocabulary makes these distinctions: (1) **disposition vs. act**: yir.ah (the noun — the possessed disposition) vs. ya.re (the stative verb — the ongoing state) vs. specific imperative uses ("fear the Lord" — the commanded act); (2) **condition vs. quality**: ba.hal (H0926) covers both the shocked condition (something that happens) and the rash-urgency quality (a pattern of response, in M01-D-VCG-05's Ecclesiastes corpus); (3) **disposition vs. quality**: cha.red (H2730 — the one who trembles, a character quality) vs. cha.rad (H2729 — the trembling event). The vocabulary across the cluster does distinguish dispositional, conditional, and quality aspects through its grammatical forms. |
| M01-G | finding | M01-G's deilia (noun — the quality/possession of timidity), deiliaō (verb — to exercise timidity), and deilos (adjective — the cowardly one) distinguish the quality from its exercise and from the person defined by it. |

### T7.1.5  ·  Tier T7

> Does the vocabulary include a term for the structural opposite or absence of this characteristic?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The cluster lacks a dedicated antonym vocabulary. The absence is expressed through negation ("no fear," "not afraid"), through commanded-against states ("do not fear"), and through named positive alternatives (trust, faith, love). This pattern is consistent with a characteristic whose primary expression is positive (the reverential orientation) and whose absence is expressed as a diagnostic failure rather than an achieved counter-state. |
| M01-A | finding | The M01 vocabulary does not include a dedicated antonym term. The structural opposites are expressed through: (1) **negative constructions** — "no fear of God before their eyes" (Psa 36:1; Rom 3:18); "do not fear" (the entire M01-B-VCG-06 corpus); "not afraid" (numerous instances); (2) **paired contrasting terms** — cha.tat in M01-D (dismay/shattering) is used in M01-D-VCG-04 as the opposite of composure and courage; (3) **positive opposites** — the vocabulary of trust (batach) and faith (emunah) function as the structural opposites of fear in multiple passages but are not M01 cluster terms. The absence of a dedicated antonym for reverential fear (other than through negative construction) is consistent with Hebrew vocabulary structure: the positive disposition is the norm, and its absence… |
| M01-G | finding | M01-G does have a specified positive opposite within the text: the spirit of power, love, and self-control (2Ti 1:7 anchor) is explicitly named as the opposite of timidity. The term deilia's opposite is implicitly andreia (courage) in the Greek ethical tradition, though this term does not appear in the M01 verse evidence. |

### T7.1.6  ·  Tier T7

> Does the vocabulary include a person-type term — a term for the one who habitually possesses or exercises this characteristic?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The cluster has a well-developed person-type vocabulary for M01-A (the God-fearer: ya.re / foboumenos) and a negative person-type for M01-G (deilos — the cowardly one). The existence of a recognised person-type category confirms that reverential fear is understood in Scripture as a defining character quality, not merely an episodic experience. |
| M01-A | finding | Yes, and prominently. The participial form **ya.re (H3373)** — "the one who fears (God)" — functions as a person-type term across M01-A-VCG-03 and VCG-06 extensively. Job 1:1 ("a man who feared God"), 1Ki 18:3 ("Obadiah feared the Lord greatly"), Neh 7:2, Mal 3:16 (those who feared the Lord), Act 10:2 (Cornelius "feared God"). The person-type term is formally "the God-fearer" (ya.re elohim / ya.re YHWH) — a recognised biblical category of person defined by this characteristic. In the NT, the "God-fearer" (foboumenos ton theon) is a recognised community category (Act 10:2, 22, 35; Act 13:16, 26). |
| M01-G | finding | M01-G has an implicit person-type: **deilos (G1169)** — the cowardly one. Used as a character-description in Mat 8:26 (Jesus calling the disciples timid) and Rev 21:8 (the cowardly as a person-category heading the list of the condemned). |

### T7.1.7  ·  Tier T7

> Does the vocabulary include a supplication or seeking term — a term for the act of seeking this characteristic from another?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | silent | The M01 vocabulary does not include a dedicated supplication or seeking term. The characteristic is formed through encounter, formation, and divine implantation rather than through explicit seeking-petition directed at the characteristic itself. |
| M01-A | silent | M01-A does not include a dedicated seeking term for reverential fear of God. The seeking pattern is indirect: Psa 34:11 (the psalmist offering to teach fear — the implied seeking is through receptive formation); Pro 2:5 (fear as the fruit of earnest seeking after wisdom — the seeking is of wisdom, the fruit of which is fear). No direct petitionary vocabulary for seeking the characteristic from God or another person is identified. |

### T7.1.8  ·  Tier T7

> What does the relationship between the OT Hebrew vocabulary and the NT Greek vocabulary reveal about continuity or development of this characteristic across the Testaments?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The OT → NT trajectory across M01 shows: (1) **Continuity** — the same dispositional reverential fear (ya.re/yir.ah → fobeō/fobos) operates across both Testaments; (2) **Christological development** — NT theophanies are Christ-theophanies, concentrating the fear-encounter vocabulary around Jesus's identity; (3) **Discriminatory development** — the NT develops the inner taxonomy of fear (servile/adoption, punishment-anticipatory/love-perfected) more explicitly than the OT; (4) **Evaluative vocabulary addition** — the Greek deilia-family provides a dedicated negative-evaluative vocabulary that the OT lacked. Overall: strong continuity of concept, development of inner discrimination, and christological intensification. |
| M01-A | finding | [E] M01-A shows substantial **continuity** across Testaments. The Greek **fobeō / fobos** translates the Hebrew **ya.re / yir.ah** consistently across the Septuagint and NT. The NT picks up the same dispositional usage: Col 3:22 (fearing the Lord as governing orientation for conduct — identical to Lev 19:14 and M01-A-VCG-01 usage); Heb 12:28 (reverence and awe as the fitting disposition for approaching God in worship — identical to the Psalms worship corpus); 1Pe 1:17; 2:17 (fear as governing posture for conduct in exile — identical to Deu 6:2 and M01-A-VCG-02 usage). The NT does not introduce a new concept but extends and deepens the OT's reverential fear vocabulary into the new-covenant context. --- [E] M01-A also shows **development** across Testaments. The NT introduces the tension be… |
| M01-B | finding | M01-B shows development in the NT through the **christological intensification** of theophanic fear: the disciples' fear at Jesus's miracles, transfiguration, and resurrection appearances (M01-B-VCG-01 and 02) use the same vocabulary (fobeō, fobos) as OT theophanies but now applied to the incarnate Son. The development is christological — the OT's ya.re at divine theophanies becomes fobeō at Christ's acts and presence. |
| M01-G | finding | M01-G shows development: the **Greek evaluative vocabulary** (deilia, deiliaō, deilos) is a distinctively NT contribution. The OT does not have an exact equivalent evaluative person-type term for the coward; the closest is the "fearful and fainthearted" soldier of Deu 20:8 (ya.re — the same root as reverential fear) and the "fear of man" (cha.ra.dah) of Pro 29:25. The NT's deilia-family provides a dedicated evaluative-negative vocabulary for timidity that the OT addressed through contextual usage of shared roots. |

### T7.1.9  ·  Tier T7

> Is there a term newly coined in the NT period for this characteristic — and if so, what does that coinage reveal?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The NT's distinctive coinages in M01 are: the ekthambeo / ekfobos compound-intensifiers (for christological encounter-fear) and the theological appropriation of deilia / deilos (for the evaluative-moral category of cowardly apostasy). Both reveal that the NT needed new or newly-deployed vocabulary to describe the intensity of the christological encounters and the seriousness of the failure of courage under pressure. |
| M01-B | finding | The NT's Greek compound intensifiers represent vocabulary newly coined or specifically deployed for the fear register in NT contexts: **ekthambeo (G1568), ekthambos (G1569), ekfobos (G1630)** — these ek- prefixed compound forms intensify the base fear-terms and appear specifically in the gospel literature describing reactions to Jesus's acts and presence. The ekthambeo root in particular appears to be used distinctively for the awe-shock produced by Jesus's supernatural acts (Mar 9:15 anchor: the crowd's amazement at seeing Jesus; Mar 14:33: Jesus himself ekthambeo in Gethsemane). The coinage of these intensified compound forms in the NT context reveals that the encounters with Jesus produced an intensity of awe-shock that the existing vocabulary of fobeō/fobos did not fully capture — a n… |
| M01-G | finding | The **deilia / deiliaō / deilos** vocabulary, while existing in classical Greek, is newly deployed in a theological-moral context in the NT. 2Ti 1:7's use of deilia as a named spirit-level disposition not from God, and Rev 21:8's use of deilos as the heading term for the condemned, represents a theological appropriation of the classical Greek ethical vocabulary into the NT's moral-spiritual framework. The coinage reveals that the NT treats timidity as a moral-theological category equivalent in seriousness to idolatry — an evaluation that goes beyond the classical Greek understanding. |

### T7.2.1  ·  Tier T7

> What is the function of this characteristic's primary term within its primary verse — what role does it play in the sentence and argument?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The primary terms function in their anchor verses as: subject/predicate nominative (constitutive definition — Pro 1:7), grounding imperative (theological basis for ethics — Lev 19:14), inner state pointing outward (christological evidence — Mar 4:41), causal inner event (producing somatic collapse — Dan 5:6), and contrast-term defining what God does not give (evaluative negation — 2Ti 1:7). The diversity of grammatical functions across anchor verses reflects the cluster's diversity of phenomenological registers. |
| M01-A | finding | [E] In Pro 1:7 (anchor M01-A-VCG-02): "The fear of the Lord is the beginning of knowledge; fools despise wisdom and instruction." The term yir.ah (fear of the Lord) functions as the **subject and predicate nominative** of the main clause — it IS the beginning of knowledge. The grammatical function is definitional and constitutive: the verse does not say fear leads to knowledge but that fear IS the beginning. This elevates fear from a precondition to a constitutive element. The contrast clause ("fools despise") makes the argument by antithesis: the absence of fear = despising wisdom = foolishness. The argument is: right inner orientation (fear) = knowledge; its absence = folly. --- [E] In Lev 19:14 (anchor M01-A-VCG-01): "You shall not curse the deaf or put a stumbling block before the bli… |
| M01-B | finding | In Mar 4:41 (anchor M01-B-VCG-02): "And they were filled with great fear and said to one another, 'Who then is this?'" The term fobos functions as the **content of their inner state** that produces the christological question. The fear functions argumentatively as the evidence that what they have witnessed exceeds natural categories — it is the inner-being sign that points toward Jesus's identity. |
| M01-D | finding | In Dan 5:6 (anchor M01-D-VCG-03): "Then the king's color changed, and his thoughts alarmed him; his limbs gave way, and his knees knocked together." The term be.hal (alarmed/dismayed) functions as the **verbal expression of the inner event** from which all somatic consequences flow — the be.hal of his thoughts produces the color change, the limb-failure, the knocking knees. The term is causal in the argument's logic. |
| M01-G | finding | In 2Ti 1:7 (anchor M01-G-VCG-01): "For God gave us a spirit not of fear but of power and love and self-control." The term deilia (fear/timidity) functions as the **named negative** in a contrast structure — God gave NOT this but THAT. The argument structure is: what God gives (positive triple) defined by contrast with what he does not give (deilia). The term carries the full evaluative weight of the sentence. |

### T7.2.2  ·  Tier T7

> What literary form carries the primary verse evidence (narrative, psalm, wisdom, prophecy, epistle, apocalyptic) — and what does that form require for responsible interpretation?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The cluster's evidence is distributed across all major biblical literary forms: wisdom, psalm, narrative, prophecy, apocalyptic, and epistle. This breadth is itself a finding: fear is not a genre-specific characteristic but one attested across the full literary range of Scripture. Responsible interpretation requires form-sensitive reading — treating wisdom axioms as universal principles, narrative events as specific instances, prophetic oracles within their covenant-address context, and epistolary instruction within its pastoral address. |
| M01-A | finding | M01-A's evidence is carried primarily by **wisdom literature** (Pro 1:7; 9:10; 14:26-27; 15:33; Job 28:28) and **psalm literature** (Psa 25:14; 34:7; 103:11-17; 111:10; 112:1). Wisdom form requires: reading as universal principle rather than historically contingent assertion; attending to the literary-wisdom genre's claim to describe the order embedded in creation; recognising that Proverbs' "fear of the Lord is the beginning of wisdom" is a wisdom axiom, not a narrative event. Psalm form requires: reading the psalmist's own experiential testimony as shaped by liturgical use; attending to the historical setting of specific psalms (individual lament, communal praise) while recognising their appropriation as generalisable patterns. |
| M01-B | finding | M01-B's evidence is carried primarily by **narrative** (OT: Gen, Exo, 1Sa, 2Ki corpus) and **gospel narrative** (NT: Mar, Luk, Mat, Joh — the miracle and resurrection stories). Narrative form requires: reading events as historically grounded particular instances rather than universal principles; attending to the narrative context and the characters' roles; recognising that narrative fear responses are descriptive (this is what happened) rather than prescriptive (this is what should happen), except where the narrator explicitly evaluates. |
| M01-C | finding | M01-C's evidence is carried primarily by **prophecy and apocalyptic** (Jer 20:10; Eze 32:23-32; Isa 19:17) and **narrative** (Gen 35:5; Exo 23:27). Prophetic form requires: attending to the oracular address (God speaking, "I will send my terror"), the historical addressees, and the eschatological horizon; recognising that prophetic deployment of terror is typically set within the covenant framework of divine governance. |
| M01-D | finding | M01-D's evidence is carried primarily by **psalm lament** (Psa 6:3; 30:7), **wisdom** (Job 4:5; 21:6; 23:15-16), and **Aramaic narrative** (Dan 4:5; 5:6; 7:15). Each form requires different interpretive care: lament psalms express experiential truth in hyperbolic emotional language; wisdom (Job) is dialogic and requires attending to the speaker (Job, friends, God — whose perspective is being expressed?); Daniel's Aramaic narrative requires attention to the visionary-apocalyptic genre. |
| M01-E | finding | M01-E's evidence is carried by **narrative** (Exo 19:16; 1Sa 28:5), **prophetic oracle** (Isa 66:2; Eze 26:16), and **NT epistle** (Phili 2:12; 1Cor 2:3; 2Cor 7:15). Epistolary form requires: reading as occasional correspondence addressed to specific communities; recognising that Paul's use of tromos/entromos is embedded in pastoral and parenetic contexts. |
| M01-F | finding | M01-F's evidence is carried by **legal/Deuteronomic corpus** (Deu 28:66-67), **psalm** (Psa 34:4; 94:19), **prophetic** (Eze 12:18-19), and **NT epistle** (Heb 2:15; 10:27; 1Jo 4:18; 2Cor 12:20). The legal corpus requires reading Deu 28 within the covenant-curse framework — the consequences are conditional on covenant violation, not universal psychological states. |
| M01-G | finding | M01-G's evidence is carried primarily by **NT epistle** (2Ti 1:7) and **apocalyptic** (Rev 21:8), with **gospel narrative** (Mat 8:26; Mat 25:25). Apocalyptic form (Rev 21:8) requires: attending to the genre's symbolic vision structure; recognising that the lake of fire is eschatological judgment, and the list of condemned types is not a sociological survey but an eschatological warning; the "cowardly" heading the list intensifies the evaluative charge. |

### T7.2.3  ·  Tier T7

> What is the logical structure of key arguments in the verse evidence — what are the premises and conclusions?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The cluster's key arguments share a common logical structure: they move from a theological premise (God's identity, God's character, God's act) through an inner-being response (reverential fear, acute alarm, commanded courage) to a practical or ontological conclusion (ethical conduct, covenant faithfulness, christological recognition, or eschatological judgment). The characteristic is consistently the pivotal middle term in these arguments. |
| M01-A | finding | [E] Pro 1:7 (anchor M01-A-VCG-02) logical structure: Premise 1: The fear of the Lord is the beginning of knowledge. Premise 2: Fools despise wisdom and instruction. Conclusion (implicit): Those who despise wisdom lack the fear of the Lord; those who have knowledge have its fear as its ground. The argument is a definition plus its negation — establishing the characteristic as constitutive by excluding its alternative. --- [E] Lev 19:14 (anchor M01-A-VCG-01) logical structure: Premise 1: You shall not exploit the vulnerable (deaf and blind). Grounding: You shall fear your God. Premise 2: I am the Lord (the identity that makes the fear meaningful). Conclusion: The ethical prohibition is grounded in the divine relationship, not in consequentialist reasoning or social accountability. The argum… |
| M01-B | finding | Mar 4:41 (anchor M01-B-VCG-02) narrative argument: Premises (narrative): Jesus has commanded the wind and sea and they obeyed. The disciples observe this. Inner response: They are filled with great fear. Conclusion (question): "Who then is this?" — the fear functions as the logical bridge between observed miraculous act and the christological question. The argument: supernatural act → inner awe → identity question. The fear is the epistemological hinge. |
| M01-G | finding | 2Ti 1:7 (anchor M01-G-VCG-01) logical structure: Premise: God gave us a spirit of power, love, and self-control. Implicit premise: Timidity is not consistent with this spirit. Conclusion: Timidity is not from God; what God gives is courage, love, and discipline. The argument is a definitional contrast: divine gift (positive triple) excludes its opposite (deilia). |

### T7.2.4  ·  Tier T7

> What contextual setting carries the primary verse evidence (judicial, liturgical, covenantal, communal, eschatological) — and what does that setting reveal?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The cluster's contextual settings span the entire range of Scripture's life-settings. M01-A governs all settings (judicial, liturgical, covenantal, communal, eschatological). The eschatological setting is particularly significant: multiple sub-groups have their climactic statements in eschatological contexts (M01-A: Rev corpus; M01-G: Rev 21:8; M01-F: Heb 10:27; M01-B: Luk 21:26), confirming that fear is a characteristic whose fullest significance is eschatological. |
| M01-A | finding | M01-A's evidence is carried across multiple contextual settings: (1) **covenantal** — Mal 2:5 (fear as the covenant's defining substance with Levi); Deu 6:2 (fear governing the covenant life); (2) **judicial** — Lev 19:14; 25:17; 2Ch 19:7-9 (fear as the inner judge in judicial settings); (3) **liturgical** — Psa 5:7; Heb 12:28 (fear as the posture of worship); (4) **communal** — Mal 3:16; Psa 119:63; Act 9:31 (fear as community-forming and sustaining); (5) **eschatological** — Rev 11:18; 14:7; 19:5 (fear as the defining posture of the redeemed at the consummation). The spread across all five settings reveals that M01-A is not restricted to one domain of life but governs the whole person's life in every setting. |
| M01-B | finding | M01-B's evidence is carried across: **narrative encounter settings** (OT military crisis, NT miracle events, resurrection appearances), **pastoral settings** (Paul's "do not fear" commands, Jesus's commands throughout the gospels), and **eschatological settings** (Luk 21:26 — cosmic fear at the end). The narrative encounter setting is dominant. |
| M01-G | finding | M01-G's evidence is carried across: **epistolary pastoral** (2Ti 1:7 — letter to a pastor in threatened community), **parabolic wisdom** (Mat 25:25 — the talent parable), and **eschatological judgment** (Rev 21:8). The eschatological setting reveals the ultimate stakes of the characteristic — timidity is not a minor personality trait but a disposition whose ultimate consequence is judgment. |

### T7.2.5  ·  Tier T7

> Does any verse function as the primary anchor for this characteristic — the verse that most fully and directly expresses its essential character?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The cluster's primary anchor is **Pro 1:7** for the whole cluster, with Lev 19:14 as primary for the ethical register, Mar 4:41 for the christological register, Isa 66:2 for the spirit-level somatic register, and 2Ti 1:7 for the evaluative-constitutional register. No single verse encompasses the cluster's full seven-sub-group scope, but Pro 1:7 has the broadest reach as the verse that establishes the foundational relationship between fear-of-God and all genuine knowing. |
| M01-A | finding | For M01-A, the two candidate primary anchors are: (1) **Lev 19:14** (anchor M01-A-VCG-01): the most direct statement of fear-of-God as interior moral constraint where no human court sees — the ethical dimension. (2) **Pro 1:7** (anchor M01-A-VCG-02): the most direct statement of fear-of-God as the epistemological root of wisdom and knowledge — the cognitive-wisdom dimension. Between them, Pro 1:7 functions as the more definitionally primary anchor for the characteristic's essential nature (it IS the beginning of knowledge), while Lev 19:14 functions as the most direct ethical instantiation. |
| M01-B | finding | For M01-B: **Mar 4:41** (anchor M01-B-VCG-02: "great fear filled the disciples as they witnessed Jesus commanding wind and sea into calm — the fear immediately issues in questioning his identity") is the anchor that most fully captures M01-B's essential character: the awe-producing quality of the divine encounter that moves immediately toward christological recognition. |
| M01-D | finding | For M01-D: **Dan 5:6** (anchor M01-D-VCG-03: "dismay striking Belshazzar's inner person so violently that it changes his color and causes his limbs to give way and his knees to knock") — dismay most fully visible in its bodily consequences, showing the inner-to-outer cascade. |
| M01-E | finding | For M01-E: **Isa 66:2** (anchor M01-E-VCG-02: "trembling at God's word is paired with humility and a contrite spirit as the inner posture God looks for — the trembling is located in the spirit") — the most theologically significant trembling verse, locating it in the spirit as the posture God values. |
| M01-G | finding | For M01-G: **2Ti 1:7** (anchor M01-G-VCG-01: "timidity is contrasted with the spirit God gives — power, love, and self-control; identified as a spirit-level disposition that God has not implanted") — the most direct statement of the characteristic as a spirit-level failure. |

### T7.2.6  ·  Tier T7

> What does the primary anchor verse reveal that no other verse reveals?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| M01-A | finding | [E] Pro 1:7 reveals uniquely that reverential fear of God is not merely a virtue alongside wisdom but is **constitutively prior to wisdom as its beginning**. No other verse makes this definitional claim as directly: it is not that wisdom leads to fear or that wisdom and fear coexist — it is that fear IS wisdom's beginning. The verse establishes a hierarchical relationship (fear → wisdom, not wisdom → fear) that no other single verse in M01 establishes as explicitly. --- [E] Lev 19:14 reveals uniquely that reverential fear of God is the **operative inner moral standard in situations of power asymmetry where no human accountability exists**. The specific pairing with the deaf and blind (who cannot see or report exploitation) shows that fear of God fills the accountability gap left by the ab… |
| M01-B | finding | Mar 4:41 reveals uniquely that acute fear before Jesus's supernatural power is not the endpoint but the **epistemological entry-point for christological recognition**. The disciples' fear immediately produces "who then is this?" — no other verse so precisely captures the cognitive-question-generating function of encounter-fear in the NT's christological argument. |
| M01-E | finding | Isa 66:2 reveals uniquely that **God himself describes and evaluates a specific human inner posture of trembling — located in the spirit — as the posture he looks for**. No other verse establishes that God actively attends to and values this specific spirit-level somatic response to his word. |
| M01-G | finding | 2Ti 1:7 reveals uniquely that timidity is **explicitly not from God** — it is a spirit-level disposition God has not implanted. No other verse makes this negative divine-origin claim for the characteristic. The verse establishes both the spirit-level location and the non-divine origin of timidity in a single assertion. |

### T7.3.1  ·  Tier T7

> Which human science framework (psychology, moral philosophy, developmental psychology, sociology, anthropology, or other) is most useful as an interpretive lens for this characteristic?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The most useful primary framework for the cluster as a whole is **affective neuroscience** (for the acute fear, somatic trembling, and freeze-collapse dimensions — M01-B, E, D), with **clinical psychology / anxiety research** as the major secondary framework for the anticipatory dimension (M01-F). **Psychology of religion / awe research** is the most relevant framework for M01-A but is limited by its inability to adjudicate normativity. |
| M01-A | finding | For M01-A (reverential fear of God as governing orientation): the most useful science framework is **psychology of religion / positive psychology of awe** (science extract Section 4: Keltner and Haidt's awe research; Otto's numinous experience operationalised in Hood's Mysticism Scale). This framework identifies awe's core features — perceived vastness and need for accommodation — and its downstream effects: self-diminishment, slowed time perception, prosocial orientation, openness to new information. These downstream effects partially overlap with what M01-A describes: the God-fearer is characterised by humility (not self-exalting), ethical other-orientation (Pro 14:2; Lev 19:14), and teachability (Pro 15:33). The framework illuminates the experiential phenomenology of M01-A; it cannot a… |
| M01-B | finding | For M01-B (acute fear and alarm): **neuroscience — affective neuroscience** (science extract Section 1: LeDoux amygdala model, Panksepp FEAR system, Barlow fear/anxiety distinction). The amygdala-centred model of fear processing establishes fear as potentially bypassing cortical processing — a subcortical rapid-response system. This is directly relevant to M01-B's "without deliberation" pattern (1Sa 17:24: all men of Israel flee immediately). Öhman's preparedness theory (some stimuli more readily activate fear circuitry) is relevant to M01-B-VCG-01's theophanic fear — the repeated biblical pattern suggests that divine presence is a maximally preparedness-activating stimulus. |
| M01-C | finding | For M01-C (terror-as-force) and the military-threat dimension of M01-B: **behavioural science / social psychology — stress and coercion research** (science extract Section 5: Lazarus and Folkman's stress/appraisal/coping model; Seligman's learned helplessness). The stress-appraisal model identifies perceived uncontrollability and unpredictability as primary determinants of whether a stressor produces overwhelming fear. M01-C's terror-as-force is characterised precisely by its uncontrollability (God's terror cannot be resisted, Gen 35:5) and its unpredictability (Exo 23:27: God's terror sent as an advance weapon, unexpected by enemies). Seligman's learned helplessness (Seligman's model of uncontrollable negative stimuli producing passivity) maps onto M01-C's paralysis effect. |
| M01-D | finding | For M01-D (dismay and inner collapse): **affective neuroscience and psychophysiology** (science extract Sections 1 and 2) in its freeze-response dimension. Porges's polyvagal theory (science extract Section 2: the freeze response distinct from fight-or-flight) is the most applicable framework for M01-D's characteristic inner collapse, colour change, limb-failure, and speechlessness. These map onto the dorsal vagal shutdown response (parasympathetic freeze/collapse) rather than the sympathetic arousal of M01-B. Porges's framework makes M01-D anatomically intelligible as a distinct physiological state. |
| M01-E | finding | For M01-E (trembling / fear made somatic): **psychophysiology** (science extract Section 2: Cannon's sympathetic nervous system description; James-Lange theory; Damasio's somatic marker theory). The somatic vocabulary of M01-E maps directly onto the psychophysiology of the fight-flight-freeze response. Damasio's somatic marker theory (bodily states as constitutive of emotional experience, not merely expressive) is directly applicable to M01-E's somatic primacy — the body's trembling is not just a symptom of inner fear but is constitutive of the fear-experience itself, consistent with what Damasio proposes. |
| M01-F | finding | For M01-F (anticipatory dread and anxiety): **clinical psychology — anxiety research** (science extract Section 3: Beck's cognitive model; Borkovec's worry research; Barlow's unified anxiety model). Borkovec's characterisation of worry as "verbal-linguistic, repetitive, and future-oriented" is the closest scientific analogue to M01-F's de.a.gah (H1674 — the cognitive-ruminating anticipatory anxiety). Beck's appraisal-model (threat appraisal + perceived inability to cope) maps onto M01-F-VCG-01's pervasive daily anxiety and VCG-02's dread that materialises. |
| M01-G | finding | For M01-G (timidity and cowardly shrinking): **moral philosophy** (the deilia / andreia framework in Aristotle's virtue ethics — though not in the science extract) is the nearest framework. The science extract does not specifically address cowardice as a psychological category; the nearest is the clinical anxiety research (M01-F framework) applied to situations of moral decision-making under threat. The programme notes that M01-G's evaluative-moral dimension exceeds what clinical psychology addresses. |

### T7.3.2  ·  Tier T7

> Where the human science framework illuminates the verse evidence — making a finding more coherent or complete — what does it reveal?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | Science illuminates the cluster primarily in three areas: (1) the somatic vocabulary of M01-E (somatic marker theory making it constitutive rather than merely expressive); (2) the subcortical-bypass mechanism of M01-B's extreme register (LeDoux's model explaining why deliberation fails under acute fear); (3) the cognitive-ruminating structure of M01-F's anxiety (Borkovec's worry model mapping onto de.a.gah). Science makes the cluster's inner-being description more anatomically and psychologically precise without replacing the theological interpretation. |
| M01-B | finding | **LeDoux's subcortical fear-processing model** illuminates M01-B-VCG-03's "without deliberation" pattern (1Sa 17:24: all men of Israel flee without deliberation): the subcortical pathway bypassing conscious appraisal is exactly what this verse describes. The science explains mechanistically why M01-B fear overrides the deliberative will in ways that M01-A reverential fear does not — M01-A operates through the prefrontal-cortical pathway (deliberate, appraised, formative); M01-B's acute register operates through the subcortical-amygdala pathway (fast, bypass, reflexive). |
| M01-D | finding | **Porges's polyvagal theory / freeze response** illuminates M01-D's bodily collapse pattern (Dan 5:6: color change, limb-failure, knees knocking; Job 32:15: complete speechlessness). The dorsal vagal shutdown response — characterised by immobility, colour changes (due to blood flow redistribution), muscle weakness, and loss of coordinated motor function — is the physiological mechanism that makes M01-D's somatic pattern coherent. The freeze response distinguishes M01-D's immobility-collapse from M01-B's arousal-flight. |
| M01-E | finding | **Somatic marker theory (Damasio)** illuminates M01-E significantly: the cluster's unusually dense somatic vocabulary — bones, flesh, hair, lips, heart, knees, hands registering fear involuntarily — is not merely expressive description but points to the bodily states as constitutive of the fear-experience itself. Damasio's position (somatic states are not merely the expression of emotions but are integral to emotional experience) makes M01-E analytically significant rather than merely illustrative. The density of somatic vocabulary in M01-E (the science extract notes it "exceeds what is typical in ancient Near Eastern emotional vocabulary compilations") is illuminated by somatic marker theory as reflecting a recognition of the body's constitutive role in fear-experience. |
| M01-F | finding | **Borkovec's worry model** illuminates M01-F-VCG-01 and VCG-05: the characterisation of worry as verbal-linguistic, future-oriented, and repetitive maps onto the de.a.gah (H1674) anxiety terms and onto Paul's anticipatory dread (2Cor 12:20: "rooted in thought about what he may find — engaging the mind with anxious expectation"). The science makes the cognitive dimension of M01-F's anxiety more precise: it is not merely affective but involves the mind in repeated forward-projection — exactly what Borkovec describes. |

### T7.3.3  ·  Tier T7

> Where the verse evidence and the human science framework diverge, what does the divergence reveal?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The primary divergences are: (1) normativity — science cannot adjudicate the fittingness of fear of God; (2) commanded virtue — science has no category for a commanded affective disposition that is simultaneously a virtue; (3) covenantal structure — anxiety as divine judgment is outside science's framework; (4) moral-eschatological equivalence — cowardice as morally equivalent to murder is a theological category science cannot evaluate. The divergence is most pronounced at M01-A's theology-of-fear-as-virtue and M01-G's eschatological judgment of cowardice. |
| M01-A | finding | [E] The most significant divergence is M01-A's **normativity claim**: science (psychology of religion) describes the phenomenology of awe and fear before the numinous (self-diminishment, openness, prosocial orientation), but science cannot and does not adjudicate whether such fear is right, fitting, or obligatory. Scripture treats fear-of-God as **categorically right** — not adaptive or maladaptive (science's functional assessment), but obligatory and virtuous. The science extract states this explicitly: "The theological distinctive of this cluster is not that fear falls outside science, but that the object and normativity of certain fears (fear of God as right response to covenant relationship) are theological categories that science does not adjudicate." This is a fundamental divergence… |
| M01-F | finding | In M01-F, the divergence concerns the **covenantal structure of anxiety**: Deu 28:66-67 (chronic anxiety as a covenant curse) has no psychological equivalent. Clinical psychology addresses anxiety as a functional disorder arising from appraisal failures or neurobiological dysregulation. The covenant-curse form of anxiety (imposed by God as a consequence of covenant violation) is a theological category — purposively sent, not merely occurring. Science cannot address whether God sends anxiety as judgment; it can only describe the phenomenology of chronic dread. |
| M01-G | finding | In M01-G, the divergence concerns the **moral equivalence of cowardice with idolatry and murder** (Rev 21:8). Clinical psychology treats anxiety and avoidance (which underlie cowardice) as disorders requiring treatment. Scripture treats sustained cowardice-under-pressure as a morally equivalent failure to idolatry — a categorical judgment that exceeds science's evaluative framework entirely. |

### T7.3.4  ·  Tier T7

> Does the human science framework surface any aspect of this characteristic that the verse evidence has not yet addressed — and does that absence require further verse investigation?

| Sub-group | Status | Finding |
|---|---|---|
| — | cluster_synthesis | The science framework surfaces three modest gaps: (1) the dissociative dimension of M01-D's freeze-collapse (Porges); (2) the verbal-self-talk dimension of M01-F's anxiety (Borkovec); (3) the body-to-soul feedback direction in M01-E (Damasio). None requires immediate further verse investigation in M01 but all are noted for Session C report acknowledgment and potential future research. |
| M01-D | finding | **Porges's freeze response** framework surfaces a potential gap: the polyvagal theory suggests that freeze/shutdown (dorsal vagal) responses may have a dissociative dimension — a kind of psychological absence during the shutdown. M01-D's dismay-evidence (Dan 7:28: Daniel keeps the matter inward after his colour changes; Dan 5:10: the queen urging the king to master the inner dismay) partially addresses this, but the programme notes that the dissociative dimension of extreme dismay has not been explicitly examined in the verse evidence. This is a modest research note for Phase 12 rather than a gap requiring immediate further verse investigation, given that the existing evidence is adequate for the cluster's findings. |
| M01-E | finding | **Damasio's somatic marker theory** surfaces an implicit question about the direction of the body-soul relationship in M01-E: if somatic states are constitutive of emotional experience (not merely expressive), then the body's trembling might itself intensify or sustain the fear, not merely express it. The verse evidence (M01-E) describes the direction as inner → body, but does not address whether the body → inner feedback operates. This is a T7.3.4 gap — the science framework suggests the feedback direction is relevant, but the verse evidence is silent on it. Researcher note for Phase 12. |
| M01-F | finding | **Borkovec's worry model** surfaces a gap: the verbal-linguistic dimension of worry (Borkovec: worry is specifically verbal, repetitive self-talk) is not explicitly evidenced in M01-F's vocabulary. The de.a.gah terms carry a cognitive-ruminating quality but the verse evidence does not describe the specific verbal-internal character of the anxiety. This is a potential gap — whether the anxiety terms in M01-F include a verbal/self-talk dimension is worth noting for researcher attention at Phase 12. It does not require new verse investigation in M01 but may surface in the Session C report as an acknowledged gap between the science framework and the verse evidence's specificity. |

## 2. Anchor verses

### Sub-group — — 

**Group 1153-001** — H0928 *be.ha.lah* (Hebrew, “dismay”)

- _Group context_: Sudden panic and terror as inner affliction — the state of dismay, panic, and anguish that falls upon persons, including the heart-aching dimension of divine visitation
- _Anchor verse_ — **Lev 26:16**: Lev 26:16 then I will do this to you: I will visit you with panic , with wasting disease and fever that consume the eyes and make the heart ache . And you shall sow your seed in vain , for your enemies shall eat it.

**Group 105-001** — H1670 *de.a.vah* (Hebrew, “dismay”)

- _Group context_: Term names terror or dismay — the inner condition of overwhelming dread in the face of what cannot be resisted or comprehended
- _Anchor verse_ — **Job 41:22**: Job 41:22 In his neck abides strength , and terror dances before him.

### Sub-group M01-A — Reverential Fear / Fear of God as Governing Orientation

**Group M01-A-VCG-06** — G6015 *deos* (Greek, “fear”)

- _Group context_: Fear of God as the sustained inner orientation that defines a person's identity, governs their whole way of life, and marks the community of the faithful — transmitted across generations, constitutive of covenant relationship, defining the person who is acceptable to God. This is the enduring, generational, communal dimension of fear-of-God.
- _Group notes_: Created by DIR-20260516-003 (wa-cluster-M01-dir-003-vcg-create-v1-20260516) in sub-group M01-A
- _Anchor verse_ — **Heb 12:28**: Heb 12:28 Therefore let us be grateful for receiving a kingdom that cannot be shaken , and thus let us offer to God acceptable worship, with reverence and awe ,
- _Anchor note_: | DIR-20260516-003 (wa-cluster-M01-dir-003-vcg-create-v1-20260516) provisional anchor (R4 fallback): term G6015 deos had no AI-designated anchor; first canonical-order is_relevant verse promoted.

**Group M01-A-VCG-01** — H3372H *ya.re* (Hebrew, “to fear: revere”)

- _Group context_: Fear of God functions as the operative interior force that constrains wrongdoing, motivates ethical treatment of the vulnerable, and produces just conduct where no external court can see. These verses show the fear as an internal judge substituting for external accountability — the sole operative restraint against exploiting the poor, the servant, the neighbour in business, the dependent. God-directed reverence is presented as the only adequate check on the impulse to abuse power.
- _Group notes_: Created by DIR-20260516-003 (wa-cluster-M01-dir-003-vcg-create-v1-20260516) in sub-group M01-A
- _Anchor verse_ — **Lev 19:14**: Lev 19:14 You shall not curse the deaf or put a stumbling block before the blind , but you shall fear your God : I am the Lord .

**Group M01-A-VCG-04** — H3372H *ya.re* (Hebrew, “to fear: revere”)

- _Group context_: Fear is the inner response evoked by witnessing or contemplating God's mighty deeds, incomparable greatness, holiness, or terrifying power displayed in history or nature. Not primarily a chronic orientation but the inner event of awe-overwhelm at divine display — reverential dread triggered by what God has done and what he is. These meanings characterise God himself as the source and object of the awe.
- _Group notes_: Created by DIR-20260516-003 (wa-cluster-M01-dir-003-vcg-create-v1-20260516) in sub-group M01-A
- _Anchor verse_ — **Exo 15:11**: Exo 15:11 “ Who is like you , O Lord , among the gods ? Who is like you , majestic in holiness , awesome in glorious deeds , doing wonders ?

**Group M01-A-VCG-05** — H3372H *ya.re* (Hebrew, “to fear: revere”)

- _Group context_: These meanings address the direction of fear — the command to fear God and not other objects (enemies, idols, the crowd), the exposure of misplaced fear as the root of covenant failure, and the positive freedom from human fear that trust in God produces. The characteristic phenomenon is the redirection of the inner disposition of fear toward its proper object.
- _Group notes_: Created by DIR-20260516-003 (wa-cluster-M01-dir-003-vcg-create-v1-20260516) in sub-group M01-A
- _Anchor verse_ — **Jer 5:22**: Jer 5:22 Do you not fear me? declares the Lord . Do you not tremble before me ? I placed the sand as the boundary for the sea , a perpetual barrier that it cannot pass ; though the waves toss , they cannot prevail ; though they roar , they cannot pass over it .

**Group M01-A-VCG-06** — H3372H *ya.re* (Hebrew, “to fear: revere”)

- _Group context_: Fear of God as the sustained inner orientation that defines a person's identity, governs their whole way of life, and marks the community of the faithful — transmitted across generations, constitutive of covenant relationship, defining the person who is acceptable to God. This is the enduring, generational, communal dimension of fear-of-God.

- _Anchor note_: dual-context verse

**Group M01-A-VCG-03** — H3373 *ya.re* (Hebrew, “afraid”)

- _Group context_: Fear of God is presented as the relational posture that aligns a person with God's saving purposes and opens them to his provision, protection, steadfast love, and covenant faithfulness. The God-fearers form a community with a distinctive inner identity — defined by this reverence, which functions as the relational ground of divine attention and care across both Testaments.

**Group M01-A-VCG-02** — H3374 *yir.ah* (Hebrew, “fear”)

- _Group context_: Fear of God is identified as the foundational inner orientation from which wisdom, knowledge, and genuine understanding begin. Without it the mind is disoriented; with it, the whole cognitive and moral life is rightly ordered. These meanings characterise reverential fear not primarily as restraint on wrongdoing but as the epistemological starting point of genuine insight — wisdom's root, medium, and beginning.
- _Group notes_: Created by DIR-20260516-003 (wa-cluster-M01-dir-003-vcg-create-v1-20260516) in sub-group M01-A
- _Anchor verse_ — **Pro 1:7**: Pro 1:7 The fear of the Lord is the beginning of knowledge ; fools despise wisdom and instruction .

**Group M01-A-VCG-07** — H4172A *mo.rah* (Hebrew, “fear”)

The outward-facing dimension of M01-A: how Israel's God produces reverential fear among the nations through the deeds of the Exodus, the conquest, and later history, with the expectation that all nations will ultimately fear him.

### Sub-group M01-B — Acute Fear and Alarm

**Group M01-B-VCG-02** — G1568 *ekthambeo* (Greek, “be awe-struck”)

- _Group context_: The awe-struck fear produced specifically by witnessing Jesus exercise supernatural power — calming storms, healing, raising the dead, walking on water, casting out demons. These meanings form a distinct NT phenomenon: fear as the immediate communal inner response that precedes and accompanies the dawning recognition of who Jesus is. The fear is not paralysing but question-raising.
- _Group notes_: Created by DIR-20260516-003 (wa-cluster-M01-dir-003-vcg-create-v1-20260516) in sub-group M01-B
- _Anchor verse_ — **Mar 9:15**: Mar 9:15 And immediately all the crowd , when they saw him , were greatly amazed and ran up to him and greeted him .
- _Anchor note_: | DIR-20260516-003 (wa-cluster-M01-dir-003-vcg-create-v1-20260516) provisional anchor (R4 fallback): term G1568 ekthambeo had no AI-designated anchor; first canonical-order is_relevant verse promoted.

**Group M01-B-VCG-02** — G1569 *ekthambos* (Greek, “astonished”)

- _Group context_: The awe-struck fear produced specifically by witnessing Jesus exercise supernatural power — calming storms, healing, raising the dead, walking on water, casting out demons. These meanings form a distinct NT phenomenon: fear as the immediate communal inner response that precedes and accompanies the dawning recognition of who Jesus is. The fear is not paralysing but question-raising.

### Sub-group M01-C — Terror as Overwhelming Force

**Group M01-C-VCG-05** — H0366 *a.yom* (Hebrew, “terrible”)

- _Group context_: Terror as a quality radiating from powerful beings or nations outward — producing dread in those who encounter them. The terror here is a projective force characterising a person or entity as intrinsically awe-inspiring and fear-inducing.
- _Group notes_: Created by DIR-20260516-003 (wa-cluster-M01-dir-003-vcg-create-v1-20260516) in sub-group M01-C
- _Anchor verse_ — **Hab 1:7**: Hab 1:7 They are dreaded and fearsome ; their justice and dignity go forth from themselves.

**Group M01-C-VCG-01** — H0367 *e.mah* (Hebrew, “terror”)

- _Group context_: God deploys dread and terror ahead of Israel as an active weapon that paralyses enemy resistance before battle — an externally imposed inner state in the enemies that melts their will and renders them motionless. The terror is explicitly divine in origin and instrumentally purposive: God's dread, not Israel's military strength, defeats the enemy.
- _Group notes_: Created by DIR-20260516-003 (wa-cluster-M01-dir-003-vcg-create-v1-20260516) in sub-group M01-C
- _Anchor verse_ — **Exo 23:27**: Exo 23:27 I will send my terror before you and will throw into confusion all the people against whom you shall come , and I will make all your enemies turn their backs to you.

**Group M01-C-VCG-04** — H0367 *e.mah* (Hebrew, “terror”)

- _Group context_: Terror as the quality of divine majesty itself — not deployed as a weapon at Israel's enemies but as the inherent character of God's presence, judgment, and risen power that drives people to hide, flee, or be overwhelmed. These meanings describe what the divine majesty itself does to inner composure when it rises in judgment.
- _Group notes_: Created by DIR-20260516-003 (wa-cluster-M01-dir-003-vcg-create-v1-20260516) in sub-group M01-C
- _Anchor verse_ — **Psa 55:4**: Psa 55:4 My heart is in anguish within me; the terrors of death have fallen upon me .

**Group M01-C-VCG-02** — H1091 *bal.la.hah* (Hebrew, “terror”)

- _Group context_: Terror characterised as an active, hunting, encircling force that overwhelms the inner person with no escape — pursuing relentlessly like a predator, overtaking like a flood, surrounding on every side. These meanings emphasise the agency and relentlessness of the terror itself.
- _Group notes_: Created by DIR-20260516-003 (wa-cluster-M01-dir-003-vcg-create-v1-20260516) in sub-group M01-C
- _Anchor verse_ — **Job 18:11**: Job 18:11 Terrors frighten him on every side , and chase him at his heels .

- _Anchor verse_ — **Jer 49:16**: Jer 49:16 The horror you inspire has deceived you, and the pride of your heart , you who live in the clefts of the rock , who hold the height of the hill . Though you make your nest as high as the eagle’s , I will bring you down from there , declares the Lord .

### Sub-group M01-D — Dismay and Inner Collapse

**Group M01-D-VCG-01** — H0926 *ba.hal* (Hebrew, “to dismay”)

- _Group context_: Dismay arising from receiving terrible news, witnessing catastrophe, or experiencing the withdrawal of God's presence — the inner collapse of confidence and composure that follows a sudden shattering of the assumed order. The person is overwhelmed, speechless, or undone.
- _Group notes_: Created by DIR-20260516-003 (wa-cluster-M01-dir-003-vcg-create-v1-20260516) in sub-group M01-D
- _Anchor verse_ — **Psa 6:3**: Psa 6:3 My soul also is greatly troubled . But you , O Lord — how long ?

**Group M01-D-VCG-05** — H0926 *ba.hal* (Hebrew, “to dismay”)

- _Group context_: Inner agitation in the sense of rashness, impulsive urgency, or panic-driven flight — the ba.hal meanings that name hasty inner drive rather than the shattering of composure. Includes Ecclesiastes corpus of rashness before God and kings, and the panic that dissolves military resolve.
- _Group notes_: Created by DIR-20260516-003 (wa-cluster-M01-dir-003-vcg-create-v1-20260516) in sub-group M01-D
- _Anchor verse_ — **Pro 28:22**: Pro 28:22 A stingy man hastens after wealth and does not know that poverty will come upon him .

**Group M01-D-VCG-03** — H0927 *be.hal* (Hebrew, “to dismay”)

- _Group context_: Dismay characterised by its visible bodily effects — color change, limbs giving way, knees knocking, speechlessness, hands paralysed. These meanings emphasise the radical interiority-to-exteriority dynamic: the inner collapse is so complete it writes itself on the body.
- _Group notes_: Created by DIR-20260516-003 (wa-cluster-M01-dir-003-vcg-create-v1-20260516) in sub-group M01-D

### Sub-group M01-E — Trembling / Fear Made Somatic

**Group M01-E-VCG-01** — G1790 *entromos* (Greek, “trembling”)

- _Group context_: The involuntary whole-body trembling produced by direct encounter with the divine presence — at Sinai, in theophanies, and in visionary encounters. The trembling here is the bodily response to holiness overwhelming the person — involuntary, whole-body, paired with paralysis of the will.

This is trembling not as terror but as the appropriate somatic gravity of serious engagement with divine things.

### Sub-group M01-F — Anticipatory Dread and Anxiety

**Group M01-F-VCG-04** — G5398 *foberos* (Greek, “fearful”)

- _Group context_: The specific form of anticipatory dread directed at divine judgment — the inner experience of fearing God as judge, either in the sense of his wrath coming or of being unable to survive his presence. Includes the NT fearful expectation of condemnation.
- _Group notes_: Created by DIR-20260516-003 (wa-cluster-M01-dir-003-vcg-create-v1-20260516) in sub-group M01-F
- _Anchor verse_ — **Heb 10:27**: Heb 10:27 but a fearful expectation of judgment , and a fury of fire that will consume the adversaries .

**Group M01-F-VCG-05** — G5399 *fobeō* (Greek, “to fear”)

- _Group context_: A specific form of anticipatory dread characterised by Paul's protective apprehension about the spiritual welfare of his churches — anxious forward-looking concern about outcomes, motivated by love rather than threat.
- _Group notes_: Created by DIR-20260516-003 (wa-cluster-M01-dir-003-vcg-create-v1-20260516) in sub-group M01-F
- _Anchor verse_ — **2Cor 12:20**: 2Cor 12:20 For I fear that perhaps when I come I may find you not as I wish , and that you may find me not as you wish — that perhaps there may be quarreling , jealousy , anger , hostility , slander , gossip , conceit , and disorder .

**Group M01-F-VCG-01** — H1674 *de.a.gah* (Hebrew, “anxiety”)

- _Group context_: Anxiety as a sustained, all-pervasive inner burden that saturates every moment and every ordinary activity — not triggered by a specific anticipated event but settling as a constant companion to daily existence under threat or judgment.
- _Group notes_: Created by DIR-20260516-003 (wa-cluster-M01-dir-003-vcg-create-v1-20260516) in sub-group M01-F
- _Anchor verse_ — **Eze 12:18**: Eze 12:18 “ Son of man , eat your bread with quaking , and drink water with trembling and with anxiety .

**Group M01-F-VCG-02** — H3025 *ya.gor* (Hebrew, “to fear”)

- _Group context_: Dread as a forward-looking inner state that precedes and then corresponds to the actual suffering feared — fear as inner anticipatory anguish that proves accurate. The feared event arrives and confirms the dread.
- _Group notes_: Created by DIR-20260516-003 (wa-cluster-M01-dir-003-vcg-create-v1-20260516) in sub-group M01-F
- _Anchor verse_ — **Job 3:25**: Job 3:25 For the thing that I fear comes upon me, and what I dread befalls me .

**Group M01-F-VCG-02** — H4034 *me.go.rah* (Hebrew, “fear”)

- _Group context_: Dread as a forward-looking inner state that precedes and then corresponds to the actual suffering feared — fear as inner anticipatory anguish that proves accurate. The feared event arrives and confirms the dread.

### Sub-group M01-G — Timidity and Cowardly Shrinking

**Group M01-G-VCG-01** — G1167 *deilia* (Greek, “timidity”)

- _Group context_: Cowardly, faithless inner shrinking that is morally condemned or contrasted with the peace, faith, and courage that should govern the inner person. These meanings evaluate fear as a deficiency of inner constitution — the disposition that God has not implanted, that faith displaces, and that identifies moral failure.
- _Group notes_: Created by DIR-20260516-003 (wa-cluster-M01-dir-003-vcg-create-v1-20260516) in sub-group M01-G
